State v. Sagen


Appeal No. 2010AP2119-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2011 WI App 27; 331 Wis. 2d 731; 795 N.W.2d 493; 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 44



January 20, 2011, Decided 
January 20, 2011, Filed


NOTICE: SEE RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, RULE 809.23(3), REGARDING CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. NOTE: THIS OPINION WILL NOT APPEAR IN A PRINTED VOLUME. THE DISPOSITION WILL APPEAR IN A REPORTER TABLE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Rock County: RICHARD T. WERNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2009CT957.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Rock County, Wisconsin, denied his motion to suppress evidence and convicted him for operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration in excess of 0.08, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b) (2007-08), third offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the traffic stop initiated by a police officer was not supported by the community caretaker exception, and therefore the circuit court erred when it denied his motion to suppress evidence. The appellate court applied a three-part test to determine whether a seizure unsupported by probable cause or reasonable suspicion was justified under the community caretaker exception. A seizure occurred when the officer stopped defendant's vehicle. Under the circumstances, it was objectively reasonable for the officer to stop the vehicle in order to determine whether anyone needed assistance. The officer's "feeling" that there was a disturbance in the vehicle was not unsupported: the officer heard a yell coming from within the vehicle and his experience provided a reasonable basis to believe the yell could be a call for help. Since the officer was the only person in the area when he heard the yell, he believed that someone inside the vehicle was attempting to get his attention. He testified that people tried to get his attention only when they were in need of help. There was a substantial public interest in police assistance in such situations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

602 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shaw


Appeal No. 2010AP693-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2011 WI App 19; 331 Wis. 2d 489; 795 N.W.2d 63; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1043



December 23, 2010, Decided 
December 23, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Lincoln County: JAY R. TLUSTY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Lincoln County, Wisconsin, denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence that police obtained following the stop and arrest, and defendant was convicted under Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2007-08) of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, fifth offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the investigative traffic stop was supported by probable cause that defendant had violated Wis. Stat. § 346.13(1) because an officer observed defendant moving abruptly from the right lane completely onto the shoulder of the road, and then moving back into the right lane, while maintaining a speed of about 40 miles per hour. The court also held that defendant's subsequent arrest was supported by probable cause that he committed the offense of driving while intoxicated. The circumstances included that the officer saw defendant swerve onto the shoulder of the road and then back into his own lane while maintaining his rate of speed; defendant failed to respond to emergency lights and siren; defendant's eyes were bloodshot, he spoke in a slow and deliberate manner, and his voice was raspy; he admitted to having one or two beers earlier in the day and stated he was on pain medication; he performed field sobriety tests indicating numerous clues of intoxication; and his preliminary breath test indicated a blood alcohol content of.015. Thus, there was no constitutional violation requiring suppression of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Marathon County Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. Lorie O. (In re Kody O.)


Appeal No. 2010AP2351


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2011 WI App 19; 331 Wis. 2d 490; 795 N.W.2d 64; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1023



December 21, 2010, Decided 
December 21, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Marathon County: JILL N. FALSTAD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2009TP24.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Marathon County, Wisconsin, that found her to be an unfit parent under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4) based on a continuing denial of visitation and that terminated her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother and daughter were living with a friend before the mother was arrested on a fugitive warrant and returned to California. The friend became the daughter's guardian until the child was removed from her care five years later and was placed in foster care. Because the mother was to remain incarcerated for another seven years and because the child had no contact with her mother since her mother's arrest, the circuit court found the mother to be unfit and terminated her parental rights. On review, the court held that the circuit court's failure to previously set forth the conditions necessary for the mother to be granted visitation as required by Wis. Stat. § 48.356(1) precluded a finding of unfitness under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4) because the requirement that a parent be provided with conditions to satisfy for the return of his or her child was critical to the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4).


OUTCOME: The order terminating the mother's parental rights was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to dismiss the proceedings.

State v. Lorraine J. (In re Tyanna J.)

NOTICE: SEE RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, RULE 809.23(3), REGARDING CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. NOTE: THIS OPINION WILL NOT APPEAR IN A PRINTED VOLUME. THE DISPOSITION WILL APPEAR IN A REPORTER TABLE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Johnny J., 2011 WI 29, 332 Wis. 2d 280, 797 N.W.2d 525, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 256 (2011)
Review denied by State v. Lorraine J., 2011 WI 29, 332 Wis. 2d 280, 797 N.W.2d 525, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 255 (2011)
Review denied by State v. Johnny J., 2011 WI 29, 332 Wis. 2d 280, 797 N.W.2d 525, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 281 (2011)
Review denied by State v. Lorraine J., 2011 WI 29, 332 Wis. 2d 280, 797 N.W.2d 525, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 313 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM S. POCAN and KAREN E. CHRISTENSON, Judges. 1 Cir. Ct. Nos. 2005TP396, 2005TP398, 2005TP396, 2005TP398.


1 The Honorable Dennis R. Cimpl originally presided over the cases making up this appeal and entered the first termination of parental rights ("TPR") orders. However, Judge Cimpl later vacated the TPR orders and recused himself. The Honorable William S. Pocan was then assigned to the cases and presided over the subsequent jury trial on grounds and the dispositional hearing, and entered the July 2009 TPR orders from which the parties appeal. The Honorable Karen E. Christenson entered the orders denying the parties' post-termination motions.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 2



2 By prior order, we consolidated the instant appeals for dispositional but not briefing purposes. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.107(6)(e) (2007-08), this court is required to issue a decision resolving TPR appeals within thirty days after the filing of the reply brief. We may extend that deadline pursuant to Wis. Stat. Rule 809.82(2)(a) (2007-08) for good cause. See Rhonda R.D. v. Franklin R.D., 191 Wis. 2d 680, 694, 530 N.W.2d 34 (Ct. App. 1995). Here, Johnny J. filed  [*2] his reply brief in Case Nos. 2010AP136 and 2010AP137, on October 15, 2010, and Lorraine J. filed her reply brief in Case Nos. 2010AP52 and 2010AP53, on October 20, 2010. On our own motion, we now extend the decisional deadline in these matters through the date of this decision. Our review was made immeasurably more difficult by the confusing numbering of the record at the circuit court level.

All references to the Wisconsin Statutes are to the 2007-08 version unless otherwise noted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered an order terminating their parental rights to their two youngest children under Wis. Stat. § 48.415. The parents also appealed orders that denied their post-termination motions for visitation. Respondent, the State of Wisconsin, opposed the parents' appeal.


OVERVIEW: In September 2004, the Bureau of Milwaukee Child Welfare removed all five children of the parents' children from their home. One of the children was then seven months old and did not have a crib. The home was dirty and in disrepair. The father had unmet drug and alcohol issues, and the mother had untreated mental health issues. In November 2004, the trial court found all five children to be in need of protection and services and entered an order setting forth conditions for their return to the parents' custody. On May 29, 2005, another child was born to the parents while her five siblings were in the custody of the Bureau. The Bureau later removed that child when the father was noncompliant with court-ordered alcohol and drug assessment monitoring and treatment and refused to provide urine samples and the mother had missed many appointments with her therapist. When placed in foster care, the youngest child had diaper rash, thrush, and her milk bottle was crusted with dirt. The court upheld the decision because the occasional supervised visits the parents had with the two youngest children were described by the supervisors as chaotic and unsuccessful.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Stewart


Appeal No. 2009AP2477-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2011 WI App 19; 331 Wis. 2d 487; 795 N.W.2d 62; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 988



December 7, 2010, Decided 
December 7, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Motion denied by, As moot, Certificate of appealability denied Stewart v. Schaub, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29386 (E.D. Wis., Mar. 8, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM SOSNAY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CF393.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to four counts of Medicaid fraud, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 49.49(1)(a)3. (2005-06) in the Circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). The circuit court denied defendant's motions for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the information that was in the complaint and presented at the plea hearing through her trial counsel was inaccurate. The court of appeals disagreed. The facts offered in support of the guilty plea--both those alleged in the complaint and stated by trial counsel at the plea hearing--clearly supported the charges. Trial counsel stated, and defendant agreed, that when she learned that her employees were billing for services that had not been performed, she attempted to solve the problem by covering it up, by offering her employees financial incentive to falsify records. Defendant's valid guilty plea forfeited all nonjurisdictional defects and defenses. When defendant chose to plead guilty, she forfeited her right to challenge discrepancies in the evidence against her. Moreover, at sentencing, defendant personally told the trial court that when she became aware of improperly billed services, she went to the various case managers to ask them to fix their documents.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Martin


Appeal No. 2009AP533


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2011 WI App 1; 330 Wis. 2d 832; 794 N.W.2d 926; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 952



November 23, 2010, Decided 
November 23, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Martin, 2011 WI 86, 335 Wis. 2d 146, 803 N.W.2d 849, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 399 (2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Martin v. Wis., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8762 (U.S., Dec. 5, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1990CF903777A.
State v. Martin, 195 Wis. 2d 84, 537 N.W.2d 147, 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 571 (Wis. Ct. App., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which overruled his postconviction motion Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2007-08) and motion for reconsideration based on his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant had been convicted of first-degree intentional homicide and first-degree recklessly endangering safety while using a dangerous weapon, both as party to a crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the circuit court erroneously gave the jury a coercive instruction and that his attorney was ineffective because he did not object to the instructions given to the jury. The court upheld the decision because defendant's argument took the circuit court's statement out of context, and a consideration of that context defeated defendant's argument. Defendant further argued that his trial counsel was ineffective for not objecting to several instances of prosecutorial misconduct during the State's closing argument. Specifically, defendant contended that the State misrepresented facts and referred to evidence not in the record. The court reviewed the State's closing argument and did not find that the prosecutor's comments rose to the level of prosecutorial misconduct. The court held that the prosecutor's argument and conclusions were fair game and that the State did not improperly vouch for the witness's credibility as alleged by the defendant. The court also held that there was not reasonable probability that a co-defendant's testimony from another trial would have resulted in a different outcome of used for the purpose of impeachment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

Kruse v. Walworth County Dep't of Land Use & Res. Mgmt.


Appeal No. 2010AP229


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2011 WI App 1; 330 Wis. 2d 835; 794 N.W.2d 928; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 882



November 3, 2010, Decided 
November 3, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: MICHAEL S. GIBBS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV1374.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners sued respondents, a land use department and a board (collectively, the county), requesting declaratory judgment. The Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin) declared that the owners had the right to possess and convey their three lots individually and separately, there was no language in Walworth County, Wis., Ordinance § 74-221 that enabled retroactive application, and exhaustion of remedies was not required.


OVERVIEW: The owners purchased three lots, recorded a quitclaim deed, and the lots were then designated as three separate tax parcels. The owners were then told their request to permit three lots under one tax key number was denied. The owners sued and the trial court ruled in the owners' favor. The court affirmed. The county focused on whether the owners were entitled to judicial review. Considering the owners' request for judicial review in light of the factors set forth in case law, the trial court did not err in its finding that the adverse consequences that would result from application of the exhaustion doctrine outweighed its benefits. The question presented for declaratory judgment, whether the county erred in applying the property classification under the ordinance retroactively, was essentially the same as would have been presented on certiorari review under Wis. Stat. § 59.694(10). There was no dispute as to the material underlying facts, the owners had a sound defense to the application of the ordinance, and the application of the exhaustion doctrine to their claim would be harsh. Thus, the trial court properly treated the case as an exception to the exhaustion doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Melendrez (In re Melendrez)


Appeal No. 2009AP2070


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2010 WI App 145; 330 Wis. 2d 97; 791 N.W.2d 405; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 711



September 2, 2010, Decided 
September 2, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: SEE RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, RULE 809.23(3), REGARDING CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. NOTE: THIS OPINION WILL NOT APPEAR IN A PRINTED VOLUME. THE DISPOSITION WILL APPEAR IN A REPORTER TABLE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Melendrez, 2011 WI 1, 793 N.W.2d 70, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 804 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD G. NIESS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CI1.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which found that he was a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (2007-08). He also appealed the circuit court's order denying his motion for post-commitment relief. Defendant had been convicted of third-degree sexual assault under Wis. Stat. § 940.225(3) (2007-08) and of resisting or obstructing an officer under Wis. Stat. § 946.41(1) (2007-08).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was entitled to dismissal of the petition against him because an amendment to Wis. Stat. ch. 980 had a retroactive effect on him that violated his right to due process. The amendment, enacted by 2005 Wis. Act 434, added third-degree sexual assault to the list of sexually violent offenses under Wis. Stat. § 980.01(6)(a) (2007-08), and this occurred after he had pleaded guilty to that offense. The court determined that 2005 Wis. Act 434 did not have a retroactive effect on defendant and therefore did not violate due process in determining that he was a sexually violent person. Defendant further asserted that new research on a test that was used by the State's expert to predict future offenses, contained in an article published after the trial, was newly discovered evidence under Wis. Stat. § 805.15(3) (2007-08) and entitled him to an evidentiary hearing to determine if he is entitled to a new trial. The court disagreed because the information contained in the article was cumulative and even if it were admitted, there was not a reasonable probability there would have been a different result.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Ludwig


Appeal No. 2009AP1724-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2010 WI App 135; 329 Wis. 2d 710; 790 N.W.2d 543; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 702



August 31, 2010, Decided 
August 31, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: SEE RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, RULE 809.23(3), REGARDING CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. NOTE: THIS OPINION WILL NOT APPEAR IN A PRINTED VOLUME. THE DISPOSITION WILL APPEAR IN A REPORTER TABLE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Ludwig, 2011 WI 15, 331 Wis. 2d 46, 794 N.W.2d 900, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 62 (2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ludwig v. Wisconsin, 131 S. Ct. 2940, 180 L. Ed. 2d 226, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 4046 (U.S., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Motion denied by, As moot, Certificate of appealability denied Ludwig v. Schaub, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 94416 (E.D. Wis., July 10, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Brown County: MARC A. HAMMER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF663.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded no contest to two counts of homicide by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle, three counts of first-degree reckless endangerment, and one count of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, third offense in the circuit court for Brown County (Wisconsin). Defendant appealed the circuit court's judgment of conviction and order denying postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, she was denied effective assistance of counsel because her attorney did not conduct an accident reconstruction. The court of appeals disagreed. While trial counsel did not conduct his own accident reconstruction, he did seek information from the State regarding its reconstruction. Even if defendant's trial counsel was deficient in not conducting his own accident reconstruction, defendant could not have shown prejudice. The affirmative defense under Wis. Stat. § 940.09(2)(a) (2007-08) was only available if defendant could have proven by a preponderance of the evidence that the deaths would have occurred even if she had been exercising due care and had not been under the influence of an intoxicant. Defendant could not have met this burden. Had defendant exercised due care, she would have realized that she was driving the wrong way before the head-on collision. Thus, even if her counsel had conducted his own accident reconstruction, it was doubtful that defendant would have been entitled to an instruction on § 940.09(2)(a). Without such an instruction, defendant could not credibly maintain that she would have exercised her right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dunagan


Appeal No. 2009AP1115-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2010 WI App 135; 329 Wis. 2d 710; 790 N.W.2d 542; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 610



August 3, 2010, Decided 
August 3, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: SEE RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, RULE 809.23(3), REGARDING CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. NOTE: THIS OPINION WILL NOT APPEAR IN A PRINTED VOLUME. THE DISPOSITION WILL APPEAR IN A REPORTER TABLE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from judgment of the circuit court for Dunn County: WILLIAM C. STEWART, JR., Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF63.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction for sexually assaulting an individual who suffered from a mental illness or deficiency rendering him incapable of appraising his conduct, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(c). He argued that the Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin) made errors in the admission of other acts evidence, that there was insufficient evidence to support the conviction, and that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court properly exercised its discretion when it admitted evidence concerning defendant's sexual assaults of another mentally incapacitated individual. The evidence went to defendant's motive, intent, plan and modus operandi and was relevant to show defendant's method of inviting young mentally challenged men to his house to perform yard work to pay off a debt and then sexually abusing them. The crimes against the other individual were made more relevant by defendant's suggestion that he was merely performing a "test" on the victim, in effect denying the sexual contact was for his own sexual gratification. The danger of unfair prejudice did not substantially outweigh the probative value of the other acts evidence. There was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction. The victim was mentally deficient and defendant, as the victim's mentor, was well-aware of the victim's inability to consent to the acts. Contrary to defendant's assertion, the statute was not void for vagueness, nor did it impermissibly shift the burden of proof by creating a presumption of the victim's incapacity to consent.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

613 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Cargill Feed Division v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n


Appeal No. 2009AP1877


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI App 115; 329 Wis. 2d 206; 789 N.W.2d 326; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 605


February 5, 2010, Submitted on Briefs 
July 29, 2010, Decided 
July 29, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Jefferson County: JACQUELINE R. ERWIN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2009CV182.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an employer and its insurer, challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), which confirmed the Labor and Industry Review Commission's (Commission) determination that appellee claimant, an injured employee, was permanently and totally disabled under the so-called "odd-lot" doctrine.


OVERVIEW: The Commission applied the wrong legal standard in determining whether the employer had rebutted the employee's prima facie odd-lot case. The Commission expanded the evidentiary burden on employers seeking to rebut a claimant's prima facie odd-lot case beyond that established in prior case law by: (1) requiring the employer to produce evidence it disclosed to prospective employers a claimant's age, disability, and other facts about the claimant; and by (2) establishing a preference for evidence that the employer referred the claimant to prospective employers with specific job openings actually available. Once a claimant established a prima facie odd-lot case, it fell to the employer to prove that the claimant was probably employable and that an actual, suitable job was regularly and continuously available to the claimant. An employer was not required to disclose any descriptive information of a claimant to a prospective employer to satisfy its rebuttal burden. The employer's duty in ascertaining whether an actual job existed was to obtain information from the prospective employer about the job requirements, not provide information about the claimant.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's decision affirming the Commission's decision was reversed. The Commission's decision was set aside and the matter was remanded for the Commission to determine whether the employer rebutted the employee's prima facie case.

Affeldt v. Green Lake County


Appeal No. 2009AP2315


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2010 WI App 120; 329 Wis. 2d 271; 789 N.W.2d 755; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 588



July 28, 2010, Decided 
July 28, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Affeldt v. Green Lake Co., 2010 WI 487, 329 Wis. 2d 372, 791 N.W.2d 380, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 561 (2010)
Reversed by, Cause remanded by Affeldt v. Green Lake County, 2011 WI 56, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 345 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Green Lake County: WILLIAM M. McMONIGAL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008CV92.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action, appellant property owners sought review of an order entered by the Circuit Court for Green Lake County (Wisconsin), which granted summary to respondent county. The owners asserted that the county was not permitted to work on a county highway to expand its width; the owners sought a temporary restraining order (TRO) and a permanent injunction.


OVERVIEW: The county sought to do reconstruction and maintenance on the highway, which abutted the owners' farms to the north and the south, including the full right-of-way width of 66 feet (four rods). The owners would not approve the reconstruction or the removal of fences that within the highway's right-of-way. A TRO was denied, and summary judgment was granted to the county. On appeal, the court affirmed. While the owners argued that they could rebut the presumption that the highway's right-of-way was four rods, that presumption was only triggered if the highway had not been recorded or the records had been lost or destroyed under Wis. Stat. § 82.31(1) and (2) (2007-08). However, the highway at issue was recorded under Wis. Stat. § 82.01(8) (2007-08) based on a resolution of a county board adopted in 1939. Because the highway was recorded, its right-of-way was four rods wide under Wis. Stat. § 82.50(1) (2007-08); nothing triggered the need to resort to the statutory presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

State v. Mulder


Appeal No. 2009AP2306-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2010 WI App 120; 329 Wis. 2d 271; 789 N.W.2d 755; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 571



July 27, 2010, Decided 
July 27, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Mulder, 2011 WI 1, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 808 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: M. JOSEPH DONALD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF2926.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of sexual assault of a child who had not attained the age of 16 years and denied his third petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of sexual assault of a child who had not attained the age of 16 years. He pled no contest to one count. The trial court denied his third postconviction motion for relief. On appeal, the court found that he forfeited his claim that the criminal complaint was not sufficiently definite when he pled no contest. He also forfeited his claim that he was unconstitutionally denied the right to be present at the bail reduction hearing. To the extent he argued that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel at the bail hearing, neither his third postconviction motion nor his appellate brief explained how he was prejudiced by counsel's alleged deficiency. Further, he did not explain why there was reason to doubt his competence. He provided no case citations to support his implied proposition that a competence determination was automatically required when an accused was on medication for anxiety. However, the trial court's plea colloquy was faulty because the trial court did not tell him that it was not bound by the plea agreement. He was entitled to an evidentiary hearing on whether his plea was knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently entered.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the third postconviction order denying defendant's request for an evidentiary hearing. On remand, the trial court was to conduct a hearing consistent with the dictates of Hampton. In all other respects, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Banks


Appeal No. 2009AP1436-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI App 107; 328 Wis. 2d 766; 790 N.W.2d 526; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 561


April 8, 2010, Submitted on Briefs 
July 21, 2010, Decided 
July 21, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Racine County: EMILY S. MUELLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CF606.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) of possession of a firearm by a felon and resisting or obstructing an officer. The court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the State violated his constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV when it suggested that the jury should draw an adverse inference from defendant' refusal to voluntarily submit to the DNA test before the search warrant was presented and that counsel was ineffective for failing to object. The court of appeals agreed. At trial, the State elicited testimony about defendant refusing to voluntarily submit a DNA sample on at least two occasions through different law enforcement witnesses. When the State commented on defendant's refusal during closing, suggesting his refusal demonstrated consciousness of guilt, defendant's attorney should have objected. The State had two eye witnesses, both with credibility issues stemming from past convictions, who presented contradictory testimony regarding defendant's possession of a gun. The State's use of defendant's refusal to submit a DNA sample bolstered the testimony of a witness, who said defendant had a gun. Without the DNA refusal, a witness's observation that defendant did not have a gun might have been just as persuasive as the other witness's observation that defendant did have a gun.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Collins v. City of Kenosha Hous. Auth.


Appeal No. 2009AP1656


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI App 110; 328 Wis. 2d 798; 789 N.W.2d 342; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 563


March 8, 2010, Submitted on Briefs 
July 21, 2010, Decided 
July 21, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Collins v. City of Kenosha Hous. Auth., 2011 WI 15, 331 Wis. 2d 46, 794 N.W.2d 900, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 102 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: BRUCE E. SCHROEDER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV2301.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant participant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, housing authority and commissioners, in the participant's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action seeking reinstatement of her Section 8 voucher and monetary relief. The participant alleged her rights were violated under U.S. Const. amend. XVI, although she never sought relief under Wis. Stat. § 68.13(1).


OVERVIEW: The participant was involved in a federally funded Section 8 housing voucher program. On April 12, 2005, the housing authority sent the participant a letter informing her that her Section 8 voucher would be terminated effective May 31, 2005, because she failed to be home for two inspections. The participant made a timely request for a hearing to appeal the termination. She received notice the determination was upheld. The participant never sought the state provided remedy of certiorari review under Wis. Stat. § 68.13(1). Two years later, the participant filed a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim, seeking reinstatement of her voucher and monetary relief. The trial court granted the housing authority and commissioners' motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed and held the housing authority's regulations did not allow discretion which could foreseeably result in constitutional violations. The court ruled that when a remedy of certiorari review is made available, as it was here, the requirement for procedural due process is satisfied and no actionable claim exists. Thus, the participant did not have an actionable § 1983 claim for relief under the procedural due process clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the housing authority and commissioners.

State v. Gonzalez


Appeal No. 2009AP1249-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2010 WI App 104; 328 Wis. 2d 182; 789 N.W.2d 365; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 509



July 7, 2010, Decided 
July 7, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Gonzalez, 2010 WI 125, 329 Wis. 2d 371, 791 N.W.2d 380, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 513 (2010)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Gonzalez, 2011 WI 63, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 350 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: PATRICIA D. MCMAHON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF2405.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, that convicted him of exposing a child to harmful material in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.11(2)(a) (2005-06) and an order that denied his motion for postconviction relief, arguing that district court erred in precluding him from presenting psychological profile or Richard A.P. evidence and erred in permitting the State to show a pornographic video to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of exposing a child to harmful material after viewing a pornographic video and masturbating while his three-year-old daughter watched. On review of defendant's conviction, the court held that the trial court did not err in precluding defendant from introducing testimony from an expert witness who opined that defendant did not present with traits or qualities of known sex offenders or pedophiles because the harmful exposure charge did not require proof that defendant had any sexual interest in children or that he was likely to assault or molest them for his own pleasure. The expert's testimony that defendant lacked such characteristics was not relevant to the charge because there was no fact at issue that the testimony would have made more or less probable; as such, the evidence was properly excluded under Wis. Stat. § 904.03 for having a tendency to confuse the issues that were relevant to a determination of defendant's guilt. Further the trial court did not err in allowing the jury to view the video because the State was required to prove that the video was harmful to children, and the video was thus admissible to prove an element of the crime charged.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the order denying postconviction relief were affirmed.

 

619 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Wendy M. v. Helen E.K. (In re Guardianship of O. G. M-K)


Appeal Nos. 2009AP720, 2009AP721


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI App 90; 327 Wis. 2d 749; 787 N.W.2d 848; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 481


September 9, 2009, Submitted on Briefs 
June 24, 2010, Decided 
June 24, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Wendy M. v. Helen K., 2011 WI 15, 331 Wis. 2d 46, 794 N.W.2d 899, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 50 (2011)
Review denied by Wendy M. v. Helen K., 2011 WI 15, 331 Wis. 2d 46, 794 N.W.2d 899, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 79 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Dane County: STEVEN D. EBERT, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2008JG87, 2008JG88.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, caregiver and guardian ad litem, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the caregiver's guardianship petitions under Wis. Stat. § 54.15(5), on summary judgment and granted guardianship of the children to respondent adoptive parent. The caregiver alleged she was a parent within the meaning of the guardianship statute and not a third party to the children.


OVERVIEW: A same-sex couple sought to adopt two children. One adopted two children and the other was the caregiver. After the two ended their romantic relationship, the caregiver filed petitions for guardianship under Wis. Stat. § 54.15(5). The trial court dismissed the petitions on summary judgment, concluding that the caregiver failed to make a showing for guardianship filed over the objection of a legal parent by a third party. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal. The caregiver was not a parent within the meaning of § 54.15(5). The court ruled that under Barstad, a person who was not a biological or adoptive parent of a child was a third party who could not become the child's guardian over the biological or adoptive parent's objection absent compelling reasons, such as the unfitness of the biological or adoptive parent. The caregiver failed to meet the compelling reasons standard. The court noted that the parties had adopted a coparenting agreement, in which both spent equal time with the children. There were no triable factual issues concerning whether compelling reasons existed under Barstad to justify granting the caregiver's guardianship petitions over the adoptive parent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the caregiver's guardianship petitions on summary judgment.

Whitefish Bay v. Czirr


Appeal No. 2010AP92


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2010 WI App 100; 327 Wis. 2d 800; 788 N.W.2d 385; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 462



June 22, 2010, Decided 
June 22, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JONATHAN D. WATTS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008TR16300.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was cited for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OWI), first offense, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2007-08), after a traffic stop that took place in the early morning hours. Defendant was found guilty by a municipal court and sought de novo review in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). Although defendant pled guilty upon a stipulated agreement, he sought review.


OVERVIEW: The officer testified that he observed defendant's truck gradually drift towards a median, hit a snowbank, and return to the traffic lane. The trial court viewed the squad car's video recording of the events leading up to the stop. Defendant alleged that his pretrial motion to suppress should have been granted because the traffic stop was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11. The court disagreed. Defendant's momentary travel on the median gave rise to probable cause that an OWI violation occurred. That probable cause justified the stop. Defendant also alleged that his truck did not actually travel on the median, or that doing so for only a second, did not constitute an OWI violation. The officer testified that defendant's truck ended up traveling on the median where there was a snowbank. Having reviewed the video, the court could not say that the trial court's acceptance of the officer's testimony was clearly erroneous. The court could not conclude that the video clearly contradicted defendant's testimony. While he might have only briefly traveled on the median, that act gave the officer probable cause to initiate the stop.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

St. Croix Valley Home Builders Ass'n v. Twp. of Oak Grove


Appeal No. 2009AP2166


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2010 WI App 96; 327 Wis. 2d 510; 787 N.W.2d 454; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 470



June 22, 2010, Decided 
June 22, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by St. Croix Valley Home Builders Ass'n v. Twp. of Oak Grove, 2010 WI 125, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 580 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Pierce County: ROBERT W. WING, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008CV114.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trade association sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin), which dismissed its action against defendant town challenging the validity of an impact fee ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The town enacted Oak Grove, Wis., Ordinance § 19.05 (2003), pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 66.0617(10) (2007-08), which imposed an impact fee on any person seeking to construct or create a land development within the town. None of the association's members appealed the fees under the ordinance's appeal process. However, the association served the town with a notice of claim. The town denied the claim. The association sued the town, seeking a declaration that the ordinance was invalid. The trial court dismissed the action for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. On appeal, the court found that the association not only could have, but should have, used the ordinance's administrative appeal process. The association's claims contested the amount of the fee and the ways in which the fee was spent. Such issues were squarely within the ordinance's appeal process. The association presented claims that the town had the authority to remedy; it could have refunded the fees in whole or part, or revised the ordinance to correct any errors. Because the association's claims could have been resolved administratively, requiring it to use the ordinance's appeal process promoted judicial efficiency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Husar v. City of Brookfield


Appeal Nos. 2009AP326, 2009AP327


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2010 WI App 100; 327 Wis. 2d 797; 788 N.W.2d 383; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 432



June 9, 2010, Decided 
June 9, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: MICHAEL O. BOHREN, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2007CV3479, 2007CV3481.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which awarded a condemnation judgment in favor of respondent, the City of Brookfield. The landowners had set forth the action pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 32.05 (2007-08) by contesting the City's right to condemn the proposed portions of their properties and by claiming that the City's actions constituted a total taking.


OVERVIEW: Cases set forth by two adjacent landowners were consolidated. On appeal, the landowners did not challenge the necessity of the taking. Rather, they argued that the City should have condemned the entirety of their properties on the basis that the City's taking of a permanent limited easement across the property was an illegal and improper taking for private use and that without the easement they were landlocked. Thus, the landowners claimed that the City's actions rendered their properties uneconomic remnants and thereby resulted in a total taking. It was determined that the trial court's grant of judgment for the City was based on an erroneous finding of fact that was premised in large part on the parties' treatment of the easement at issue as private in nature. As the easement was public and because the nature of the easement was central to the issues in dispute, the decision was improper and further proceedings were necessary.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed and remanded.

Henke-Clarson Funeral Serv., LLC v. Jackson


Appeal No. 2009AP363


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2010 WI App 100; 327 Wis. 2d 798; 788 N.W.2d 383; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 421



June 3, 2010, Decided 
June 3, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: JAMES WELKER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV1263.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state agency challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County, Wisconsin, that denied its motion for summary judgment in a suit by plaintiffs, a funeral director and her business manager, alleging a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 by the infringement of their commercial speech and seeking injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The state agency charged the funeral director and her business manager with violating Wis. Admin. Code FD § 2.03(1) (2010), which prohibited anyone other than licensed funeral directors from making funeral arrangements, in allowing the business manager to gather obituary information, meet with pastors, set the time of funeral services, and discussing contract provisions with clients. They filed suit seeking damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, arguing that the application of the regulation unconstitutionally infringed upon their right of commercial speech under U.S. Const. amend I. On review, the court held that the state agency was entitled to summary judgment on the § 1983 claim because the complaint failed to allege that plaintiffs' speech was actually curtailed because of the state agency's action. Because plaintiffs failed to establish an actual constitutional injury, their claim failed. In addition, the parties' appellate arguments were insufficient to permit the court to determine whether the state agency's attempts to apply the regulations were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The denial of summary judgment as to plaintiffs' claim for injunctive relief was affirmed; the denial of summary judgment on plaintiffs' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to enter summary judgment in favor of the state agency on that claim.

State v. Parmley


Appeal No. 2009AP1210-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2010 WI App 79; 325 Wis. 2d 769; 785 N.W.2d 655; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 395


January 14, 2010, Submitted on Briefs  
May 26, 2010, Decided 
May 26, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Parmley, 2010 WI 125, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 570 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
Ct. No. 2004CF564. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: JAMES J. BOLGERT, Judge. Cir.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin) that exempted defendant from registering as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: After the defendant was convicted of second-degree sexual assault of a child, the circuit court ordered him to register as a sex offender. The circuit later granted defendant's request for exemption from the registration requirements under Wis. Stat. § 301.45 (2003-04) because at the time of the offense the age difference between the defendant and the victim was 4 years; the defendant was 18 and the victim was 14. On appeal, the State argued that the age difference should have been calculated by using the parties' dates of birth instead of their ages. The court of appeals agreed. The court noted that under the defendant's view, there could be almost a five-year gap between an actor and a victim. But, calculating age disparity comparing birth dates was more consistent with the purpose of registration and using the parties' dates of birth prevented the exception to registration from including actors who were more than four years older than the victim. The court held that application of the exemption from registration as a sex offender when the actor is "not more than 4 years older," was properly determined by calculating the time between the birth dates of the actor and the victim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Godlewski v. Godlewski Living Trust


Appeal No. 2009AP1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2010 WI App 71; 325 Wis. 2d 403; 786 N.W.2d 490; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 329



April 29, 2010, Decided 
April 29, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Monroe County: TODD L. ZIEGLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008CV205.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a son's children, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Wisconsin), which granted defendant daughter's motion to dismiss an action to interpret a trust.


OVERVIEW: The mother, a resident of Illinois, created a trust. The mother was the trustee. The trust was funded with her assets, which included a farm in Wisconsin. All of the other assets were in Illinois. Her son and his family lived on the farm in Wisconsin. Her daughter, the successor trustee, lived in Illinois. Upon the mother's death, the daughter became the trustee. After the son died, three of his children filed an action for a declaration that the true intent of the mother was that the son's share of the trust be distributed to his living descendants. The trial court granted the daughter's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction. On appeal, the court found that the trust met its burden of establishing that, notwithstanding the minimum contact of owning the Wisconsin farm property and the mother and daughter's visits after the trust was created, Wisconsin's exercise of jurisdiction over the trust did not comport with fair play and substantial justice. The burden on the trust if the action was litigated in Wisconsin would be significant and the interest of the interstate judicial system in obtaining the most efficient resolution of the controversy heavily favored Illinois.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Luckett

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO

April 21, 2010, Decided 
April 21, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: BRUCE E. SCHROEDER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008CM1747.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County, Wisconsin, convicting him for obstructing an officer, as a repeater, and from a postconviction order affirming the conditions imposed on defendant while on extended supervision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had prior convictions for battery, disorderly conduct, and bail jumping. His current conviction for obstructing an officer stemmed from a domestic dispute. The circuit court set conditions for defendant's extended supervision, including restrictions required him to obtain the court's permission before residing with women and children. He claimed the condition was unconstitutionally overbroad, unreasonable, and imposed without authority. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin upheld the condition of his extended supervision. The condition was reasonably related to his offense, reflected the concern for women and children in the community, provided an opportunity for defendant to overcome the condition by applying for permission, and addressed defendant's need to overcome his violent behavior. The circuit court did not go beyond the parameters of the original sentencing conditions when it added this condition to defendant's extended supervision after sentencing without a hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order was affirmed.

State v. Rosche


Appeal No. 2008AP1037-CR

2010 WI App 62; 324 Wis. 2d 582; 785 N.W.2d 687; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 222



March 25, 2010, Decided 
March 25, 2010, Filed

Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Rosche v. Paquin, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 73854 (E.D. Wis., May 24, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Monroe County: TODD L. ZIEGLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CF74.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of second-degree sexual assault of a child as a repeat offender in the circuit court for Monroe County (Wisconsin). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in applying the patient/therapist privilege to the victim's failure to report her assault during therapy, and that the error deprived him of his right to a fair trial by limiting his ability to present a defense. He argued that nondisclosure of something did not qualify as a "communication" within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 905.04 (2007-08). The court appeals found that any error was harmless. The absence of direct testimony from the victim that she did not tell her therapist about the assault did not prohibit the defendant from getting that same information before the jury. Given testimony that the victim first disclosed the assault to a friend and to a teacher a year and a half after the assault, it was an obvious inference that she had not disclosed the assault to the therapist. Defendant was not prohibited from asking the victim why she delayed reporting, or from exploring the answer that she gave when the State asked her that question. The defendant did not identify any argument he could have made based on testimony from the victim that he could not have made based upon evidence that was already before the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

630 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


In re Rachel


Appeal No. 2009AP1132


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI App 60; 324 Wis. 2d 465; 782 N.W.2d 443; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 217


January 27, 2010, Submitted on Briefs 
March 24, 2010, Decided 
March 24, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: WILBUR W. WARREN, III, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1994CF469.
State v. Rachel (In re Rachel), 2002 WI 81, 254 Wis. 2d 215, 647 N.W.2d 762, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 479 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County, Wisconsin, that denied his petition for supervised release from his Wis. Stat. ch. 980 commitment, arguing that the circuit court applied an incorrect legal standard and erroneously allocated the burden of proof to him.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a petition under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 for the commitment of petitioner as a sexually violent person. Twelve years later, the State filed notice of petitioner's right to apply for discharge. Petitioner applied for supervised release rather than discharge. Following a hearing, the circuit court concluded that petitioner failed to show by clear and convincing evidence that supervised release should be granted. On review, the court held that, when the legislature revised Wis. Stat. § 980.08(4) (2007-2008), it eliminated the State's burden of proof on a committed person's petition for supervised release and now authorized a circuit court to grant supervised release if petitioner demonstrated by clear and convincing evidence that he met the five criteria under Wis. Stat. § 980.08(4)(cg). Petitioner failed to make such a showing because he had more work to do in treatment, because a more specific and well-defined post-release treatment plan was needed, and because petitioner did not establish a substantial probability that he was unlikely to engage in sexual violence if discharged on supervised release.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was affirmed.

APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: J. MAC DAVIS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CF496.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him following a jury trial of, among other things, two counts of sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(d) (2007-08) and twenty-seven counts of capturing a nude representation in violation Wis. Stat. § 942.09(2)(am)1 (2007-08).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's girlfriend knew that defendant took six to nine pictures of her in the nude while she was unconscious after a night of heavy drinking. Police later discovered that he actually took twenty-seven photographs of the victim while she was nude and unconscious, including photographs depicting defendant digitally penetrating the victim's anus and vagina. Defendant argued on appeal that Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(d), which prohibited sexual contact or sexual intercourse with a person who the defendant knew was unconscious, was unconstitutionally overbroad. The court disagreed. Because § 940.225(2)(d) could be applied constitutionally to defendant, he could not argue that it might conceivably be unconstitutional on facts not before the court. Second, there was sufficient evidence supporting the nude representation charges. Although defendant and the victim might have slept together regularly in the nude, the victim had a reasonable expectation of privacy under the circumstances that she would not be recorded in the nude. Further, there was ample evidence for the jury to conclude the victim did not consent to defendant photographing her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

State v. O'Connell


Appeal No. 2009AP2289-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ELLEN R. BROSTROM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008CT4324.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of operating while under the influence of an intoxicant, third offense, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2007-08). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his motion to suppress should have been granted. The appellate court noted that the State conceded that defendant had an actual, subjective expectation of privacy in the stairwell leading to his apartment, and that this expectation was reasonable. The State failed to show whether defendant took precautions to protect his privacy in the stairwell, or whether his claim of privacy there was inconsistent with historical notions of privacy. The officers' warrantless entry into defendant's stairwell was not justified by exigent circumstances because at the time of the entry, the officers had no basis to believe the underlying offense was a jailable offense. Because the officers entered into defendant's residence prior to the determination of whether defendant's actions were subject to the penalty of jail, the warrantless entry into the residence was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Baake


Appeal No. 2009AP713-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2010 WI App 46; 324 Wis. 2d 306; 784 N.W.2d 183; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 104



February 4, 2010, Decided 
February 4, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Portage County: JOHN V. FINN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008CT162.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin) with operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant and operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration. After the court granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence, the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State contends that police validly stopped defendant's vehicle based on reasonable suspicion that defendant failed to yield to a stopped police car contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.072. The court of appeals disagreed. Section 346.072 required a motorist to slow his rate of speed while passing an emergency vehicle if there was only one lane in the motorist's direction or if there were two lanes but a lane change was unsafe. The statute did not require a motorist on a roadway with only one lane of travel in the motorist's direction to move into the lane for oncoming traffic when passing a stopped motor vehicle. Defendant was proceeding along a roadway with only one lane of travel in his direction, and therefore, he was required to slow his vehicle while passing the squad car. The officer did not provide any testimony that defendant failed to slow down or that he was traveling at an unsafe speed, or any other details that would support reasonable suspicion of a traffic violation. Therefore, the trial court properly granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM SOSNAY AND DENNIS R. CIMPL, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CF4362.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him upon a jury verdict of first-degree reckless injury while armed and being a felon in possession of a firearm, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 940.23(1)(a), 939.63, and 941.29(2)(a) (2007-08). He also appealed from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief without a hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued with his ex-girlfriend at her mother's home. Defendant shot her adult brother in the neck when he asked defendant to leave. Defendant claimed it was an accident. Defendant was distraught after the shooting, said that he did not mean to do it, and asked the mother to shoot him. During deliberations, the jury twice asked whether it could consider facts and circumstances after the shooting in deciding whether defendant showed an utter disregard for human life under § 940.23(1)(a). Over defendant's objections, the trial court read language from the Jensen case to the jury. On appeal, the court ordered a new trial on first-degree reckless injury because there was a reasonable likelihood that the trial court's answer misled the jury and that it applied potentially confusing instructions in an unconstitutional manner. There was a reasonable likelihood that the jury interpreted the answer as suggesting that defendant's after-the-fact conduct was not important or compelling, that it should not be considered equally with other circumstances, or that no amount of after-the-fact regard for human life could negate early behavior suggesting disregard for human life.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for being a felon in possession of a firearm because he abandoned the issue on appeal. The court reversed defendant's conviction for first-degree reckless injury and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

State v. Tischer

January 14, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Wood County: JAMES M. MASON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CT493.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, appellant pled guilty to operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration, third offense, Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b), and the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin) entered a judgment of conviction. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: An anonymous tip told police that someone in a car matching appellant's was seen dumping beer in a parking lot. An officer responded, found appellant's car and followed him, observing appellant driving under the speed limit and hugging the dividing line. Appellant was stopped and based on the findings during the stop, he was charged with drunk driving. Appellant argued that the stop violated the Fourth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11, because it was not supported by reasonable suspicion that he had an open intoxicant on a public highway, Wis. Stat. § 346.935, or that he was driving while intoxicated, Wis. Stat. § 346.63. The court concluded that the totality of the circumstances did not amount to reasonable suspicion supporting the stop. The tip was from an unknown informant calling from an unknown location and it provided no verifiable information beyond the easily obtained information of the location of appellant's car, the car's description, and license plate number. The officer's observations did not bolster the reliability of the tip that appellant had poured beer out of his car in the parking lot, as they did not corroborate any information received in the tip.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

Vill. of Butler v. Clay


Appeal No. 2009AP1763


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2010 WI App 33; 323 Wis. 2d 824; 781 N.W.2d 551; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 21



January 13, 2010, Decided 
January 13, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: Linda M. Van De Water, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2009CV470.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a default judgment entered by the Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Wisconsin, arguing that the circuit court erred in entering a default judgment based upon his nonappearance because he did appear through counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant failed to personally appear for his trial on a charge of operating a vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OWI), first offense, although counsel appeared in his behalf. The circuit court, noting that defendant had not personally appeared at his suppression hearing and that it had ordered defendant to appear at all subsequent judicial proceedings, ordered a default judgment. On review, the court held that the circuit court lacked authority to default a defendant in a noncriminal action as long as defendant appeared by his attorney. Under Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 11.02, a party in a civil action appeared by the fact that counsel appeared, and under Wis. Const. art. I, § 21, defendant was afforded the right to choose whether to defend himself personally or to have his attorney do it. The circuit court lacked authority to require defendant to personally appear, so long as counsel for defendant appeared.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

In re Grandparental Visitation of Opichka v. Opichka


Appeal No. 2009AP40


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2010 WI App 23; 323 Wis. 2d 510; 780 N.W.2d 159; 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 28



January 13, 2010, Decided 
January 13, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: JOHN S. JUDE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007PR302.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County, Wisconsin, that granted visitation to respondents, his children's maternal grandparents, under Wis. Stat. § 54.56 (2007-08) and ordered that the grandparents would have overnight visitation during the second weekend of each month as well as one full week during the summer.


OVERVIEW: After the children's mother died, her parents petitioned for visitation. On review of the circuit court order granting visitation, the court rejected the father's argument that the award was contrary to law because it was akin to a physical placement award under Wis. Stat. § 767.001(5) (2007-08) as found in divorce cases and thus put the grandparents on equal footing with a divorced parent who did not have primary placement of the children. During visitation, the grandparents had the responsibility to make routine daily decisions regarding the child's care but could not make any decisions inconsistent with the major decisions made by a person having legal custody, and the same was true of a parent who did not have joint legal custody but had a right to physical placement. In both instances, routine daily decisions could be made, but nothing greater, and examples of such minor matters included what and when to eat, what clothes to wear, and when to go to bed. Therefore, the visit, whether for a few hours or an overnight, was still a visit, and the quantity of time ordered did not depend on whether it was a visitation order or a physical placement order.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was affirmed.

APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CF2882.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Proceeding pro se, appellant inmate sought review of an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denying his pro se motion to modify his reconfinement sentence. The inmate previously pleaded guilty to one count of second-degree sexual assault of a fourteen-year-old girl in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2) (2001-02). He was sentenced to three years of initial confinement and eight years of extended supervision.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had a sexual relationship with a fourteen-year-old girl who was thirty-one years his junior. Pursuant to his plea agreement, the circuit court imposed a no-contract provision barring the inmate from having any contact with the victim. The inmate did not object, did not pursue a direct appeal of the sentence, and did not file a motion under Wis. When he was released to extended supervision, he began living with the victim, married her, and never informed his extended supervision agent. The circuit court imposed reconfinement, and the inmate again did not appeal. The court upheld the order denying relief because (1) the inmate did not identify any new factors that would justify sentence modification; and (2) his motion, even construed as brought under Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2007-08), did not establish a violation of his constitutional right to marry. Although the inmate both waived and forfeited his right to contest the provision, continuing to deny him the right to have contact with the adult victim was constitutionally reasonable under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order.

State v. Reinwall


Appeal No. 2009AP1840


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2010 WI App 19; 323 Wis. 2d 279; 779 N.W.2d 725; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 954



December 17, 2009, Decided 
December 17, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: JOHN W. MARKSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008TR19377, 2008TR19378.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI) and operating with a prohibited alcohol concentration (PAC) of.10 or more, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) and (b) (2007-08), first offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his detention by the arresting officer was not supported by reasonable suspicion or by the community caretaker exception and, therefore, the circuit court should have granted his motion to suppress evidence. The appellate court found that the facts as found by the circuit court met the objective standard of a bona fide community caretaker activity. It was clearly unusual for a motorcyclist to be stopped on the shoulder of a moderately busy interstate highway with no lights activated and talking on a cell phone. The trooper's manner of performing his community caretaker function was reasonable. The trooper's approach to determine if defendant needed assistance in these circumstances was reasonable. The public's substantial interest in ensuring that police assist motorists, including motorcyclists, who may be stranded on the highway outweighed the limited intrusion into defendant's privacy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
