State v. Lesik


Appeal No. 2008AP3072-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2010 WI App 12; 322 Wis. 2d 753; 780 N.W.2d 210; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 917



December 1, 2009, Decided 
December 1, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Lesik, 2010 WI 110, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 238 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: J. MAC DAVIS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CF835.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Wisconsin, convicting him for sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sexually assaulting his stepdaughter. She reported that when she was seven years old, defendant came into her bedroom several times after she had gone to bed, rubbed her vagina underneath her clothes and penetrated her vagina with his finger. Defendant was charged with two counts of first-degree sexual assault of a child. On appeal of his conviction, he argued Wis. Stat. § 948.02 was unconstitutional because it did not contain a medical care exception. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin found that it would be absurd to imagine the legislature intended to include legitimate medical procedures within the bounds of the sexual assault of a child statute. Because this construction of Wis. Stat. § 948.02 cured the statute's silence regarding medically appropriate conduct, it was not unconstitutionally overbroad. The circuit court amended the standard jury instruction to add the clarification that sexual intercourse "does not include an intrusion for a proper non-sexual purpose, such as a medical examination." This instruction fully and completely conveyed the theory of the defense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gillund v. Meridian Mut. Ins. Co.


Appeal No. 2008AP1301


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI App 4; 323 Wis. 2d 1; 778 N.W.2d 662; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 921


May 29, 2009, Submitted on Briefs

December 1, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Winnebago County: WILLIAM H. CARVER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV1462.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed summary judgment granted by the Circuit Court for Winnebago County, Wisconsin, in favor of defendant insurance companies under Wis. Stat. § 802.08, arguing that the circuit court erred in concluding that none of the three homeowners' insurance policies afforded coverage for acts constituting an invasion of her privacy.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a young woman who periodically stayed with her aunt and uncle until it was discovered that her uncle had, without her knowledge or consent, taken pictures and made videos of her in various stages of undress. She filed suit against her uncle and against the insurance companies that issued homeowners' policies of insurance. On review of summary judgment, the court held that summary judgment was properly granted in favor of two of the insurance companies because, under policy language, coverage was not afforded for intentional acts or violations of the penal law. As to the third insurance company, which joined the lawsuit by filing a motion to intervene, the court held that summary judgment was improper. The motion to intervene was not, as required by Wis. Stat. § 803.09(3), accompanied by a pleading setting forth the claim or defense for which intervention was sought. Because no pleading was ever filed by the third insurance company, coverage under its policy was never put in issue; without a pleading from that party, the court could not examine the pleadings to determine if factual issues existed between the parties.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of two of the insurance companies was affirmed, but summary judgment in favor of the third insurance company was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.


 

644 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Phillips


Appeal No. 2009AP249-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 179; 322 Wis. 2d 576; 778 N.W.2d 157; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 847



November 3, 2009, Decided 
November 3, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 16, 2009.
Review denied by State v. Phillips, 2010 WI 53, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 154 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: TIMOTHY M. WITKOWIAK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF6302.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of delivery of a controlled substance, cocaine; possession of a controlled substance, tetrahydrocannabinols (marijuana); and possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, cocaine, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 961.41(1)(cm)1g, 961.41(3g)(e), 961.41(1m)(cm)1r, and 961.48 (2005-06). The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred under the Fourth Amendment by denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained in a search because the police created the exigent circumstances that led them to enter his house following a controlled buy completed by an undercover police officer. The reviewing court held that the exigent circumstances were not manufactured by the police. The police decided to conduct a knock and talk after the undercover officer exited defendant's house having purchased drugs from defendant, and on the way to the back door to conduct the knock and talk, the police saw defendant standing in the doorway. Defendant, after seeing the police, fled into the residence and shut the door. Defendant, not the police, created the exigency (the risk that evidence would be destroyed) that resulted in the warrantless search when, after seeing the police outside the residence, he retreated into the residence and shut the door after the police ordered him to stop. The court also held that it was a proper exercise of discretion when the trial court denied defendant's postconviction motion without holding a Machner hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

 

645 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Xiong v. Kulcinski


Appeal No. 2008AP1588


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 174; 322 Wis. 2d 573; 776 N.W.2d 287; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 841



October 29, 2009, Decided 
October 29, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Xiong v. Kulcinski, 2010 WI 53, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 132 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse County: RAMONA A. GONZALEZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CV174.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver and appellant insurer of the driver separately appealed a judgment entered by the circuit court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) following a jury trial in a personal injury action brought by respondents, a seven-year-old child pedestrian appearing by his guardian ad litem who was struck by the driver near a school and the child's parents. Respondents sought frivolous appeal costs and fees under Wis. Stat. § 809.25(3) (2007-08).


OVERVIEW: The driver struck the child on a street near a school where the posted speed limit was 15 miles per hour when children were present. The circuit court held that the driver was negligent as a matter of law because he was driving in excess of 15 miles per hour in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.57(4) (2007-08). The jury subsequently apportioned 80 percent of the causal negligence to him. The court rejected the driver's argument that § 346.57(4) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of the case. Construing § 346.57(4)(b) according to the common meaning of its terms, it put the driver on notice that when children were both visible and so near a school that they were in or next to a street adjacent to the school, he was required to reduce his speed to 15 miles per hour. Further, the circuit court did not erroneously exercise its discretion in denying the driver's request for a separate inquiry on the special verdict as to whether the child was outside the crosswalk when he was struck. Finally, improper remarks by respondents' counsel during closing arguments which referred to the parties' failure to settle did not warrant a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment and denied respondents' motion for frivolous appeal costs and fees.

In re Cameron W.


Appeal Nos. 2009AP1472, 2009AP1473, 2009AP1474


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE

NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Marathon County Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. Lynn W., 2010 WI 5, 322 Wis. 2d 128, 779 N.W.2d 180, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 881 (2009)
Review denied by Marathon County Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. Lynn W., 2010 WI 5, 322 Wis. 2d 128, 779 N.W.2d 180, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 825 (2009)
Review denied by Marathon County Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. Lynn W., 2010 WI 5, 322 Wis. 2d 128, 779 N.W.2d 180, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 768 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEALS from orders of the circuit court for Marathon County: THOMAS CANE, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2008TP32, 2008TP33, 2008TP34.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Marathon County, Wisconsin, terminated appellant mother's rights to her three minor children under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4) (2007-08). The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the conditions of return in the underlying no-contact order violated her substantive due process right to parent her children as her cognitive disability prevented her from satisfying the conditions. The appellate court noted that the circuit court found the conditions listed in the children in need of protection or services (CHIPS) order obtainable but determined that the mother was unwilling to satisfy them. Petitioner Marathon County Department of Social Services (Social Services) accounted for the mother's limitations and disabilities when making these efforts. The conditions of return were tailored to address Social Services' concerns regarding the mother's interaction with her children. Specific facts in the record supported each condition. The record was replete with circumstances justifying the mother's participation in the Parenting Education Program. The conditions established by the CHIPS order were designed to address the mother's self-esteem and relationship issues. Her abusive behavior toward her husband and his child by another marriage justified the requirement that she demonstrate control over aggressive behaviors and dangerous actions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Peters


Appeal No. 2009AP384-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 174; 322 Wis. 2d 574; 776 N.W.2d 288; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 788



October 8, 2009, Decided 
October 8, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: JOHN W. MARKSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CT4050.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County (Wisconsin) convicting her upon her plea of no contest to a charge of operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration, fourth offense, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b) (2007-08). She also appealed the circuit court's order denying her motion to suppress evidence gained as a result of an investigatory stop of her vehicle.


OVERVIEW: During a stop of defendant's vehicle for a registration violation, the police officer became aware that there was an outstanding warrant for her arrest and that she had prior offenses for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. Although defendant did not seem impaired, the officer noticed a slight odor of alcohol and she admitted drinking two beers. The officer administered a preliminary breath test (PBT) because jail regulations prohibited booking intoxicated inmates. The State later sought to use the 0.02 reading as evidence against defendant to show a violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) and (b). The court overturned the conviction. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 343.303 restricted the admissibility of PBT results in all proceedings relating to violations of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1). Although the PBT was initially administered for another reason, the State was still prohibited from using the results to prove that defendant had violated § 346.63(1). Without the PBT results, the officer did not have probable cause to arrest defendant for violating § 346.63(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and order of the circuit court.

State v. McQueen


Appeal No. 2008AP1407-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 174; 322 Wis. 2d 573; 776 N.W.2d 287; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 757



October 1, 2009, Decided 
October 1, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: STEVEN D. EBERT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CT2319.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicant, third offense, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2007-08). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the evidence obtained during the traffic stop of his vehicle. He contended that the stop violated his constitutional rights because the police lacked reasonable suspicion to conduct the traffic stop. The appellate court found that the tip in the case did not add anything of value to its reasonable suspicion analysis. However, the remaining facts in the record--that the officers observed defendant drifting back and forth two to three times within his line and then cross the fog line, at bar time--provided reasonable suspicion of intoxicated driving that supported the stop. A witness' report of seeing a driver he or she believed was "possibly impaired" did not indicate what the witness had observed, and there was irrelevant. However, the officers observed defendant drifting back and forth in his land, and then cross the fog line, at bar time. These facts together provided a reasonable suspicion that defendant was driving while intoxicated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

649 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Town of Cross Plains v. Kitt's "Field of Dreams" Korner, Inc.


Appeal No. 2008AP546


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI App 142; 321 Wis. 2d 671; 775 N.W.2d 283; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 737


July 9, 2009, Oral Argument 
September 24, 2009, Decided 
September 24, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Town of Cross Plains v. Kitt's "Field of Dreams" Korner, Inc., 2010 WI 5, 322 Wis. 2d 124, 779 N.W.2d 177, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 787 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV1424, 2005CV1519, 2005CV2035.
Town of Cross Plains v. Kitt's "Field of Dreams" Korner, Inc., 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 247 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 2, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, granted summary judgment in favor of respondent town by finding that appellant owners' use of the premises for adult entertainment from February 11, 2005, until the effective date of the ordinance amendment did not create a vested interest in an ongoing adult entertainment business and therefore was not a lawful nonconforming use. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners argued they were entitled to summary judgment because the undisputed facts showed there was actual and active use of the tavern as an adult entertainment venue on the effective date of the ordinance amendment and that was sufficient to give them a vested interest in the continuance of that use for purposes of Wis. Stat. § 59.69(10)(a) (2007-08). The appellate court found that, in order for a use to be protected under the statute, at the time the new ordinance became effective, the business owner had to have a vested interest in the continuation of that use, meaning that, were the continuance of the use to be prohibited, substantial rights would be adversely affected. Because the owners did not reasonably rely on existing law when they made the expenditures and incurred the liabilities to establish an adult entertainment use of the premises, they did not acquire a vested interest by virtue of those investments and incurred liabilities, regardless of the amount. The purpose of § 59.69(10)(a) was undermined if a business owner may avail himself of the protection of the statute by establishing a use after learning that it would soon be prohibited.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Osborne


Appeal No. 2008AP1519-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2009 WI App 158; 321 Wis. 2d 748; 776 N.W.2d 100; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 717



September 15, 2009, Decided 
September 15, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Osborne, 2010 WI 53, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 87 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Marathon County: DOROTHY L. BAIN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CF492.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Marathon County, Wisconsin, denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained during the execution of an allegedly defective search warrant.


OVERVIEW: An officer prepared a search warrant complaint. The affidavit stated that a man had reported several items missing from his garage. A neighbor saw the missing items in plain view in defendant's house. A search warrant was issued the same day; it was an exact copy of the complaint. The judge modified the title of the complaint to read "search warrant" and substituted his signature for that of the officer. But instead of directing the officers to search the premises, the document concluded by requesting that the judge issue a search warrant. Defendant argued that the search warrant did not comply with Wis. Stat. § 968.12(1), and that the search was executed in violation of his constitutional rights. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin held that the omission of an explicit directive to the officers did not affect defendant's right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. Therefore, the evidence obtained from the search was admissible.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's suppression motion was affirmed.

Metro. Assocs. v. City of Milwaukee


Appeal No. 2009AP524


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 157; 321 Wis. 2d 632; 774 N.W.2d 821; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 705



September 9, 2009, Decided 
September 9, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Metro. Assocs. v. City of Milwaukee, 2010 WI 5, 322 Wis. 2d 122, 779 N.W.2d 176, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 811 (2009)
Reversed by Metro. Assocs. v. City of Milwaukee, 2011 WI 20, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 154 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEAN W. DI MOTTO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008CV9866.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant City of Milwaukee appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granting summary judgment to plaintiff taxpayer. The order declared unconstitutional Wis. Stat. § 74.37(4)(c) and (4)(d) and enjoined the City from relying on those subsections in connection with challenges to the assessment of real property brought under Wis. Stat. § 74.37.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Wisconsin previously determined in Nankin v. Village of Shorewood that Wis. Stat. § 74.37(6) violated the equal-protection rights of property taxpayers in Milwaukee County under Wis. Const. art. I, § 1 because it prevented them from getting a review of their assessments by filing an action under Wis. Stat. § 74.37(3)(d) and relegated them to a more limited review by certiorari. By enacting Wis. Stat. § 74.37(4)(c) and (4)(d), the Wisconsin Legislature attempted to meet Nankin's equal-protection concerns but still give communities the ability to opt out of the action route by the adoption of an appropriate ordinance. The City adopted such an ordinance. The taxpayer brought an action on behalf of itself and other similarly situated taxpayers seeking a declaration that the opt-out provision deprived it of equal protection. The court found no violation because the statute not only gave taxpayers in jurisdictions with such ordinances the functional equivalent of a court trial, it also changed board of review procedure to give to the taxpayer a more level playing field. Thus, the treatment of taxpayers in jurisdictions with ordinances was not substantially different.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

State v. Thomas


Appeal No. 2009AP426-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 158; 321 Wis. 2d 750; 776 N.W.2d 101; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 681



September 1, 2009, Decided 
September 1, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: BONNIE L. GORDON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008CM761.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, convicting him of misdemeanor theft as a party to a crime, making him jointly and severally liable for restitution, and denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty, as party to a crime, to misdemeanor theft of movable property with a value of less than $ 2,500, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.20(1)(a), (3)(a), 939.05. He contended that the judgment making him jointly and severally liable for restitution with his co-actor violated his right to due process. The circuit court did not err by denying postconviction relief. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin held that Wis. Stat. § 973.20(7) permitted sentencing courts to impose joint and several liability for restitution. In this case, the plea bargain called for restitution. Thus, appellant waived his right to complain about it on appeal. Appellant did not explain why he should not be held to the bargain. He also failed to demonstrate that Wis. Stat. § 973.20(7) was unconstitutional, or that the circuit court denied his right to due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

 

653 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Konkel v. Acuity


Appeal No. 2008AP2156


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 132; 321 Wis. 2d 306; 775 N.W.2d 258; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 629



August 11, 2009, Decided 
August 11, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Konkel v. Acuity, 2010 WI 5, 322 Wis. 2d 125, 779 N.W.2d 178, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 721 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CHRISTOPHER R. FOLEY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV12905.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury suit in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), appellants, an insurer and its insured, brought a third-party complaint in subrogation against respondents, a physician and his practice, for alleged unnecessary surgery performed on the person who filed the personal injury suit. The trial court granted respondents' summary judgment motion, and appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The insurer said Wis. Stat. ch. 655 (2007-08) did not abolish its subrogation claim. The appellate court disagreed because ch. 655's framework did not permit such claims and allowing them would contradict ch. 655's legislative purposes by creating new exposure for health care providers, since the physician's patient did not sue him for malpractice. The insurer's argument that it sought reimbursement of payments to the patient for damages from unnecessary surgery did not remove its claim from ch. 655 because the claim alleged medical malpractice, and a subrogation claim was subject to all limits applicable had the patient brought it. The insurer and its insured lacked standing because they were not a patient or representative, under Wis. Stat. § 655.001(10) and (12) (2007-08), nor were they equitable patients or representatives, as this would contradict Wis. Stat. ch. 655's (2007-08) intent. Applying ch. 655 to bar the insurer's claim did not offend equal protection because it was germane to ch. 655's purposes to reduce malpractice claims. Public policy barred the claim because it encouraged unnecessary treatment claims and strained physician/patient relationships.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

654 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



State ex rel. Kuehne v. Burdette


Appeal No. 2008AP1342


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2009 WI App 119; 320 Wis. 2d 784; 772 N.W.2d 225; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 482



July 7, 2009, Decided 
July 7, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Kuehne v. Burdette, 2010 WI 5, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 794 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown County: WILLIAM M. ATKINSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008CV406.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent residents sought an injunction against appellant town, which was holding a referendum. The Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, held a preliminary hearing, but declined to issue any orders before the election. The day following the passage of the referendum, the trial court issued a temporary injunction against the town. Two months later, the trial court issued a permanent injunction against the town. The town appealed.


OVERVIEW: The residents attempted to incorporate into a village. The department of administration's incorporation review board dismissed the petition. The legislature passed a biennial budget, creating Wis. Stat. § 66.0203 (2007-08). Wis. Stat. § 66.0203(11) (2007-08), as created by the budget bill, specifically provided for the town to incorporate into a village. As a result, the statute violated the constitutional prohibition in Wis. Const. art. IV, § 31(9) (2007-08). The constitutional provision prohibited the enactment of special or private laws for incorporating a village. The town argued there was no factual basis for granting an injunction because although the residents presented evidence at the preliminary hearing, they did not present evidence at the permanent injunction hearing. First, the town did not claim it was foreclosed from presenting evidence at the permanent injunction hearing. In fact, it did present evidence of its own. Second, the town did not argue the evidence from the preliminary injunction hearing was insufficient to support a permanent injunction. Therefore, the appellate court concluded the permanent injunction was supported by an adequate factual basis.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Terrance D. v. Tonia D. (In re Natasha J.D.)


Appeal No. 2008AP1597


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2009 WI App 110; 320 Wis. 2d 703; 771 N.W.2d 929; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 425



June 16, 2009, Decided 
June 16, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Terrance D. v. Tonia D., 2009 WI 99, 775 N.W.2d 532, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 401 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Oneida County: PATRICK F. O'MELIA, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007GN37.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the order for guardianship entered by the Circuit Court for Oneida County, Wisconsin, appointing respondent sister, as guardian of his child who was born with Down syndrome.


OVERVIEW: The child was approximately twenty-three years old at the time of the guardianship hearing, but had been developmentally disabled since birth. The child functioned mentally at the level of a third grader. There was no dispute that the child required a guardian, and the only issue at the guardianship hearing was who should serve as guardian, the child's father or the child's sister. The appellate court ruled that the circuit court applied the correct legal standard and its findings were not clearly erroneous under Wis. Stat. § 805.17(2) (2007-2008). The circuit court specifically found that the child's best interest would not be served by appointing the father as guardian under Wis. Stat. § 54.15(5) (2007-2008). The circuit court contrasted the father's desire to cloister the child and limit her social contact and development potential, with the opportunities the sister provided. The sister utilized multiple caregivers and tutors who provided diversified experiences for the child. By all accounts, the child was thriving, well adjusted, and had made friends in her current active social environment.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

656 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pryes


Appeal No. 2009AP2-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2009 WI App 110; 320 Wis. 2d 705; 771 N.W.2d 930; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 413



June 10, 2009, Decided 
June 10, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Manitowoc County: PATRICK L. WILLIS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CM828.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was then 51 years old, was charged with having sexual intercourse with a child who was not his spouse and who had attained the age of 16 years, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 948.09, 939.51(3)(a) (2007-08). After denying defendant's motion to dismiss, the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County, Wisconsin, convicted him and sentenced him to. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss on the ground that Wis. Stat. § 948.09 (2007-08) was unconstitutional because it applied to unmarried persons age 16 and 17, but not to married persons of the same age, thus creating a classification that was irrational and served no legitimate state purpose. The appellate court disagreed, holding that there was a rational basis which justified the legislature's decision to treat differently unmarried and married 16 and 17 year olds. Many of the significant interests of the State were addressed when a minor obtained permission to marry, most obviously the lack of considered consent, heightened vulnerability to physical and psychological harm, the lack of mature judgment, the potential for sexual exploitation, and the potential for a minor bearing a child outside of a marital relationship. Wis. Stat. § 948.09 (2007-08) reflected the legislature's judgment that absent the assurance of parental guidance and considered consent involved in the marriage of a minor, the State was justified in continuing to protect the minor until age 18.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

657 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Flynn


Appeal No. 2008AP2017-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 95; 320 Wis. 2d 484; 769 N.W.2d 878; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 551



May 27, 2009, Decided 
May 27, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Flynn, 2009 WI 98, 321 Wis. 2d 49, 775 N.W.2d 256, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 329 (2009)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Dismissed by Flynn v. Radcliff, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 54560 (E.D. Wis., May 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CF3976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of being a felon in possession of a weapon as a habitual criminal in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 941.29(2)(a) and 939.62 (2007-08). He also appealed from the order denying his postconviction motion for relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction for being a felon in possession of a weapon as a habitual criminal and from an order denying his postconviction motion for relief. The appellate court affirmed. Whether a challenge to the information or verdict form would have been successful was uncertain. Moreover, challenging the information, jury instructions, or verdict form would likely have led to the State separating the single possession charge into two separate charges, which trial counsel understandably wanted to avoid. Trial counsel also explained the basis for her strategic decision to make sure that the burglary of the home of defendant's brother-in-law was not mentioned and that decision was reasonable. The evidence was sufficient to support the conviction because the jury heard the brother-in-law's testimony that defendant possessed a gun in the hardware store that the brother-in-law owned and that defendant possessed a lock box that the brother-in-law said that he believed contained a gun. Further, the gun was found in a lock box that was in the trunk of the car that defendant and his wife owned and had parked in their driveway.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

658 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Berggren


Appeal No. 2008AP786-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI App 82; 320 Wis. 2d 209; 769 N.W.2d 110; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 522



May 27, 2009, Decided  
May 27, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Berggren, 2009 WI 98, 321 Wis. 2d 48, 775 N.W.2d 255, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 567 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF6669.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, that convicted him, upon his guilty pleas, of two counts of first-degree sexual assault of a child, two counts of second-degree sexual assault of an unconscious victim, two counts of sexual exploitation of a child, and one count of possession of child pornography, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 948.02(1), 940.225(2)(d), 948.05(1)(b), and 948.12 (2005-06).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's crimes came to light when his 12-year-old daughter discovered photographs of defendant engaged in various sexual acts with his 12-year-old stepdaughter. Defendant's daughter gave the memory stick containing the incriminating photographs to her mother, who in turn contacted her brother, a police lieutenant. On appeal, defendant argued that he should be permitted to withdraw his guilty pleas because his counsel was ineffective in failing to file a motion to suppress evidence related to the seizure of the memory stick. The court rejected defendant's argument because the police lieutenant who viewed the photos did so in responding to his sister's call about his niece, he was off-duty when he went to the home, and his actions were taken in his capacity as the girl's uncle. Further, nothing suggested that he acted to assist governmental efforts; as such, the search was a private search and was not subject to the protections afforded by the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV. Because a suppression motion related to the memory stick would have been denied, trial counsel was not ineffective in failing to assert such a motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

State v. Edwards


Appeal No. 2008AP1186


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 95; 320 Wis. 2d 483; 769 N.W.2d 877; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 379



May 27, 2009, Decided 
May 27, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Edwards, 2009 WI 99, 321 Wis. 2d 572, 775 N.W.2d 532, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 605 (Sept. 24, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1996CF960232A.
State v. Edwards, 2007 WI App 130, 301 Wis. 2d 746, 731 N.W.2d 382, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 296 (Mar. 27, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2007-08) motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed an order that denied his motion for postconviction relief, but the appellate court affirmed, stating that his trial counsel was not ineffective and that meant that postconviction counsel was not ineffective for failing to so allege. Further, postconviction counsel did not provide ineffective assistance during cross-examination of trial counsel at the Machner hearing. The inmate argued under Wis. Stat. § 971.01(2) (2007-08) that trial counsel should have objected to the fact that the information was filed before the preliminary hearing started, but the inmate failed to show prejudice. The complaint was sufficiently detailed as to have apprised the inmate of the charges against him and the information was consistent with the formant spelled out in Wis. Stat. § 971.03. The inmate implicitly acknowledged that the parties spoke off the record. However, he asserted that the entire conference had to have taken place on the record. The appellate court disagreed under Wis. Stat. § 805.13(3). While it would have been preferable for an armed robbery jury instruction to have had more specific language, the language was broad enough to encompass use of an actual firearm.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Clayton


Appeal No. 2008AP481-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 95; 320 Wis. 2d 482; 769 N.W.2d 877; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 565



May 21, 2009, Decided 
May 21, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Clayton, 2009 WI 98, 321 Wis. 2d 47, 775 N.W.2d 254, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 347 (2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Clayton v. Jenkins, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 116236 (E.D. Wis., Oct. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: ROBERT A. DeCHAMBEAU and JOHN W. MARKSON, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF1379.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of armed robbery and possessing a firearm as a convicted felon. He also sought review of an order denying him postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that counsel performed ineffectively because counsel failed to challenge a victim's arrest-scene identification of defendant, and failed to take the steps necessary to introduce the victim's prior convictions as impeachment evidence. The court held that counsel's decision not to challenge the victim's arrest-scene identification of defendant was a reasonable exercise of professional judgment, even if the court assumed that counsel could have persuaded the court to suppress the identification. Defendant presented a defense based on one of a previous contacts with the victim, and how it gave the victim a motive to falsely accuse defendant. A defense of misidentification would have directly conflicted with the defense actually presented, and a reasonable attorney could have chosen to avoid that conflict. Further, even it the court assumed counsel's failure to seek admission of the victim's four prior convictions was deficient, defendant failed to show that counsel's omissions prejudiced him. There was no reasonable probability of a different credibility determination, and therefore a different verdict, had the jury known of the victim's four convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

Wis. v. McGuire


Appeal No. 2007AP2711-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2009 WI App 95; 320 Wis. 2d 482; 769 N.W.2d 877; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 378



May 20, 2009, Decided 
May 20, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. McGuire, 2009 WI 99, 321 Wis. 2d 570, 775 N.W.2d 531, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 659 (2009)
Affirmed by State v. McGuire, 2010 WI 91, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 168 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Walworth County: JAMES L. CARLSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF80.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of five counts of having taken indecent liberties with two children in 1967 and 1968, and denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a Jesuit priest, appealed from his convictions for five counts of having taken indecent liberties with two children in 1967 and 1968. His motion for postconviction relief was also denied. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the more than 36-year delay in bringing the criminal charges against him was not inappropriate because the out-of-state tolling provision in the Wis. Stat. § 939.74(1) (1966-69). Defendant was unable to establish that the delay in charging was to gain a tactical advantage since there was no dispute that the State did not learn about the crimes until 2003. The appellate court was also unable to conclude that he was denied the fundamental right to present a defense or that defendant received the ineffective assistance of counsel. Counsel did not overlook a witness, but rather made a reasoned decision not to explore her testimony both because her testimony could have been impeached and it would not have helped the defense. Evidence that defendant sexually assaulted the two boys on other occasions was admissible because the evidence established, in part, that the touching was not a mistake.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

662 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Luu


Appeal No. 2008AP2138-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 91; 319 Wis. 2d 778; 769 N.W.2d 125; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 360



May 14, 2009, Decided 
May 14, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Luu, 2009 WI 98, 775 N.W.2d 256, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 654 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: STUART A. SCHWARTZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CF75.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant petitioner pled no contest to issuing a worthless check, he was placed on three years' probation and ordered to pay restitution. The petitioner failed to satisfy the restitution order. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, subsequently issued an order revoking the petitioner's probation and sentenced him to 18 months' imprisonment. The petitioner's motion for postconviction relief was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the petitioner contended his probation terminated as a matter of law prior to revocation because the probation was extended beyond the maximum possible term of imprisonment for the crime he committed. The appellate court disagreed, holding that Wis. Stat. § 973.09(2) (2007-08) did not prohibit the lower court from extending the petitioner's probation beyond the maximum term of imprisonment the petitioner faced for the crime he committed. The statute limited extensions of probation by requiring extensions to be "for cause," and requiring courts to specify the length of the extension. The plain language of § 973.09 authorized parole extensions beyond the original term of probation, not limited by statutory limits on the original term. Further, there were no constitutional violations in this construction of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

663 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Taylor


Appeal No. 2008AP781-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 77; 319 Wis. 2d 233; 769 N.W.2d 572; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 297



April 23, 2009, Decided 
April 23, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MEL FLANAGAN and TIMOTHY M. WITKOWIAK, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF2984.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied her motion to suppress and convicted her of possession of cocaine, between one and five grams, with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: An officer saw defendant carrying what appeared to be a beer bottle wrapped in a brown paper bag. Suspecting that she was in violation of a public drinking ordinance, the officer approached her. The officer verified that the beer bottle was not open. Defendant was arrested on outstanding warrants. Defendant admitted that she was hiding cocaine on her person. The trial court denied her motion to suppress. She pled guilty to possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. On appeal, the court held that the fact that defendant was walking down the street while carrying what appeared to be a beer bottle wrapped in a brown paper bag did not, alone, provide a reasonable suspicion under Wis. Stat. § 968.24 (2007-08) that she had or was about to commit a crime, even if it was in an area known for public drinking. The circumstances surrounding the stop were insufficient to give rise to a reasonable, articulable suspicion of criminal activity that would justify the intrusion of an investigatory stop. Lacking a legal basis for the stop and subsequent search, the search was unlawful and the evidence seized from defendant's person should have been suppressed as fruit of the poisonous tree.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

664 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robert H. ( In the Interest of Vanessa P.)


Appeal No. 2008AP3086, 2008AP3087


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


319 Wis. 2d 236; 769 N.W.2d 574; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 290



April 21, 2009, Decided 
April 21, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM S. POCAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2006TP327, 2006TP328.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State filed a petition to terminate appellant father's parental rights to respondent children. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, granted the State partial summary judgment on grounds that the children were born of incestuous parenthood (Wis. Stat. § 48.415(7) (2008)). After an evidentiary hearing, it held that it was in the best interests of the children to terminate the father's parental rights. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father and the children's mother were full brother and sister. A psychologist who conducted a competency exam found the father not competent and diagnosed him as having mild mental retardation and adjustment disorder with mixed mood. The father claimed that termination based on § 48.415(7), as applied to him, violated his constitutional right to substantive due process because none of the State's compelling interests in discouraging incestuous parenthood applied, since he and his sister did not grow up as biological siblings. The appellate court held that this fact did not change the risk of genetic defects and the psychological harm to children of incestuous unions caused by being raised by their biological parents. As the State had a compelling interest to prevent incestuous parenthood under the circumstances presented, and § 48.415(7) was narrowly tailored to protect that interest, the statute was constitutional as applied to the father. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.426(3), the trial court properly considered the children's special needs and the father's cognitive delays at the dispositional hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Heine


Appeal No. 2008AP501-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 77; 319 Wis. 2d 233; 769 N.W.2d 572; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 264



April 14, 2009, Decided 
April 14, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Heine, 2009 WI 99, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 479 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CHARLES F. KAHN, JR., and M. JOSEPH DONALD, Judges. 1 Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF4688.


1 The Hon. Charles F. Kahn, Jr., presided over the trial and the first postconviction motion. The Hon. M. Joseph Donald presided over the second postconviction motion.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, orders affirmed in part and reversed in part, and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner was convicted of second-degree sexual assault by use of force and second-degree sexual assault by a correctional staff person. The petitioner voluntarily dismissed his appeal and filed a postconviction motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin denied the motion, and the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the petitioner contended the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions and he should have been granted a new trial based on the unconstitutional withholding of the internal affairs transcripts and report. The appellate court disagreed in part, finding first that testimony from the victim that defendant had sexually assaulted her, evidence that defendant's sperm and DNA were present in sample the victim was able to save and on the victim, and testimony of a forensic scientist in the DNA analysis unit at the Wisconsin State Crime Laboratory supported the convictions. However, the appellate court could not conclude that the transcripts and report would have had no effect upon the factfinder's deliberations. In particular, defendant's report and interviews could have been used to corroborate defendant's testimony, and the victim's interview could have been used to impeach her testimony. The failure to timely produce these documents prior to trial deprived defendant of important material impeachment evidence and of corroborating evidence, both of which he was entitled to receive in order to prepare for trial. Due to this Brady violation, a new trial was warranted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

City of Washburn v. Kreinbring


Appeal No. 2008AP2228-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2009 WI App 56; 317 Wis. 2d 733; 768 N.W.2d 64; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 210



March 24, 2009, Decided 
March 24, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Washburn v. Kreinbring, 2009 WI 99, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 518 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Bayfield County: JOHN P. ANDERSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2008TR432, 2008TR433.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The City appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Bayfield County, Wisconsin, granting defendant's suppression motion.


OVERVIEW: While on patrol, the officer noticed an occupied parked vehicle. When the officer later encountered the same vehicle pulled over to the curb in a different location, he slowed down and shined his spotlight on it. The officer stopped, exited his squad car, and approached the vehicle. Although the officer continued to shine his spotlight, he did not activate the car's red and blue lights. As the officer approached, defendant rolled his window down. The officer detected a strong odor of intoxicants, defendant indicated he had been drinking, and the officer administered field sobriety tests. An Intoxilyzer test subsequently confirmed defendant had a blood-alcohol concentration above the legal limit. The City argued that the circuit court erred by concluding defendant was seized when the officer shined a spotlight on his car. The appellate court ruled that the officer's illumination of defendant's parked vehicle with a spotlight, viewed objectively, was not a show of authority which would lead a reasonable person to believe he or she was not free to leave. Shining a spotlight on a parked car, by itself, was not a seizure.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded.

Oneida County Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. Nicole W. (In re Termination of Parental Rights to Tatiana A.W.)


Appeal No. 2008AP2330


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2009 WI App 56; 317 Wis. 2d 733; 768 N.W.2d 64; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 218



March 23, 2009, Decided 
March 23, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Oneida County Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. Nicole W., 2009 WI 98, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 582 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Oneida County: PATRICK F. O'MELIA, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2008TP5.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Oneida County, Wisconsin, terminating her parental rights under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(10) (2007-2008).


OVERVIEW: The county took the child into custody immediately after she was born and placed her into foster care. Four months later, the circuit court found the child to be a child in need of protection or services. Two years later, a petition to terminate the mother's parental rights was filed. The record was overwhelming in evidence that the mother exhibited poor judgment in caring for herself as well as her child. The appellate court ruled that Wis. Stat. § 48.415(10) was not unconstitutional on its face. The statutory scheme was sufficiently narrowly tailored to the State's interest in protecting children from unfit parents. Also, Wis. Stat. § 48.415 was constitutional as applied to the mother. The mother's unfitness to parent the child was not due to her status as a victim. Rather, it derived from her own history of consistently failing to meet the standards required by Wisconsin law to adequately parent her children. The mother's parental rights were terminated based on her inability to parent the child, not on per se unfitness.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Thiel (In re Commitment of Thiel)


Appeal No. 2007AP2742


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2009 WI App 56; 317 Wis. 2d 729; 768 N.W.2d 62; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 193



March 18, 2009, Decided 
March 18, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Thiel, 2009 WI 99, 319 Wis. 2d 211, 775 N.W.2d 100, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 638 (2009)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Thiel, 2012 Wisc. App. LEXIS 206 (Wis. Ct. App., Mar. 14, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: ROBERT J. WIRTZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1997CF152.
State v. Thiel (In re Thiel), 2004 WI App 225, 277 Wis. 2d 698, 691 N.W.2d 388, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 925 (2004)
State v. Thiel, 2009 WI 23, 315 Wis. 2d 725, 764 N.W.2d 533, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 71 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin), which denied his petition for supervised release from commitment as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had been under a Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (2005-06) commitment order for over a decade. He filed a petition for supervised release. The trial court denied the petition. On appeal, the court ascertained no error in the trial court's exercise of discretion. The trial court specifically addressed the criteria in Wis. Stat. § 980.08(4)(cg), relying on expert testimony to conclude that appellant was more likely than not to reoffend; that he needed additional treatment before he was ready to enter the outside community; that there was insufficient evidence that he would be amenable to treatment; and that the community could not offer reasonable measures for supervising him. The trial court linked each of its findings to testimony given by the experts. The burden rested with appellant to show that the five statutory criteria were met.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

670 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Gehl v. Town Bd. of Perry


Appeal No. 2007AP1067


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 56; 317 Wis. 2d 729; 768 N.W.2d 62; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 184



March 12, 2009, Decided 
March 12, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Gehl v. Town Bd. of Perry, 2010 WI 5, 322 Wis. 2d 123, 779 N.W.2d 176, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 869 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: C. WILLIAM FOUST, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CV1652.
Gehl v. Town of Perry, 2006 WI App 156, 295 Wis. 2d 490, 719 N.W.2d 800, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 536 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner filed an action in the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) against defendants, a town board and board members in their individual capacity, asserting claims arising out of the denial of certain permits and other actions taken by the town. The circuit court granted the board's and the members' motions for summary judgment and dismissed the landowner's complaint in its entirety. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The litigation had been ongoing for years. The landowner owned 225 acres in the town. He purchased an adjacent 22-acre parcel and had been attempting since 2000 to construct a farmhouse, an agricultural accessory building, and a driveway on the 22-acre parcel, but defendants had denied his applications for various permits and had condemned portions of his property for inclusion in a historic district. The landowner argued that the town did not have authority to regulate the location of buildings because such regulation was defined in Wis. Stat. § 59.69(4)(g) (2007-08) as an exercise of zoning powers, which were expressly granted only to counties. The court held that the town's building ordinance was not a zoning ordinance because it did not regulate the use of land by establishing zones, and the ordinance was authorized under Wis. Stat. § 61.34(1) (2007-08). The trial court did not err in refusing to admit evidence of conversations between the parties' attorneys which the landowner contended proved that the town was trying to force him to donate acres to the historic district, but which were inadmissible settlement negotiations under Wis. Stat. § 904.08 (2007-08).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the town.

 

671 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Emerging Energies, LLP v. Manitowoc County


Appeal No. 2008AP1508


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2009 WI App 56; 317 Wis. 2d 731; 768 N.W.2d 63; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 149



March 4, 2009, Decided 
March 4, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Manitowoc County: DARRYL W. DEETS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV280.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County (Wisconsin), which dismissed its action against defendant county for a declaration that a county wind energy system ordinance was invalid.


OVERVIEW: The owner developed renewable energy sources, including wind energy. In 2005, it applied for a conditional use permit (CUP) to build a seven turbine wind energy system in the town. One month after it filed its application, the county enacted a moratorium on granting permits for wind energy systems. In 2006, the county adopted a revised large wind energy system ordinance with an effective date of May 1, 2006. The owner filed a declaratory judgment action, alleging that the ordinance conflicted with Wis. Stat. § 66.0401(1) (2005-06). The trial court dismissed the case, finding that the complaint was not ripe for judicial determination. On appeal, the court found that the owner's facial challenge to the ordinance was not ripe for adjudication. Section 66.0401(1) required a case-by-case approach because the information needed to evaluate the impact of the ordinance on the proposed wind system was quantitative. The owner's "as applied" challenge was likewise unripe because the opinions of its experts failed to take into consideration the discretion vested in the county board of adjustment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Ninham


Appeal No. 2008AP1139


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2009 WI App 64; 316 Wis. 2d 776; 767 N.W.2d 326; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 143



March 3, 2009, Decided 
March 3, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Ninham, 2010 WI 125, 329 Wis. 2d 371, 791 N.W.2d 380, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 434 (2010)
Affirmed by State v. Ninham, 2011 WI 33, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 324 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown County: JOHN D. McKAY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1999CF523.
State v. Ninham, 2002 WI App 34, 250 Wis. 2d 354, 639 N.W.2d 802, 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1240 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which denied his postconviction motion for modification of his life sentence to allow for the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree intentional homicide. He was 14 years old at the time of the crime. The evidence showed that defendant and four accomplices knocked a 13-year-old boy off of his bicycle without provocation, beat him, chased him to the fifth story of a parking ramp, and threw him over the side to his death. Defendant was sentenced to life in prison without the possibility of parole. The trial court denied his motion for sentence modification. On appeal, the court held that the sentence did not violate the constitutional prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. The trial court considered defendant's home life along with the seriousness of the offense, his character, and the need to protect the public. It was not necessary to conclude that defendant would remain incorrigible for the rest of his life or that he was forever irredeemable to support the sentence. The brutality of the crime and the additional offenses defendant committed after his arrest defeated the argument that the sentence was disproportionate to the offense. Recent research on adolescent brain development did not constitute a new factor that would support a sentence reduction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Moua


Appeal No. 2008AP208-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 41; 316 Wis. 2d 773; 766 N.W.2d 241; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 121



February 24, 2009, Decided 
February 24, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: TIMOTHY G. DUGAN and WILLIAM SOSNAY, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF6027.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree recklessly endangering safety while armed and denied his postconviction motion for sentence modification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree recklessly endangering safety while armed. The trial court denied his postconviction motion for sentence modification. On appeal, the court found that defendant's 15-year sentence, with a 10-year period of initial confinement, was not unduly harsh. Defendant had repeatedly fired a sawed-off shotgun and then a handgun into a home occupied with a family and young children, for no apparent reason except possibly as retaliation for gang involvement. The 15-year sentence was well within the 17-year, six-month maximum potential liability for the offense under Wis. Stat. §§ 941.30(1); 939.50(3)(f); and 939.63(1)(b) (2005-06). The sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. Further, defendant's sentence and the sentence of a codefendant were not disparate. The codefendant's three-year period of initial confinement did not constitute a new factor warranting sentence modification. There was no dispute that defendant was the shooter and that he had been to the same house three separate times to shoot it up. The sentences were predicated on consideration of the sentencing factors, including each person's culpability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Walton v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n


Appeal No. 2007AP2853


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 41; 316 Wis. 2d 773; 766 N.W.2d 241; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 114



February 19, 2009, Decided 
February 19, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 15, 2009.
Review dismissed by Walton v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n, 2009 WI 99, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 511 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: SCOTT L. HORNE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV32.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), affirming a decision of respondent Wisconsin Labor and Industry Review Commission, which affirmed a ruling by an administrative law judge pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 102.30(7) (2007-08) that temporary total disability worker's compensation benefits awarded to the employee be paid directly to respondent insurer.


OVERVIEW: The worker's compensation benefits were to be paid directly to the insurer in order to reimburse the insurer for disability benefits it had previously paid to the employee under a nonindustrial insurance policy. The employee argued that the reimbursement was not appropriate because he discharged his obligation to the insurer in bankruptcy. The Commission argued that the insurer had a preexisting subrogation right that survived the bankruptcy and thus, the reimbursement order was proper. On appeal, the court noted that the policy between the employee and the insurer was not made a part of the record. As a result, the court was unable to determine whether the policy created a subrogation interest. Nor could the court determine whether the policy was one of indemnity or one of investment. Absent a showing of a valid subrogation interest, the Commission had no authority to direct a payment otherwise owed to the employee to be made to the insurer under § 102.30(7)(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order.

State v. Bobby G. (In re Marquette S.)


Appeal No. 2008AP1320


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 41; 316 Wis. 2d 774; 766 N.W.2d 242; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 118



February 19, 2009, Decided 
February 19, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Bobby G., 2009 WI 99, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 488 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM S. POCAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004TP285.
State v. Bobby G. (In re Marquette S.), 2007 WI 77, 301 Wis. 2d 531, 734 N.W.2d 81, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 406 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of respondent State and terminated the father's parental rights to his child.


OVERVIEW: The father appealed from an order terminating his parental rights to his child on the grounds that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to raise an objection to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6) (2007-08) as unconstitutional as applied to him. The appellate court affirmed however, and agreed with the State that the father failed to establish a relationship with his child. As a result, he had no fundamental liberty interest in his child that would implicate the protections of due process and equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Further, Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6) was not unconstitutional as applied to the father because terminating his parental rights was rationally related to the goal of the statute, which was the protection and nurturing of children in a stable home. The father's trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to make a meritless argument. The father's actions prevented him from knowing of the mother's pregnancy. His choices of committing crimes, violating rules, skipping court dates, and using drugs made him largely unavailable to see, support, parent or even visit his child. It was not his incarceration alone that prevented his relationship with the child.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Kopsi


Appeal No. 2008AP96-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2009 WI App 41; 316 Wis. 2d 773; 766 N.W.2d 241; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 106



February 18, 2009, Decided 
February 18, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Green Lake County: WILLIAM M. McMONIGAL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF116.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Green Lake County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of two felony counts of failure to pay child support, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.22(2) (2005-06), and denied his postconviction motion for plea withdrawal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction and from an order denying his postconviction motion for plea withdrawal and a new trial. He was convicted of two felony counts of failure to pay child support and contended that the circuit court denied him his constitutionally protected right to counsel, conducted an insufficient plea colloquy, and improperly participated in the plea negotiation by changing the plea to two felonies rather than one felony and one misdemeanor. The appellate court agreed that the circuit court did not engage in the proper inquiry before concluding that defendant had waived his right to counsel; therefore, the appellate court reversed and remanded the matter for further proceedings. It was significant that defendant agreed to waive his right to counsel not in court following a proper colloquy, but rather in a meeting with the prosecutor. None of the protections afforded defendant were available. His waiver of counsel under Wis. Const. art. I, § and U.S. Const. amends. VI and XIV was not knowingly and voluntarily made.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

State ex rel. Myers v. Smith


Appeal No. 2008AP911


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI App 49; 316 Wis. 2d 722; 766 N.W.2d 764; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 109


January 21, 2009, Submitted on Briefs 
February 18, 2009, Decided 
February 18, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: SCOTT C. WOLDT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV1392.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was a practicing Wiccan and ordered a book which was deemed pornographic. He lodged a complaint when the prison refused to give him the book, and an institution complaint examiner recommended dismissal. Respondent warden dismissed the complaint. Ultimately, the Circuit Court for Winnebago County, Wisconsin, concluded it did not have jurisdiction and dismissed the inmate's petition for certiorari review. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate contended the circuit court erred when it made findings after it had determined it had no jurisdiction to hear the petition, and his due process right to discovery was stifled when the State would not produce the file so that he could prepare his arguments. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the inmate misdirected his petition to the warden and, in doing so, deprived the circuit court of jurisdiction. Furthermore, no error occurred when the circuit court concluded that the inmate's litigation was frivolous, but refrained from ordering sanctions under Wis. Stat. § 807.15 (2005-06). Finally, the inmate could not circumvent security policies regarding injurious materials by demanding discovery of a prohibited book.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
