Schmidt v. Froedtert Mem. Lutheran


Appeal No. 2007AP2964


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 41; 316 Wis. 2d 773; 766 N.W.2d 241; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 94



February 12, 2009, Decided 
February 12, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Schmidt v. Froedtert Mem'l Lutheran, 2009 WI 99, 321 Wis. 2d 571, 775 N.W.2d 532, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 376 (2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Schmidt v. Froedtert Mem, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 4364 (U.S., May 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN J. DI MOTTO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV6201.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action, plaintiff, the father of a deceased patient, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, that dismissed his cause of action against defendant health care providers, arguing that the statute limiting medical malpractice liability, Wis. Stat. ch. 655 (2007-08), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Following the patient's demise, his father filed a medical malpractice claim against the health care providers whose negligence allegedly resulted in the wrongful death. The health care providers moved to dismiss; at the hearing on the motion, the trial court dismissed the claim and explained to the father that he had no standing to bring a claim on behalf of his son because he had not been appointed the personal representative of the patient's estate. On review, the court held that, while a patient or a patient's representative had a direct claim for medical malpractice against a health care provider under Wis. Stat. § 655.007 (2007-08), the father was never appointed the personal representative of the patient's estate; therefore, he lacked standing to bring a direct claim on behalf of his son's estate against the health care providers. Further, the father could not bring a derivative claim for loss of his son's society and companionship because, although Wis. Stat. § 655.007 allowed a derivative action to be brought by a parent for the loss of a minor child, it did not allow such a claim to be asserted by the parent of an adult child.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

January 21, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Chippewa County: RODERICK A. CAMERON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007FA291.
Kunsman v. Woodbeck, 2008 WI 122, 314 Wis. 2d 74, 758 N.W.2d 93, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 704 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mother and father, challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Chippewa County, Wisconsin, granting grandparent visitation of their two children with respondents, grandmother and grandfather.


OVERVIEW: Both children were raised in the same household. The mother and father lived together and were the unmarried parents of the youngest child. The mother had a second child with respondent third party, with whom she was never married. Appellants stopped allowing the grandmother to visit the children. The third party stated that he had no objection to allowing the grandparental visitation. The trial court granted the grandmother's petition for visitation. The appellate court ruled that the grandmother had standing under Wis. Stat. § 767.43(3) and (3c) (2005-2006) to bring the petition for visitation. Also, there was no erroneous exercise of discretion by the trial court in ordering appellants to pay any portion of the guardian ad litem (GAL) fee. The mother did not object to paying a portion of the GAL fee prior to or when the circuit court rendered its decision, and thus, failed to preserve the issue, except as to whether the third party should share responsibility for the fee. Furthermore, it was a reasonable exercise of discretion to not order the third party to pay any GAL fees, because he had not objected to the visitation.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

City of Milwaukee v. MK Invs., LLC


Appeal No. 2008AP109


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 27; 316 Wis. 2d 412; 763 N.W.2d 559; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 34



January 21, 2009, Decided 
January 21, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CHRISTOPHER R. FOLEY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV4764.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent city filed a lawsuit against appellants, property owners, seeking to recover the costs associated with razing and removing the owners' building. The owners answered and counterclaimed alleging a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, dismissed the counterclaim and granted the city's motion for summary judgment on the underlying complaint. The owners' appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss the counterclaim, explaining that it was not persuaded by the owners' argument that the exclusive remedies available to it under state statutes and the municipal code were not triggered because of defective service of the raze order. At issue was whether the allegations set forth in the owners' counterclaim were sufficient to state a claim for a deprivation of the owners' constitutional rights or interests under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The appellate court ruled that the owners' counterclaim did not present a cognizable claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, because the counterclaim was devoid of any allegations regarding a municipal policy or custom which resulted in constitutional infringements. The owners' counterclaim was devoid of any reference to either the issue of service of raze orders or the placarding of buildings by the city, upon which its 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim was apparently based, as evidenced by its appellate briefing. The nature and bases of the owners' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim were wholly unclear and insufficient to notify the city of the owner' position, even under Wisconsin's liberal rules of pleading.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Jensen


Appeal No. 2008AP552-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 26; 316 Wis. 2d 377; 762 N.W.2d 833; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 24



January 15, 2009, Decided 
January 15, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Jensen, 2009 WI 99, 319 Wis. 2d 210, 775 N.W.2d 100, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 456 (2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Jensen, 2010 WI 38, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 33 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, III, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CF2453.
State v. Jensen, 2007 WI App 256, 306 Wis. 2d 572, 743 N.W.2d 468, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 973 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction for misconduct in public office was reversed and remanded for a new trial. Based on a newly created venue statute, Wis. Stat. § 971.19(12) (2007-08), defendant moved to transfer his case. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, denied the motion, concluding that § 971.19(12) did not apply to the charges pending against defendant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in concluding that the newly created venue statute, Wis. Stat. § 971.19(12) (2007-08), did not apply to his case. The appellate court disagreed, finding that "the investigation" in § 971.19(12) plainly meant a Government Accountability Board (GAB) authorized investigation. Because defendant was not the subject of a GAB investigation, category two of the statute did not apply. Defendant was charged with misconduct in public office under Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3) (2007-08). While the elections and ethics chapters provided one source of defendant's overall duties as a public officer, and violation of those duties formed the basis for one element of the misconduct in public office charge, the appellate court held that misconduct in public office under § 946.12(3) was not a matter that involved elections, ethics, or lobbying regulation as per Wis. Stat. § 971.19(12) (2007-08). Rather, Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3) (2007-08) was a criminal statute found under an entirely separate chapter. Thus, the plain language of Wis. Stat. § 971.19(12) (2007-08) excluded this case from its coverage.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Rice


Appeal No. 2008AP1335


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 27; 316 Wis. 2d 413; 763 N.W.2d 560; 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 12



January 13, 2009, Decided 
January 13, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Rice, 2009 WI 34, 316 Wis. 2d 720, 765 N.W.2d 580, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 166 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF2966.
State. v. Rice, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1157 (Wis. Ct. App., Mar. 12, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) to the charge of second-degree reckless homicide in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.06(1) (2005-06). Defendant appealed, and the judgment of conviction was affirmed. Defendant then filed a motion for postconviction relief. The circuit court rejected the motion as procedurally barred, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that (2005-06). He argued that this improper amendment violated his constitutional rights in several respects and that his conviction must be set aside as a result. The court held that the motion for post-conviction relief was procedurally barred by defendant's prior no-merit appeal, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06(4) (2005-06). The no-merit appeal had addressed defendant's motion to suppress custodial statements, the validity of the guilty plea, and the circuit court's exercise of sentencing discretion. The no-merit review conducted by appellate counsel and by the court represented a full and conscientious examination of the record. Therefore, resolution of the no-merit proceeding carried a sufficient degree of confidence warranting the application of the procedural bar. Further, defendant admitted shooting the victim and that he acted alone. Therefore, he directly committed the crime, which was one way to be a party to a crime under Wis. Stat. § 939.05 (2005-06).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for post-conviction relief.

State v. Jahnke


Appeal No. 2007AP2130-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 4; 316 Wis. 2d 324; 762 N.W.2d 696; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1048


March 11, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
December 30, 2008, Decided 
December 30, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Jahnke, 2009 WI 34, 316 Wis. 2d 718, 765 N.W.2d 578, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 233 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage County: FREDERIC W. FLEISHAUER, Judge. Affirmed. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF169.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin) convicting him of recording another person in the nude in violation of Wis. Stat. § 942.09(2)(am)1 (2007-08).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for secretly videotaping his girlfriend, without her knowledge, while she was nude. Defendant appealed, arguing that his girlfriend did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy within the meaning of the statute because she knowingly and consensually exposed her nude body to him while he was secretly videotaping her. On appeal, the court disagreed and affirmed. The court held that the phrase "reasonable expectation of privacy" in § 942.09(2)(am)1 meant a reasonable expectation under the circumstances that one would not be recorded in the nude. The court further held that the stipulated facts were sufficient to establish a factual basis for defendant's plea. The parties stipulated that: (1) defendant and his girlfriend had a three-year, sexually intimate relationship; (2) on April 1, 2006, while in her bedroom, the girlfriend knowingly exposed her nude body to defendant; and (3) defendant secretly videotaped her without her consent, using a video camera that was concealed under a pile of clothing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

City of Madison v. Engel


Appeal No. 2008AP1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 21; 316 Wis. 2d 358; 763 N.W.2d 249; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1016



December 23, 2008, Decided 
December 23, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Madison v. Engel, 2009 WI 99, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 361 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: PATRICK J. FIEDLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CV1918.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which found him guilty of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2005-06) (OWI) and driving with a prohibited alcohol concentration in violation of § 346.63(1)(b) (PAC).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for OWI and PAC, but the appellate court affirmed, stating that the officers' conduct in arriving at the scene, knocking on the window, and, when there was no response, opening the truck doors was justified by the community caretaker exception. It was December and the officers were responding to a call in the early morning hours about a person slumped over the steering wheel of a truck in a parking lot, with the headlights and brake lights turned on, more than two hours after the establishment had closed. The public's substantial interest in encouraging officers to act quickly to determine whether there was a need for medical assistance in situations such as the one presented outweighed the limited intrusion into defendant's privacy. Accordingly, the officers were lawfully acting in a community caretaker role when they opened the doors to the truck. Further, from defendant's stumbling and slurred speech, a reasonable officer could have believed that defendant had consumed sufficient alcohol to impair his ability to speak, to concentrate, and to walk steadily.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State ex rel. Heimermann v. McCaughtry


Appeal No. 2007AP2961


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2009 WI App 21; 316 Wis. 2d 355; 763 N.W.2d 247; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1005



December 18, 2008, Decided 
December 18, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Heimermann v. McCaughtry, 2009 WI 34, 316 Wis. 2d 719, 765 N.W.2d 579, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 202 (2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Heimermann v. McCaughtry, 130 S. Ct. 512, 175 L. Ed. 2d 349, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 7747 (U.S., 2009)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Heimermann v. McCaughtry, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 804 (Wis. Ct. App., Oct. 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, III, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CV1499.
State ex rel. Heimermann v. McCaughtry, 2007 WI App 34, 299 Wis. 2d 781, 728 N.W.2d 373, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 49 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his claims against defendant sheriff's department employee and denied his motion for reconsideration in an action for breach of contract and violation of constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of two counts of first-degree intentional homicide as a party to a crime. He brought an action against the employee, asserting claims for breach of contract, a claim under Heck, access to courts, failure to protect, and concerted action. The trial court dismissed the claims. On appeal, the inmate claimed that the employee breached a contract she made with him to get him to help in the investigation of a former prison guard. The court found that the alleged contract was contrary to public policy. Because the employee did not work for the Wisconsin Department of Corrections, she had no authority to affect the terms or conditions of the inmate's confinement. As to the inmate's claim that the employee denied him access to the alleged testimony of a codefendant, the court found that the claim was barred by Heck because the inmate was challenging his conviction and imprisonment. The trial court properly dismissed the claim for failure to protect because the inmate did not allege that the employee participated in the decisions about where he would be confined. Finally, the inmate did not specifically allege in the complaint a cause of action for civil conspiracy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Town of Manitowish Waters v. Malouf


Appeal Nos. 2008AP1839-FT, 2008AP1840-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2009 WI App 21; 316 Wis. 2d 357; 763 N.W.2d 249; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 994



December 16, 2008, Decided 
December 16, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Town of Manitowish Waters v. Malouf, 2009 WI 34, 765 N.W.2d 580, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 154 (2009)
Review denied by Town of Manitowish Waters v. Malouf, 2009 WI 34, 765 N.W.2d 580, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 155 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEALS from judgments of the circuit court for Vilas County: NEAL A. NIELSEN, III, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2006CV226, 2006CV227.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Vilas County (Wisconsin), which held that they violated an ordinance imposed by plaintiff town regulating the number of licensed vehicles stored outdoors at a residence.


OVERVIEW: The town cited the property owners, a mother and son, for exceeding the permissible number of licensed vehicles stored outdoors on each of their properties. The trial court denied the owners' motion challenging the constitutionality of Manitowish Waters, Wis., Ordinance 2-06 (May 18, 2006) on equal protection and due process grounds. The trial court concluded that both owners violated the ordinance. On appeal, the court held that tying the number of permissible licensed vehicles to the number of licensed drivers was perfectly rational. The ordinance included an allowance for one additional vehicle per lot and placed no restrictions on the number of additional vehicles that could be stored indoors. The ordinance was clearly directed at the unusual case where there were excessive vehicles stored outside. The accumulation of vehicles in a residential neighborhood was an aesthetic concern and could reasonably be expected to detract from property values. The vehicle restriction was rationally tied to the number of licensed drivers residing at a property. The owners failed to prove that the ordinance was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Smith


Appeal No. 2008AP1011-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2009 WI App 16; 316 Wis. 2d 165; 762 N.W.2d 856; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 996



December 16, 2008, Decided 
December 16, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Smith, 2009 WI 34, 316 Wis. 2d 717, 765 N.W.2d 578, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 201 (2009)
Affirmed by State v. Smith, 2010 WI 16, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 18 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown County: RICHARD J. DIETZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF1266.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which found that he failed to comply with the reporting requirements of Wis. Stat. § 301.45 (2005-06), Wisconsin's sex offender registry.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction for his failure to comply with the reporting requirements of Wisconsin's sex offender registry, complaining that the registry scheme was unconstitutional as applied to him because the underlying crime of which he was convicted, false imprisonment as party to a crime, lacked a sexual element. The appellate court rejected his challenges and affirmed the judgment. Ultimately, there was a rational basis for the distinctions created by the legislature, the means specified in the statute, and the legislative goals of the statute. It was reasonable to exempt parents convicted of falsely imprisoning their own children from the reporting requirement of Wis. Stat. § 301.45. Because not all defendants convicted of crimes lacking sexual elements posed an inherent danger to children, not all criminal defendants would have been required to register. There was no equal protection or due process violation; § 301.45 was constitutional as applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

688 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


City of Wausau v. Jusufi


Appeal No. 2008AP1107


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2009 WI App 17; 315 Wis. 2d 780; 763 N.W.2d 201; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 942



December 2, 2008, Decided 
December 2, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Wausau v. Jusufi, 2009 WI 23, 764 N.W.2d 533, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 87 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marathon County: GREGORY B. HUBER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CV1244.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin) finding him guilty of two municipal ordinance violations for failing to enforce respondent city's restaurant smoking ban within his restaurant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued the ordinance's differential treatment of restaurants and private clubs violated equal protection. No fundamental interest or suspect class was implicated, so the rational basis standard applied. While the purpose in enacting the ordinance was to protect the public from secondhand smoke in restaurants, it was undisputed that no rationale was articulated for defining private clubs as non-profit clubs only. Whether a rational basis exists for the classification scheme depended on whether the instant court could construct one. The circuit court identified a rational basis for the classifications, and the instant court agreed with the circuit court's reasoning. The ordinance's method of distinguishing private clubs from other restaurants sought to protect the greatest number of restaurant patrons, while preserving the right to associate in truly private clubs that were not open to the public. Absent the ordinance's narrow definition of private clubs as non-profit organizations controlled by their members, ordinary for-profit restaurants seeking the public's patronage would have been able to avoid enforcement of the smoking ban by instituting a few formalities.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lamar Cent. Outdoor, LLC v. Wis. DOT


Appeal No. 2008AP439


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2008 WI App 187; 315 Wis. 2d 190; 762 N.W.2d 745; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 914


September 8, 2008, Submitted on Briefs  
November 20, 2008, Decided 
November 20, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Lamar Cent. Outdoor, LLC v. DOT, 2009 WI 23, 315 Wis. 2d 723, 764 N.W.2d 532, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 129 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Portage County: THOMAS T. FLUGAUR, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CV438.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Portage County, Wisconsin, dismissed appellant sign company's action for compensation for an outdoor advertising sign that was removed by appellee Wisconsin Department of Transportation (DOT) by concluding that the administrative procedure provided in Wis. Stat. § 84.30(18) (2005-06) was the exclusive procedure and the company had not exhausted this procedure. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company argued that the circuit court erred in dismissing its petition because the procedure in Wis. Stat. § 84.30(18) for challenging sign removal orders was not applicable once the sign was removed by DOT. The appellate court found that DOT's removal of the sign to facilitate the highway project did not render moot the issue whether the sign was an illegal nonconforming sign. The need for determining the lawfulness of the removal order remained critical to the question whether the owner was entitled to just compensation. Even after DOT removed the sign, § 84.30(18) provided a procedure for administrative and judicial review of DOT's decision that the sign was illegal and therefore subject to removal without compensation. A sign owner had to challenge the removal order in a hearing before the Division of Hearing and Appeals followed by judicial review under Wis. Stat. ch. 227, and only if the owner prevailed on the issue of the sign's illegality could the owner seek just compensation. If the company did not prevail in its challenge to the removal order, it was not entitled to just compensation. Equitable considerations did not warrant an exception to the exhaustion doctrine.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Peck


Appeal No. 2007AP2732-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2009 WI App 1; 315 Wis. 2d 769; 762 N.W.2d 864; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 900



November 19, 2008, Decided 
November 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Ozaukee County: THOMAS R. WOLFGRAM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF15.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County, Wisconsin, that convicted him of three counts of identity theft involving the identity of his ex-wife under Wis. Stat. § 943.201(2)(c) (2005-06), arguing that the word "harm"; as it appears in the statute is unconstitutionally vague and that the State failed to prove that he intended to harm his ex-wife's reputation, property, person, or estate.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's ex-wife began to receive unsolicited books and magazines and discovered that she was subscribed to an adult-themed matchmaking site through her personal e-mail account. Because the subscriptions coincided with vandalism to her yard, the ex-wife contacted the police. The police obtained copies of the subscription cards, one of which bore a forged signature, and the ex-wife identified defendant's handwriting. When questioned, defendant acknowledged his actions and indicated that he wanted to make his ex-wife miserable. Defendant was charged with identity theft for intentionally using his ex-wife's personal identifying information without her consent for the purpose of harming her reputation, property, person, or estate. On review, the court agreed with the trial court's determination that the jury permissibly gave the word "harm"; its ordinary meaning and that the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction. Although the legislature did not define "harm" the term was non-technical and thus could be given its common usage. Further, the jury could infer defendant's intent to harm his ex-wife from the evidence, and there was no requirement that actual harm be shown.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Ozaukee County v. Labor Ass'n of Wis.


Appeal No. 2007AP1615


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI App 174; 315 Wis. 2d 102; 763 N.W.2d 140; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 906


June 3, 2008, Argued 
November 19, 2008, Decided 
November 19, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Ozaukee County: PATRICK J. FARAGHER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV350.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Labor Association of Wisconsin (LAW), challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County (Wisconsin), which awarded summary judgment to plaintiffs, a county and a sheriff, in a suit for a declaration of the sheriff's constitutional authority with respect to the Wisconsin Court Services Unit (CSU) and assigning Unit members to transport federal and state prisoners without regard to a collective bargaining agreement (CBA).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action requesting that the trial court declare the sheriff's constitutional authority with respect to the CSU and assigning Unit members to transport federal and state prisoners without regard to a CBA. Plaintiffs filed a motion for summary judgment. The trial court granted the motion and recognized the sheriff's constitutional authority to appoint CSU deputies to transport state and federal prisoners who were being housed in the county under a rental contract for prisoner bed space. On appeal, the court found that because the trial court had to determine whether the sheriff was acting in a constitutionally protected manner, it did not abuse its discretion by retaining jurisdiction over the action. However, the assignment of deputies to transport federal and state prisoners to and from the county jail pursuant to a contract for the rental of bed space was not a constitutionally protected duty of the sheriff's office and was thus, subject to the restrictions of the CBA. The money-generating actions did not hold up as certain immemorial, principal, and important duties of the sheriff at common law that were peculiar to the office of sheriff.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's retention of jurisdiction over the action. The court reversed the trial court's award of summary judgment to plaintiffs.

State v. Brown


Appeal No. 2007AP2879-CR, 2008AP268-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2009 WI App 1; 315 Wis. 2d 770; 762 N.W.2d 864; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 896



November 18, 2008, Decided 
November 18, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Brown, 2009 WI 34, 765 N.W.2d 579, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 240 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM W. BRASH and JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF302.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) of being a felon in possession of a firearm and possession of a short-barreled shotgun. Defendant also pleaded guilty to fleeing an officer. After his motion for postconviction relief was denied, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erroneously denied his request for a new attorney. The court of appeals disagreed. The request was made on the scheduled date of the trial. The trial court called defendant's concern "very suspect," but did not make detailed findings about the timing of the request. Rather, the trial court focused on whether the alleged conflict was so great that it likely resulted in a total lack of communication that prevented an adequate defense and frustrated a fair presentation of the case. The trial court concluded that there was not such a total lack of communication. It noted that there had been no indication of new evidence that would require trial counsel to seek an adjournment or further time to follow up on information. At the time the trial court decided defendant's implicit motion, there were no indications that any facts needed investigating or that defendant and his counsel needed more time to prepare a defense. Thus, while trial counsel accepted fault for not returning defendant's phone calls, he indicated that he was still prepared to proceed, even if he was not optimistic about the strength of defendant's case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Oliver

October 1, 2008, Decided 
October 1, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Oliver, 2009 WI 5, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 1072 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine County: EMILY S. MUELLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF700.



DISPOSITION:  [*184] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) found defendant guilty of first-degree recklessly endangering safety while armed, as party to a crime, and as a repeater, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 941.30(1), 939.50(3)(f), 939.05 and 939.63(1) (2005-06). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The jury heard testimony that defendant drove his companions to a specific area looking for rival gang members to avenge the shooting of his companions' fellow gang member; that upon seeing several people on a nearby street corner, the principal, seated directly behind defendant, slid open the van door and fired seven shots from a big gun; that the area was residential; that the principal himself was shot in the face and leg; and that defendant admitted lying to the police earlier when he thought it would serve his interest. The court held that the jury reasonably concluded that shooting seven times at people on the street from a moving van in a residential neighborhood created a substantial risk of bodily harm, even if those people also engaged in similar conduct. Although the party to a crime instruction did not state that the jury needed to be satisfied beyond a reasonable doubt of the principal's guilt before it could find defendant guilty of aiding and abetting him, defendant's counsel affirmatively stated that he had no objections to the instruction, thereby waiving his objection under Wis. Stat. § 805.13(3) (2005-06). There was no structural error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Fischer


Appeal No. 2007AP1898-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI App 152; 314 Wis. 2d 324; 761 N.W.2d 7; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 717


May 16, 2008, Submitted on Briefs  
September 10, 2008, Decided 
September 10, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: October 27, 2008, Released for Publication
Review granted by State v. Fischer, 2009 WI 23, 315 Wis. 2d 721, 764 N.W.2d 531, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 41 (2009)
Affirmed by State v. Fischer, 2010 WI 6, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 5 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Ozaukee County: THOMAS R. WOLFGRAM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CM123.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County, Wisconsin, found defendant guilty of operating while intoxicated (OWI). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought to admit the testimony of an expert to tell the jury that he compared defendant's blood test result with defendant's preliminary breath test (PBT) result and, by doing so, could extrapolate a probable blood alcohol concentration at the time defendant was last seen operating his vehicle, about 30 minutes before the PBT was administered. The reviewing court held that the PBT testimony was properly excluded, as required by Wis. Stat. § 343.303 (2005-06). Although the expert's analysis was relevant and necessary for the defense, the State's interest in not allowing PBT evidence in OWI trials was legitimate and overrode defendant's interest in presenting the expert testimony. The testing mechanism for the PBT was simply not designed so the result obtained during the investigation of a possibly intoxicated driver was accurate enough to help a jury determine the driver's guilt or innocence. The legislature did not want the PBT admitted as evidence for that reason. If the underlying basis for an opinion was a result that could not be tested for accuracy at the time of the test, then it could not assist the trier of fact and had no probative value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling excluding the evidence.

State v. Trattner

September 3, 2008, Decided 
September 3, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Trattner, 2009 WI 5, 315 Wis. 2d 56, 759 N.W.2d 771, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 1085 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Ozaukee County: THOMAS R. WOLFGRAM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF27.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County, Wisconsin, that convicted him of first-degree reckless homicide in violation of WIS. STAT. § 940.02(1) (2005-06) and an order denying his postconviction motion for resentencing, arguing that the circuit court relied upon inaccurate information at sentencing in relying upon his statements about feeling threatened by his wife.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's wife told defendant that she wanted a divorce, defendant beat and strangled her to death. In statements to police and the presentence investigation report writer, defendant indicated that he felt threatened by his wife and feared for his safety when he attacked her. The circuit court sentenced defendant to 35 years in prison and 10 years of extended supervision. Defendant challenged his sentence, contending that the circuit court relied upon inaccurate information when, at sentencing, it relied upon his statements about feeling threatened by his wife to conclude that he lacked remorse and failed to accept responsibility for his actions. On review, the court held that the circuit court was aware of defendant's claim, supported by a psychiatric expert, that defendant's meritless assertion of self-defense was not the result of a conscious effort to shift blame but was instead part of a personality structure over which defendant had no control. The circuit court's refusal to accept the expert's opinion regarding the motivation for defendant's conduct did not mean that it relied upon inaccurate information regarding defendant's psychological makeup.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief were affirmed.

State v. Sileno


Appeal No. 2007AP2955-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2008 WI App 160; 314 Wis. 2d 508; 758 N.W.2d 225; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 693



September 3, 2008, Decided 
September 3, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Sileno, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 1156 (Wis., Nov. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2006CF2261, 2007CF1403.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a bench trial, the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, found defendant guilty of possession of a machine gun, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.26(1)(a) (2005-06). Defendant appealed from the conviction and the order denying his postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 941.26(1)(a). In affirming, the court held that counsel was not rendered ineffective by failing to notify the Attorney General that he was challenging the constitutionality of the statute because there was no prejudice, given that the trial court addressed the merits of the argument. The court also held that § 941.26(1)(a) was not rendered unconstitutional by the absence of a mens rea requirement and was not void for vagueness. Read with the definitional statute, it clearly provided that one could not possess or transport a machine gun or fully automatic firearm; one could not possess or transport a weapon that either shot, was designed to shoot, or could be readily restored to shoot more than one shot with a single pull of the trigger; one could not possess any part or combination of parts designed and intended for use in converting a weapon into a machine gun or fully-automatic weapon. Thus, defendant should have had reason to believe that he was in violation of these statutes when, as he conceded, he purchased the parts required to convert a rifle into a machine gun and attached all but one of the parts to make that happen.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Peterson


Appeal No. 2007AP1867-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI App 140; 314 Wis. 2d 192; 757 N.W.2d 834; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 656


June 26, 2008, Submitted on Briefs  
August 20, 2008, Decided 
August 20, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Peterson, 2009 WI App 128, 773 N.W.2d 227, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 473 (Wis. Ct. App., July 1, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order 1 of the circuit court for Winnebago County: THOMAS J. GRITTON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF194.


1 While the appellant appeals from both a judgment and an order, we address only the order for the reasons set forth in the opinion.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of the sexual assault of a child and removed his privately retained postconviction counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order arising from his criminal conviction for the sexual assault of a child and argued in part that his privately retained postconviction counsel was improperly removed over his objection. The appellate court agreed, reversing the judgment and remanding for further proceedings. Counsel was improperly disqualified. The circuit court's comments did not convince the appellate court that it balanced defendant's right to be represented by his retained counsel against the circuit court's interest in the appearance of fairness and diffusing what it characterized as a potential conflict. The record contained little reference to defendant's interests, which should have been clearly addressed. The appellate court did not reach the merits of defendant's appeal from the judgment of conviction because that portion of his appeal largely relied on claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The ineffective assistance claims were to be the subject of the proceedings on remand; thus, current review would have been premature.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the postconviction order and remanded for further proceedings.

 

698 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Yourchuck Video, Inc. v. Burnett County


Appeal No. 2007AP2093


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2008 WI App 148; 314 Wis. 2d 260; 757 N.W.2d 850; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 651



August 19, 2008, Decided 
August 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Burnett County: ROBERT RASMUSSEN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV6.
Yourchuck Video, Inc. v. Burnett County, 2005 WI App 193, 287 Wis. 2d 133, 703 N.W.2d 383, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 588 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owner filed suit against defendant county in the Circuit Court for Burnett County (Wisconsin), challenging the constitutionality of a sign ordinance and seeking money damages. After an appellate determination that the ordinance was unconstitutional, a jury found in favor of the owner and awarded $ 200,000 in damages. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner wanted to place a sign outside his business that exceeded the size requirements in a county ordinance. The county rejected his application; there was no procedure for review or for a variance, leading to the owner's suit. The suit eventually alleged a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court rejected the county's contention that the owner was required to exhaust state remedies or follow claim procedures outlined in Wis. Stat. § 893.80. Contrary to the county's position, the § 1983 claim was that the county violated due process rights by subjecting the owner to an unconstitutional ordinance. Because the claim was one for a due process violation contrary to the United States Constitution, not a taking contrary to Wis. Const. art. I, § 13, a notice of claim under § 893.80(1) was not required, the § 893.80(3) damages cap did not apply, and § 893.80(4) immunity was not a bar. In this case, lost profits were a rational, reasonable measure of damages: without a variance or other review procedure, the owner was bound by the ordinance's size restriction. It was not unreasonable to conclude that this lack of due process deprived the owner of profits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Wakeman


Appeal No. 2007AP1955-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2008 WI App 148; 314 Wis. 2d 260; 757 N.W.2d 850; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 626



August 12, 2008, Decided 
August 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Wakeman, 2008 WI 124, 758 N.W.2d 927, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 1060 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Forest County: ROBERT A. KENNEDY, JR., Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF15.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Forest County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of one count of first-degree intentional homicide.


OVERVIEW: Following a night of drinking, defendant and others ended up at the victim's home. The victim allegedly attempted to sexually molest defendant. A fight erupted and defendant was physically assaulted by the victim and others. Defendant was able to flee to her home. At her home, defendant retrieved two knives. Defendant and her grandson returned to the victim's house. Defendant fatally stabbed the victim. She was convicted of first-degree intentional homicide. On appeal, the court found that it was within the jury's province under Wis. Stat. § 971.15(3) (2005-06) to conclude that, although defendant might have suffered from a mental disease or defect, the illness was not a factor in the homicide. It was evident that the jury rejected the experts' opinions in favor of defendant's own explanation for her behavior: she was angry and drunk. Further, a jury instruction on the duty to retreat was proper as there was evidence that defendant could and did retreat to the safety of her own home before choosing to return to the victim's house. Finally, there was no evidence of systemic exclusion, or intentionally disproportionate inclusion, of Native Americans in the jury selection process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Popke


Appeal No. 2008AP446-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2008 WI App 148; 314 Wis. 2d 261; 757 N.W.2d 851; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 616



August 7, 2008, Decided 
August 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Popke, 2009 WI 5, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 1142 (2008)
Reversed by State v. Popke, 2009 WI 37, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 28 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waupaca County: RAYMOND S. HUBER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CT230.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waupaca County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant as a third offense contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1)(a) and 346.65(2)(g)3 (2005-06). Defendant also sought review an order denying his motion to suppress arguing his rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11 were violated by an improper stop.


OVERVIEW: A police officer saw three-quarters of defendant's vehicle go left of the center of the road right after a left turn. Defendant's vehicle then moved quickly to the right side of the road where it almost hit the curb. Moments later, the vehicle faded back toward the center of the road and almost hit a median at the center of the road near an intersection. The officer then initiated a traffic stop of the vehicle and subsequently arrested defendant for operating while intoxicated. Defendant argued that the officer had neither probable cause to pull him over for violating Wis. Stat. § 346.05 nor reasonable suspicion under the totality of the circumstances to initiate a stop for some other traffic or criminal violation. The court agreed with both of defendant's assertions. Section 346.05 merely established that motorists had to travel on the right side of the road; momentarily crossing the center of the road and quickly shifting back was not a violation. In addition, the State did not show specific and articulable facts which, taken together with rational inferences from those facts, reasonably warranted the intrusion of the stop under the totality of the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order to suppress and the judgment of conviction.

State v. Dearborn


Appeal No. 2007AP1894-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI App 131; 313 Wis. 2d 767; 758 N.W.2d 463; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 570


January 2, 2008, Submitted on Briefs  
July 24, 2008, Decided 
July 24, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Dearborn, 2010 WI 5, 322 Wis. 2d 122, 779 N.W.2d 176, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 890 (2009)
Affirmed by State v. Dearborn, 2010 WI 84, 327 Wis. 2d 252, 786 N.W.2d 97, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 110 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Grant County: GEORGE S. CURRY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CM116.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin) for assaulting or otherwise obstructing or resisting a conservation warden contrary to Wis. Stat. § 29.951 (2005-06), and for possession of tetrahydrocannabinols (THC) contrary to Wis. Stat. § 961.41(3g)(e) (2005-06). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: While driving, defendant made a rude gesture to a park warden. The warden learned that defendant's driver's license had been revoked. He stopped defendant, who got out of his truck and locked it, then refused to comply with the warden's commands. They tussled, and defendant ran away, picked up rocks, and positioned himself to throw them at the warden. The warden called for backup, and eventually defendant was subdued. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on Wis. Stat. § 29.951 because the instruction allowed less than a unanimous jury verdict in violation of his right to a jury trial under Wis. Const. art. I, §§ 5 and 7. Section 29.951 forbade obstructing or resisting a warden in the conduct of his duty; defendant argued that some jurors could find that he resisted and others that he obstructed, and he could have been convicted on less than a unanimous verdict. The court held that § 29.951 defined only one crime with multiple modes of commission; the statute comported with the fundamental fairness standard embodied in the due process clause. The jury did not need to be unanimous on the mode of commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. King


Appeal No. 2007AP1420-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI App 129; 313 Wis. 2d 673; 758 N.W.2d 131; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 557


April 1, 2008, Submitted on Briefs  
July 22, 2008, Decided 
July 22, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 25, 2008.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. King, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 918 (Wis. Ct. App., Dec. 1, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOSEPH R. WALL, Judge. 1 .Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF2729.


1 The Honorable Charles F. Kahn denied Michael Anthony King's motion to suppress. The Honorable Joseph R. Wall presided over the trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, that convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver and possession of tetrahydrocannabinols in violation of Wis. Stat. 961.41(lm)(cm)2, 961.41(3g)(e), and 961.48 (2001-02), arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress physical evidence seized during the execution of an invalid anticipatory search warrant.


OVERVIEW: A detective applied for a warrant related to a three-unit townhouse. The application requested an anticipatory search warrant, as the unit in which defendant resided had not yet been verified. The warrant issued but stated that authorization to search was contingent upon the ability of the police to identify the precise unit in which defendant resided. The police subsequently searched one of the units and found drugs. Defendant was charged with and convicted of drug offenses. On review, the court held that anticipatory warrants were peculiar to property in transit and were based upon an affidavit showing probable cause that, at some future time, certain evidence of a crime would be located at a specific place. The court declined to extend the use of anticipatory warrants to encompass a situation where execution was conditioned upon verification of an individual's address. Further, the warrant was invalid for lack of particularity under the Fourth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11. Language in the search warrant referencing three separate residences failed to comply with the constitutional requirement that the warrant state with particularity the site to be searched.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

703 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Otis G. (In re Davonta S.)


Appeal No. 2008AP196


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2008 WI App 135; 313 Wis. 2d 833; 756 N.W.2d 811; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 543



July 15, 2008, Decided 
July 15, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Otis G., 2008 WI 124, 758 N.W.2d 927, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 1029 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM S. POCAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007TP222.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State filed a petition to terminate respondent father's rights to his child in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(9) (2005-06), on the grounds of parenthood as a result of sexual assault. The State's motion for partial summary judgment was granted, and the trial court made a finding of unfitness in accordance with Wis. Stat. § 48.424(4) (2005-06). The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the age of 15, the father had sex with the mother, then aged 13, resulting in the child's birth. These facts allowed the trial court to terminate the father's rights under Wis. Stat. § 48.415 (2005-06). The court held that the statute was narrowly tailored to cover a specific type of parent, here a parent under the age of 16. It did not reach parents who had conceived children out of wedlock or those who conceived children with financially poor persons. The statute advanced the State's compelling interest of reducing the number of children born to and raised by persons under 16, thereby reducing the costs to Wisconsin residents of raising these children. Additionally, § 48.415(9) did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and its corollary in Wis. Const. art. 1, § 1, because it was not facially discriminatory. Nor did a finding of unfitness based on conduct in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2) (2005-06) constitute cruel and unusual punishment prohibited by U.S. Const. amend. VIII or Wis. Const. art. 1, § 6. A finding of unfitness simply moved the process to another stage. It did not terminate any of a parent's rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Orville

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE

July 1, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Orville, 2008 WI 124, 758 N.W.2d 926, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 918 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DENNIS P. MORONEY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF6819.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to substitute an attorney as counsel or, in the alternative, for the judge to recuse himself from defendant's case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from an order denying his motion to substitute an attorney as counsel or, in the alternative, for the judge to have recused himself from defendant's case. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the attorney was aware of the standing order that the trial court would recuse itself from any case in which the attorney was counsel of record. The attorney was aware, with his filing of the notice of retainer with the trial court if not before, that defendant's case was before the trial court. The trial court's finding that the motion to substitute as counsel that required the trial court to recuse itself, in light of the attorney's knowledge of its standing order and the recent adverse ruling on the motion to suppress, created the suspicious timing that provided for an inference of intent of an improper purpose for the substitution, was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Jones


Appeal No. 2007AP1621


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2008 WI App 121; 313 Wis. 2d 522; 756 N.W.2d 478; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 487



June 24, 2008, Decided 
June 24, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Jones, 2008 WI 124, 758 N.W.2d 926, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 913 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM W. BRASH, III, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CF6368.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of his Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2005-06) postconviction motion by the Milwaukee County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), arguing that both his trial and appellate counsel were ineffective, that the charges against him were unconstitutionally multiplicitous, and that he was entitled to have his sentences run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was certainly aware of any claim that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to advise him of the consequences of his plea, and he could have easily raised the issue in a response to his counsel's no-merit report. Even if the claim were raised, however, the argument would have been unsuccessful because defendant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily entered his plea. Similarly, his claim of unconstitutional multiplicity of the charges was barred because it could have been raised in his response to the no-merit report, but was not. Even so, the claim was meritless on its face because each of the car-theft charges arose out of separate incidents that occurred on different dates and involved different cars. The misdemeanor to which he pled guilty involved the theft of a purse, which occurred on the same date as one of the car thefts, but involved a different victim. Each charge required proof of facts that the others did not; the charges were different in fact and in law, and were therefore not multiplicitous. Because defendant's arguments were meritless, he could not establish either deficient performance by appellate counsel for failure to raise them, or prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Milwaukee Journal Sentinel v. Wis. Dep't of Admin.


Appeal No. 2007AP1160


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 461



June 17, 2008, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER EDITING. IF PUBLISHED, THE OFFICIAL VERSION WILL APPEAR IN THE BOUND VOLUME OF THE OFFICIAL REPORTS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition granted by Milwaukee Journal Sentinel v. Dep't of Admin., 2008 WI 124, 314 Wis. 2d 284, 758 N.W.2d 928, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 1022 (2008)
Certified question answered by, Cause remanded by Milwaukee Journal Sentinel v. Wis. Dep't of Admin., 2009 WI 79, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 288 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV3569, 2005CV3923.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state agencies and a union, sought review of an order from a trial court (Wisconsin), which awarded summary judgment to respondent newspapers in the newspapers' action to compel compliance with the open records law, Wis. Stat. § 19.35 (2005-06).


OVERVIEW: The newspapers sought information regarding certain state employees under the open records law, Wis. Stat. § 19.35. The state agencies provided the requested documents, but redacted the names of specific employees pursuant to a collective bargaining agreement. The newspapers brought an action to compel compliance with the open records law. The union intervened to protect the provisions of the contract. The trial court awarded summary judgment to the newspapers. On appeal, the court determined that it was appropriate for the Wisconsin Supreme Court to decide whether courts had jurisdiction to review legislative compliance with Wis. Stat. § 111.92. The issue was fundamental to the relationship between the judicial branch and the other branches of government. The Supreme Court should determine whether courts had jurisdiction to review the legislature's compliance with § 111.92 because it implicated Wis. Const. art. IV, § 17 or whether, under Wis. Const. art. IV, § 8, courts were prohibited from reviewing compliance with § 111.92 under the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court certified the appeal to the Wisconsin Supreme Court to determine whether courts had jurisdiction to review the process the legislature used to amend the open records law by ratifying a collective bargaining agreement and, if so, whether the process used was effective to bring about a change in the law.

State v. Greene


Appeal No. 2007AP269-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR

June 12, 2008, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: C. WILLIAM FOUST, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CF390.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged an amended order of restitution by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) directing the Department of Corrections (DOC) to distribute 10 percent of his prison wages, earnings and accounts to pay restitution.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of first-degree intentional homicide, burglary while armed with a dangerous weapon, and armed robbery with threat of force. The inmate and two co-defendants were held jointly liable for restitution. The inmate argued the circuit court lacked the authority to direct DOC to access accounts holding gifted funds from friends and family to pay restitution. The inmate also argued that the amended restitution order violated his double jeopardy protections, and that the order wrongfully increased his sentence in the absence of a new sentencing factor. The appellate court concluded that under Wis. Stat. § 973.20 (2005-06) the circuit court properly ordered the inmate to pay restitution from funds held in his prison account, which presumably included gifted funds. The order also did not violate the inmate's double jeopardy guarantees or wrongfully increase his sentence.

State v. Baron


Appeal No. 2007AP1289-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI App 90; 312 Wis. 2d 789; 754 N.W.2d 175; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 410


December 7, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
May 29, 2008, Decided 
May 29, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Baron, 2008 WI 122, 314 Wis. 2d 69, 758 N.W.2d 90, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 701 (2008)
Affirmed by State v. Baron, 2009 WI 58, 318 Wis. 2d 60, 769 N.W.2d 34, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 268 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Jefferson County: RANDY R. KOSCHNICK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF496.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with six counts, including identity theft in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.201(2)(c) (2005-2006). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the identity theft charge on the ground that the identity theft statute was unconstitutional as applied to his conduct. The Circuit Court for Jefferson County, Wisconsin, granted the motion. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a city employee and hacked into his supervisor's work computer and sent e-mails purporting to have come from the supervisor. The content of the e-mails consisted primarily of sexual innuendoes between the supervisor and a female employee, as well as attempts to set up meetings to engage in the affair. Defendant sent the e-mails to various local and county workers, as well as to the supervisor's wife. The circuit court reasoned that because the person whose identity defendant misappropriated was a public official, application of the identity theft statute violated defendant's First Amendment right to defame a public official with true information. The appellate court ruled that the identity theft statute did not criminalize the act of defaming a public official, and therefore did not violate defendant's First Amendment rights. The identity theft statute neither prohibited defendant from disseminating information about the supervisor nor prevented the public from receiving that information. Instead, the statute prohibited defendant from purporting to be the supervisor when he sent the e-mails.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed.

State v. Ciarpaglini


Appeal No. 2006AP1187-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2008 WI App 99; 312 Wis. 2d 811; 754 N.W.2d 254; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 347



May 7, 2008, Decided 
May 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: RICHARD J. KREUL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CF722.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of one count of false swearing in, sentence was withheld, and he was placed on five years of probation. The Circuit Court for Racine County, Wisconsin, subsequently entered an order striking a rule of probation on the ground that it was overly broad and vague, and unconstitutionally barred defendant's constitutional rights to free speech and association, or to engage in interstate commerce. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State contended the trial court lacked statutory authority to decide defendant's motion to modify and strike the probation rule in question after the Division of Hearings and Appeals revoked his probation. The appellate court agreed, finding that defendant's challenge to the probation rule was moot after his probation was revoked. Further, the probation violations unrelated to the probation rule at issue were sufficient, in and of themselves, to justify the revocation. Whether defendant had shown grounds for striking the probation rule when his motion was addressed by the trial court therefore could have no effect on his revocation, and this case was moot. Further, defendant's motion did not present an issue of great public importance, or one which was likely to arise again or so frequently as to necessitate a definitive decision to guide trial courts. It also involved no challenge to the constitutionality of a statute. Thus, defendant's motion challenging the probation rule should have been dismissed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

State v. Alexander


Appeal No. 2007AP1270-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2008 WI App 99; 312 Wis. 2d 812; 754 N.W.2d 254; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 333



May 1, 2008, Decided 
May 1, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Alexander, 2008 WI 124, 314 Wis. 2d 281, 758 N.W.2d 926, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 974 (2008)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Alexander v. Grams, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 42547 (W.D. Wis., Apr. 29, 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Alexander, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 324 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 11, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: MICHAEL J. MULROY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CF352.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for La Crosse County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of first-degree intentional homicide, Wis. Stat. §§ 939.62(1) and 940.01(1) (2001-02), attempted first-degree intentional homicide, Wis. Stat. §§ 939.32, 939.62(1) (2001-02), and two counts of recklessly endangering safety, Wis. Stat. §§ 939.62(1), 939.63(1), and 941.30(1) (2001-02), all while armed as a repeat offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel on seven different grounds and he asserted four claims of circuit court error. Defendant moved the court to admit tape recorded statements of two witnesses to the shooting, who were unavailable. The appellate court found that counsel's conclusion that the better course was to have the jury hear both statements rather than neither statement, where one was helpful, was the type of strategic choice courts did not second guess. Defense counsel was not deficient for failure to object to the officer's gesture he made while testifying that it was made by a witness on confrontation-clause grounds, and counsel was not deficient for failing to object to the gesture on hearsay grounds. The prosecutor's cross-examination of defendant was proper. The outcome would not have different had the jury not heard that defendant was incarcerated for thirty months. The nature of the right to confrontation did not require a personal waiver by means of a colloquy. The circuit court did not err in denying defendant's motion to question a witness regarding his criminal history and past incidents of aiding the prosecution with information.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Mack S. (In re Mack S.)


Appeal No. 2006AP2393


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2008 WI App 83; 312 Wis. 2d 479; 751 N.W.2d 902; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 275



April 8, 2008, Decided 
April 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Mack S., 2008 WI 122, 758 N.W.2d 90, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 634 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DAVID L. BOROWSKI and FRANCIS T. WASIELEWSKI, Judges. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2002JV1619A, 2002JV1619B.
State v. Mack S. (In re Mack S.), 2005 WI App 88, 281 Wis. 2d 274, 695 N.W.2d 905, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 182 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, entered dispositional orders after finding appellant, a juvenile, delinquent based on misdemeanor battery in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.19(1) (2001-02) and felony battery to an individual over the age of 62, as a party to a crime, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.19(6)(a) and § 939.05 (2001-02). Appellant challenged the orders.


OVERVIEW: Two incidents took place when appellant was 13 years old. The first incident occurred when appellant allegedly punched a bus patron in the mouth. The second incident occurred when appellant, his brother, and another youth battered a 74-year-old man. Among the issues presented on appeal were the following: (1) whether the appellant's statements should have been suppressed pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 938.23(1m)(a) (2001-02, eff. May 25, 2002); (2) whether the trial court violated the appellant's right to counsel pursuant to the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments; and (3) whether Wis. Stat. § 940.19(6)(a) (2005-06) was constitutional. The appellate court concluded that § 938.23(1m)(a) did not apply because appellant was not interrogated in a secure detention facility after a delinquency petition had been filed. Further, the trial court did not err in granting counsel's request to withdraw, and counsel did not provide ineffective assistance. Appellant failed to rebut the presumption that because his victim was over 62 years old, the battery had a substantial risk of great bodily harm. In one final issue, the appellate court determined that appellant could not be represented by a paralegal.


OUTCOME: The trial court's orders were affirmed.

NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed pro se from the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) an order denying his motion to vacate a conviction and dismiss the underlying complaint in municipal court regarding a parking citation he received for parking in a city lot without a permit. He argued that the requirement of a parking permit was unconstitutional as it createsd an obstacle to a person's constitutional right to access and enjoy public waters.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.
