State v. Gruenberg


Appeal No. 2007AP381


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2008 WI App 64; 311 Wis. 2d 489; 750 N.W.2d 518; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 244



March 27, 2008, Decided 
March 27, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Gruenberg, 2008 WI 122, 758 N.W.2d 91, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 705 (2008)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Gruenberg v. Pollard, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 85944 (W.D. Wis., Oct. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Green County: JAMES R. BEER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1998CF137.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate entered no contest pleas in the Circuit Court for Green County (Wisconsin) to three counts of burglary as a repeat offender, in exchange for the dismissal of several other counts. Several years later, the inmate filed a Wis. Stat. § 974.06 motion seeking to set aside his convictions on multiple grounds. The trial court vacated one count but denied the inmate's other claims for relief and reconsideration. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate first argued that he was improperly denied counsel on his postconviction motion. However, there was no right to counsel for a postconviction motion brought under Wis. Stat. § 974.06, after the right to a direct appeal had expired. The inmate also argued that he was never advised of his Miranda rights, rendering his arrest unlawful, and that the search of his apartment was unlawful due to a defective warrant. The court found that the inmate waived the right to challenge these nonjurisdictional defects, which were suppression issues, by entering his guilty pleas. The inmate argued that two of the burglary counts were unsupported by a factual basis. These contentions were not waived by the pleas, but there was adequate factual support for the counts: the record contained the allegation of the burglary, an affidavit stating that a credit card which had been reported stolen had been recovered on the inmate's person, and evidence that the inmate had blue fingers from detection powder which linked him to a related robbery right around the corner. It was not necessary for the facts to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he had committed the second burglary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision vacating one count and denying further relief.

State v. Carrothers


Appeal No. 2007AP1826-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2008 WI App 64; 311 Wis. 2d 490; 750 N.W.2d 519; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 241



March 26, 2008, Decided 
March 26, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Carrothers, 2008 WI 115, 310 Wis. 2d 709, 754 N.W.2d 851, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 585 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: RALPH M. RAMIREZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007CT157.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, fourth offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that from the moment the officer stopped her car, she was not free to leave; therefore, any evidence gathered during that time was inadmissible because she had not been advised of her Miranda rights. The court of appeals disagreed. At the time that defendant made her statement about consuming two beers, she was the subject of an investigatory stop. A reasonable person would understand that he or she was temporarily detained. Defendant was still in her own vehicle and was about to hand over her driver's license for identification when she made the statement. Only one officer was present, no gun was drawn, no frisk was performed, and the length of the detention at that point was quite brief. None of the trappings of a formal arrest were present at that time. Therefore, a reasonable person in defendant's position would not have considered herself to be in custody, given the degree of restraint under the circumstances. In addition, the officer properly prolonged the initial stop because during the initial contact with defendant, he noticed the strong smell of alcohol, glassy eyes, and slurred speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Baker v. State


Appeal No. 2007AP573


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2008 WI App 64; 311 Wis. 2d 489; 750 N.W.2d 518; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 210



March 18, 2008, Decided 
March 18, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Baker v. State, 2008 WI 122, 758 N.W.2d 91, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 642 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Baker v. Wis., 129 S. Ct. 1334, 173 L. Ed. 2d 605, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 1550 (U.S., Feb. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CLARE L. FIORENZA, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CV7883.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmates, who had been convicted of various offenses as parties to the crime, filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration on the validity, under the U.S. and Wisconsin Constitutions, of Wis. Stat. § 939.05 (2005-06). The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) dismissed the action, and the inmates appealed.


OVERVIEW: Among the appellate court's holdings with respect to the constitutionality of the party to the crime statute, Wis. Stat. § 939.05 (2005-06), were: (1) § 939.05 did not violate the double jeopardy preclusion because being convicted of a substantive crime as a party to the crime did not subject a defendant to multiple punishments, as being a party to the crime was not itself a substantive crime; (2) for purposes of due process and effective assistance of counsel, the party-to-a-crime charge sufficiently notified defendants of the criminal conduct for which they were being charged and were compelled to defend against; (3) insofar as the inmates' equal protection claim was incident to the due process of law and effective assistance of counsel claims, it was rejected for the same reasons that those claims were rejected; and (4) insofar as the equal protection claim was something else, it was rejected for failure to develop it in a comprehensible fashion.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO

March 12, 2008, Decided 
March 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Adrian S., 2008 WI 115, 310 Wis. 2d 709, 754 N.W.2d 852, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 621 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: FAYE M. FLANCHER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2007JV70.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying juvenile defendant's motion to suppress evidence of marijuana found on his person during a weapons pat-down, the Circuit Court for Racine County, Wisconsin, adjudicated him delinquent on the charge of possession with intent to deliver tetrahydrocannabinol (THC). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress as the officer's protective search for weapons was a violation of the constitutional prohibition against unreasonable searches. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the officer testified he had personal safety concerns based on defendant's position near the stolen vehicle, his flight, his fabricated path of travel, and the crime level of the neighborhood, coupled with the officer's own experience that persons arrested for stealing a vehicle may have on them either weapons or tools which can double as weapons. The officer's concern for his personal safety, defendant's attire and actions, the time and place of the stop, and the area's crime level all factored into the totality of the circumstances. The trial court made numerous findings, including that the officer's testimony was credible, and it was for the trial court to determine witness credibility and the weight to be given to the testimony. The appellate court concluded that these findings were not clearly erroneous and, based on the totality of the circumstances, the pat-down was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Daniels v. Wis. Chiropractic Examining Bd.


Appeal No. 2007AP1072


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2008 WI App 59; 309 Wis. 2d 485; 750 N.W.2d 951; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 193


February 14, 2008, Submitted on Briefs  
March 12, 2008, Decided 
March 12, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: MARK GEMPELER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CV1806.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Finding that respondent chiropractor was convicted of federal tax evasion, he obtained compensation by fraud from patients, and he failed to release patient records, the administrative law judge recommended that his license be suspended. Appellant Wisconsin Chiropractic Examining Board revoked the chiropractor's license to practice, but the Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Wisconsin, reversed. The Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the Board contended the circuit court erred in reversing its decision to revoke the chiropractor's license to practice. The appellate court agreed, finding that the circuit court reversed on two grounds. First, it held that the Board did not demonstrate a proper exercise of discretion because it failed to adequately explain its decision to revoke the chiropractor's license when the administrative law judge (ALJ) only recommended suspension. Second, the circuit court held that the Board denied the chiropractor due process because it did not allow him to appear before the Board (as opposed to the ALJ) regarding the proper sanction for his violations. The appellate court held that the Board's written decision made a reasoned justification of the sanction it selected, and also explained why it departed from the ALJ's recommendation, just as the Wis. Stat. § 446.03 (2005-06) required. Further, the chiropractor's due process rights were satisfied in the proceeding before the ALJ; there was no statutory or constitutional right to a hearing before the Board as a whole, either in the first instance or on remand.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order reversing the Board's decision to revoke the chiropractor's license was reversed.

State v. Skau


Appeal No. 2007AP1121-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2008 WI App 51; 309 Wis. 2d 236; 747 N.W.2d 528; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 153



February 21, 2008, Decided 
February 21, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson County: RANDY R. KOSCHNICK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CT227



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to suppress the evidence, arguing that the police did not have reasonable suspicion to stop him or probable cause to arrest him. The Circuit Court for Jefferson County, Wisconsin, denied the motion, and defendant pled no contest to operating while intoxicated, second offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant argued that the unidentified informant's tip that defendant had passed in a no-passing zone and was tailgating was insufficient to provide police with reasonable suspicion to stop him. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the informant, who called the police to report that he or she was observing defendant as he passed in a no-passing zone and had tailgated, provided information that could have led to his or her identification: his or her phone number. The caller stayed on the phone and dispatch was able to provide the arresting officer with updated information of the vehicles' location. The information provided by the caller was sufficient to establish the caller's basis of knowledge. The combination of tailgating and passing in a no-passing zone suggested driving that could have posed an imminent threat to public safety. Under the totality of the circumstances, the appellate court concluded that the officer was justified in relying on the information from the caller in conducting an investigative stop of defendant's vehicle.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Court v. City of Milwaukee Fire & Police Comm'n


Appeal No. 2007AP709


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2008 WI App 51; 309 Wis. 2d 235; 747 N.W.2d 528; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 130



February 20, 2008, Decided 
February 20, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN A. FRANKE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CV5905.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a patrol sergeant, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of defendant, the Milwaukee Fire and Police Commission, and affirmed the finding that the sergeant violated a department rule in his supervisory capacity as a patrol sergeant.


OVERVIEW: The sergeant appealed an order concluding that a Milwaukee Police Department rule under which the sergeant was disciplined was constitutional. The Commission found that the sergeant violated the department rule in his supervisory capacity as a patrol sergeant when, as the first police supervisor on the scene of an incident, the sergeant did not take control of the situation and scene, did not begin a criminal investigation, and allowed the situation to deteriorate. His demotion to police officer was sustained by the Commission. By certiorari petition and appeal to the circuit court, the Commission's findings and conclusions were upheld in all respects. The appellate court affirmed. Milwaukee Police Dep't Rules and Procedures Manual, Rule 4 § 4/070.00(2) plainly required a patrol sergeant to be familiar with all police officer duties and to "assist and instruct" officers under his supervision in performing those duties. As applied to the facts in this case, the sergeant's responsibility was to take control of the crime scene and instruct on-duty officers so that control could be efficiently accomplished. He did not do that.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Grant County: GEORGE S. CURRY, Judge.
City of Platteville v. Ambort, 2007 WI 61, 300 Wis. 2d 197, 732 N.W.2d 862, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 392 (2007)
City of Platteville v. Ambort, 2007 WI 61, 300 Wis. 2d 197, 732 N.W.2d 862, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 393 (2007)
City of Platteville v. Ambort, 2007 WI 61, 300 Wis. 2d 197, 732 N.W.2d 862, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 391 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver was cited for violating plaintiff city's traffic ordinance, which adopted Wis. Stat. § 346.46, by failure to stop at a stop sign and reckless driving. The Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin) ordered the driver to pay a forfeiture of $375 on the reckless driving citation and $160.80 on each of two citations for failure to stop at a stop sign. The driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: The police identified the driver by obtaining from a store cashier a credit card receipt for a purchase that the driver had made just before the traffic violations. The driver contended that the circuit court should have suppressed the receipt at trial because it was obtained by an unconstitutional search and seizure. The driver also contended that the trial court improperly considered his invocation of his right to remain silent under the Fifth Amendment when reaching its decision. The appellate court disagreed, noting that: (1) nothing in the record supported the claim; and (2) regardless, it would have been within the trial court's power to draw a negative inference had it in fact done so because the case at hand was a civil case. The appellate court found no merit in several other arguments by the driver, including a contention that the evidence at trial was insufficient to prove by a clear and convincing standard that he was the driver who was seen committing the violations.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments were affirmed.

State v. Beckwith


Appeal No. 2007AP1238-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2008 WI App 51; 309 Wis. 2d 236; 747 N.W.2d 528; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 108



February 7, 2008, Decided 
February 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia County: JAMES MILLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CT301.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of driving with a prohibited alcohol content (PAC) of.08 or more, second offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with driving while under the influence of an intoxicant (OWI) and driving with a PAC of.08 or more, second offense. The jury returned a verdict of guilty on the PAC charge but not guilty on the OWI charge. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred in ruling that she could not impeach the arresting officer with testimony that he gave at two administrative review hearings in cases involving persons other than herself. The court concluded that even if there was error, the error was harmless. The court was satisfied that a reasonable jury would have convicted defendant on the PAC charge even if she had been permitted to impeach the arresting officer with respect to his knowledge of the field sobriety tests. The jury evidently was not persuaded by the arresting officer's testimony that defendant's ability to drive was impaired, even without the impeaching testimony. The arresting officer's testimony on the field sobriety tests was simply irrelevant to the elements of the PAC charge. Any error in not permitting defendant to impeach the arresting officer with respect to the field sobriety tests did not contribute to the PAC verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Albert Trostel & Sons Co. v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n


Appeal No. 2007AP923


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2008 WI App 51; 309 Wis. 2d 235; 747 N.W.2d 528; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 99



February 5, 2008, Decided 
February 5, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEAN W. DiMOTTO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CV8209.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the employer and its insurer, admitted some, but not all liability on respondent employee's benefits claim. An administrative law judge (ALJ) found the employer and the insurer liable for reasonable medical expenses, including back surgery, and temporary total-disability benefits. Respondent Labor and Industry Review Commission affirmed, as did the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin. The employer and its insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the employer and the insurer contended the Commission erred by awarding the employee temporary total-disability benefits and by ordering them to pay for the employee's surgeries. The appellate court disagreed, finding that under either version of the amended statute, Wis. Stat. § 102.18(1)(b), the employer and its insurer had to pay for the employee's treatment for his work-related injury as that treatment became necessary. Because the ALJ retained jurisdiction for such further findings and awards as might be warranted, the employer and the insurer would have the opportunity to seek a determination as to whether disc-replacement surgery was still reasonable and necessary if the employee's medical condition changed. Thus, the employer and its insurer failed to show that the statute violated their due process rights. Further, the record supported the Commission's decision, including the opinions of several doctors who recommended some additional form of surgery. As the employee was still in a healing period, he was entitled to temporary total benefits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dahl


Appeal Nos. 2007AP647-CR, 2007AP648-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE

Review denied by State v. Dahl, 2008 WI 40, 308 Wis. 2d 612, 749 N.W.2d 663, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 242 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Pierce County: ROBERT W. WING, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2005CT53, 2005CF50.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin) of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated as a fifth or subsequent offense, operating with a prohibited alcohol concentration as a fifth or subsequent offense, disorderly conduct, and operation after revocation. Defendant appealed from her convictions, as well as the trial court's order denying her motion for postconviction relief under Wis. Stat. § 752.35.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted, she sought a new trial in the interests of justice and alleged ineffective assistance of counsel. The trial court denied the motion. The court affirmed on appeal. Defendant was not entitled to a new trial, as the real controversy was fully tried, for purposes of Wis. Stat. § 752.35. In this regard, the court rejected defendant's claim that the State presented inaccurate information in referring to keys that defendant's investigator apparently determined did not fit the car in question. There was no independent verification that the investigator found and tested the correct vehicle and the State's passing reference to defendant's possession of keys in closing arguments did not prevent the real controversy from being fully tried. There was no jury instruction error as claimed and the matter was not preserved for review in any event, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 805.13(3). Even assuming that the State's questions and the resulting answers were improper, certain remarks were not a direct comment on defendant's silence and the admission of the others was harmless. Defendant was unable to show that counsel provided ineffective assistance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

724 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Marten-Hoye


Appeal No. 2006AP1104-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2008 WI App 19; 307 Wis. 2d 671; 746 N.W.2d 498; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 64


February 6, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
January 24, 2008, Decided 
January 24, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Marten-Hoye, 2008 WI 40, 749 N.W.2d 661, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 198 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD G. NIESS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF2220.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Dane County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) of disorderly conduct and possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the search was unconstitutional because it was incident to the issuance of a citation rather than a custodial arrest. The court of appeals agreed. The record revealed conflicting circumstances. The officer told defendant that she was under arrest, but also that she would be issued a citation for a municipal ordinance violation and would be free to go. She placed defendant in handcuffs but did not place her in a squad car, instead conducting the entire interaction in public. While the officer searched defendant, another officer was writing out the citation that would have ended in defendant's release. Considering all of the circumstances of the situation, a reasonable person in defendant's position would not have believed he or she was "in custody." Immediately after the officer told defendant that she was under arrest, she also told her that she would be issued a citation and then would be free to go. Defendant's being placed in handcuffs was associated with the fact that she was being loud and uttering profanities rather than indicating that she was being placed in police custody.


OUTCOME: The possession conviction was reversed. The judgment was otherwise affirmed and the case was remanded.

City of Milwaukee Post No. 2874 VFW v. Redevelopment Auth.


Appeal No. 2006AP2866


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2008 WI App 24; 307 Wis. 2d 518; 746 N.W.2d 536; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 53


September 18, 2007, Oral Argument  
January 23, 2008, Decided 
January 23, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by City of Milwaukee v. Redevelopment Auth., 2008 WI 124, 314 Wis. 2d 279, 758 N.W.2d 924, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 986 (2008)
Reversed by City of Milwaukee Post No. 2874 Vfw v. Redevelopment Auth. of Milwaukee, 2009 WI 84, 768 N.W.2d 749, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 294 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ELSA C. LAMELAS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV365.
City of Milwaukee Redevelopment Auth. v. VFW Post 2874, 2003 WI App 225, 267 Wis. 2d 960, 671 N.W.2d 717, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 918 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, dismissed appellant City of Milwaukee Post 2874 Veterans of Foreign Wars of the United States' (VFW) claim that respondent Redevelopment Authority of the City of Milwaukee's condemnation of the building within which the VFW had pre-paid for a long-term lease without compensation for the lease was unconstitutional. The VFW appealed.


OVERVIEW: The VFW argued that the unit rule was unconstitutional as applied to the particular facts and circumstances of the case. The unit rule had been used in condemnation cases to determine fair market value of the property as a single entity as if there were but one owner. The appellate court noted that strict application of the unit resulted in no compensation to the VFW. Because of the application of the unit rule, the VFW was prohibited from proving the value of its lease to the jury. The application of the unit rule under these circumstance was unconstitutional. The constitutional requirement of just compensation derived as much content from the basic equitable principles of fairness as it did from technical concepts of property law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Brown County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Ivan L.-C (In re Ivannies L.)

January 15, 2008, Decided 
January 15, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Brown County DHS v. Ivan L.-C., 2008 WI 115, 310 Wis. 2d 709, 754 N.W.2d 852, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 549 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown County: MARK A. WARPINSKI, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006TP60.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, terminating his parental rights.


OVERVIEW: In September 2005, the mother and father's parental rights to two children were terminated. In January 2006, the mother gave birth to a third child, the child at issue, who was born with cocaine in her system. The mother and father were not married at the time, and in fact, the mother was married to another man. The circuit court found evidence to overcome the marital presumption, and the father was adjudicated the child's parent. The circuit court later terminated parental rights to the third child because the parental rights to the older children had been terminated in September 2005. The appellate court ruled that there was nothing ambiguous about Wis. Stat. § 48.415(10) (2005-2006), and Wis. Stat. § 48.415(10) was narrowly tailored to advance the compelling interest in protecting children from unfit parents. The father could not be found unfit under the statute unless the child was currently in need of protection or services for the child's health, safety, or welfare, and the father had his rights involuntarily terminated to another child within the previous three years. Also, the statute was not unconstitutional as applied.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Robert T. (In re Robert T.)


Appeal No. 2006AP2206


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI App 22; 307 Wis. 2d 488; 746 N.W.2d 564; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 38


November 28, 2007, Oral Argument  
January 15, 2008, Decided 
January 15, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MARY E. TRIGGIANO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006JV387.
State v. Robert T., 2007 WI 61, 300 Wis. 2d 197, 732 N.W.2d 862, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 389 (2007).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, dismissing the delinquency petition brought against respondent juvenile for violating Wis. Stat. § 947.015 (2003-2004).


OVERVIEW: A 911 call was placed from a pay phone at the high school to the police. The caller said that there was a bomb in the school. The police were sent to the school. A surveillance camera revealed the caller, who was later identified as respondent. Respondent admitted making the call. The trial court ruled that Wis. Stat. § 947.015 was unconstitutional, finding the statute impermissibly overbroad. Respondent argued that to be a "true threat," the threat must be addressed to a person or persons and must threaten bodily harm or death. The appellate court ruled that the statute respondent was charged with violating was not unconstitutional. Respondent's telephone call was a "true threat" and fell outside the protections found in the First Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 3. The police who responded to respondent's phone call believed the threat was real. Respondent apparently intended to frighten the listener, thus his call appeared to fall within the ambit of a "true threat." A "true threat" was not limited to only threats of bodily harm or death directed to a person or group of persons.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded with directions.

Villa Italian Pizza Rest. of Muskego, LLC v. LaLicata Woods LLC


Appeal No. 2006AP2192


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2008 WI App 36; 308 Wis. 2d 393; 746 N.W.2d 604; 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 26



January 9, 2008, Decided 
January 9, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: MARK S. GEMPELER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CV139.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which denied its motion to dismiss plaintiff restaurant's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 suit that challenged the city's denial of its application for a liquor license.


OVERVIEW: The restaurant brought an action against the city under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, challenging the city's denial of its application for a liquor license. The city moved to dismiss the complaint for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court found that the allegations in the complaint were insufficient to state a claim for relief under § 1983. Because the complaint did not allege discrimination based on membership in any particular class or group, like an ethnic or racial class, an equal protection claim was not raised. The restaurant did not allege an illegitimate animus toward its business. Moreover, the facts as alleged in the complaint failed to support a conclusion that the restaurant was intentionally treated differently from others similarly situated and that there was no rational basis for the difference in treatment. The allegations of the complaint indicated that the restaurant was a new applicant for a liquor license from the city, while the building owners, who were granted a license, had been issued licenses in the past. The restaurant failed to set forth a claim for a due process violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to enter an order dismissing the complaint.

December 27, 2007, Decided 
December 27, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Bergemann, 2008 WI 40, 308 Wis. 2d 611, 749 N.W.2d 662, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 217 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown County: RICHARD J. DIETZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1996CV1156.
State v. Bergemann, 222 Wis. 2d 624, 587 N.W.2d 457, 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1151 (Wis. Ct. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, denied defendant's motion for postcommitment relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At a hearing in 1996, defendant moved to dismiss a Wis. Stat. ch. 980 petition, challenging a court's jurisdiction on the grounds that he had not been served with the petition. Defendant withdrew his motion challenging service. Because defendant withdrew his motion challenging service, the circuit court did not hear rebuttal testimony on the issue of whether defendant had been served and did not rule on the service issue. Before the court, defendant argued that Wis. Stat. ch. 980 violated due process because it did not require adequate service on the person against whom the petition was brought. The court found that defendant's position was inconsistent with the position he took during the 1996 proceedings when he decided to withdraw his challenge to service. The facts before the court were the same as the facts that existed in 1996, when defendant affirmatively requested that the circuit court not consider his motion challenging service. Thus, defendant was judicially estopped from challenging the constitutionality of the service requirements in the statute.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Fowler


Appeal No. 2007AP792-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2008 WI App 1; 306 Wis. 2d 851; 743 N.W.2d 168; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1039



November 29, 2007, Decided 
November 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Marquette County: RICHARD O. WRIGHT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CT124.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated and with operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration. The Circuit Court for Marquette County (Wisconsin) granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence based on an allegedly unconstitutional stop of defendant's vehicle. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the police officer who stopped defendant possessed reasonable suspicion for the stop under the totality of the circumstances. The appellate court agreed that the officer could have reasonably suspected that defendant was driving while impaired because defendant had exited a highway, made a U-turn without signaling, stopped in the intersection in the middle of the turn, thus blocking a lane and partially blocking the intersection, was unable to complete the turn apparently because of an island with a traffic sign in the intersection, began rolling backwards, revved his engine in a loud manner, and then proceeded forward, heading in the direction from which he had just come. All this occurred at approximately 3:00 a.m., a time when intoxicated drivers were more likely to be on the road. Although there might have been innocent explanations for these driving behaviors, conduct with innocent explanations might also give rise to a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity. The fact that the officer might have stopped defendant primarily because of the officer's subjective belief that he was executing an illegal U-turn was not determinative.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order granting the motion to suppress was reversed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

On appeal, the court held that the three counts charging defendant with violating Wis. State v. Jensen


Appeal No. 2006AP2095-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 256; 306 Wis. 2d 572; 743 N.W.2d 468; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 973


August 16, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
November 8, 2007, Decided 
November 8, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Jensen, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 24 (Wis. Ct. App., Jan. 15, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: STEVEN D. EBERT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CF2453.
State v. Jensen, 2004 WI App 89, 272 Wis. 2d 707, 681 N.W.2d 230, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 276 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of three counts of felony misconduct in public office, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3) (2005-06).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a member of the Wisconsin State Legislature, was convicted of three counts of felony misconduct in public office. The complaint alleged that he hired state employees to solicit campaign funds, recruit, otherwise assist political candidates, and work on his own campaign, all on time compensated by the state and with the intent to obtain a dishonest advantage. On appeal, the court concluded that a jury instruction on misconduct in public office was erroneous. Because the instruction directed the jury that a legislator's use of state resources for campaign purposes established that the legislator obtained a dishonest advantage, it constituted a mandatory conclusive presumption. The failure to provide a limiting instruction under Wis. Stat. § 903.03(3) was therefore reversible error. The trial court also erred in excluding defendant's testimony as to his understanding of the use of state resources for campaigns by other legislators; the testimony was relevant to the contested issue of defendant's intent. However, the trial court properly excluded the portions of defense witnesses' testimony as to those practices as their beliefs were not relevant to defendant's intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment as to the jury instruction on misconduct in public office and the exclusion of defendant's testimony as to his understanding of the use of state resources for campaigns by other legislators. The court affirmed the remainder of the trial court's judgment. The court remanded the case for a new trial.

 

736 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schultz


Appeal No. 2006AP2121-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 257; 306 Wis. 2d 598; 743 N.W.2d 823; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 974


April 20, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
November 8, 2007, Decided 
November 8, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: STEVEN D. EBERT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CF2455.
State v. Jensen, 2004 WI App 89, 272 Wis. 2d 707, 681 N.W.2d 230, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 276 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brought an interlocutory appeal of the complaint charging her with one count of felony misconduct in public office, challenging the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3) (2005-06). Her assertions were rejected on appeal. Ultimately, the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of one count of felony misconduct in public office, and she appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court's jury instruction on misconduct in public office contained mandatory conclusive presumptions on the elements of duty and intent. The appellate court agreed, finding that the error consisted of an instruction that the jury had to accept as true the elemental facts that defendant acted inconsistently with the duties of her office and intended to obtain a dishonest disadvantage if the jury found that she used state resources to promote a candidate or to raise money for political campaign purposes. This operated as mandatory conclusive presumptions in violation of Wis. Stat. § 903.03(3) (2005-06) because the jury was not instructed that it could, but did not have to, accept the elemental facts as true. Thus, the instruction required the jury to find the intent and duty elements were met upon finding that defendant participated in campaign activities on state time. Defendant's substantial rights were affected because the instruction operated to relieve the State of its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant acted inconsistently with her duties and with the intent to obtain a dishonest advantage for herself or another.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Bowden


Appeal No. 2006AP1127-CR

2007 WI App 234; 306 Wis. 2d 393; 742 N.W.2d 332; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 946


September 25, 2007, Submitted on Briefs

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of two counts of interfering with child custody as a repeat offender, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.31(2) and Wis. Stat. § 939.62(1)(b) (2005-06).


OVERVIEW: Two boys were walking home from school when they were approached by defendant. Despite the boys' assertions that they had to be home at a certain time, defendant led them to another house. The people inside of the residence testified that the boys appeared afraid. Because they were unsure of defendant's intentions, the persons inside of the residence walked the boys home. Defendant was later convicted of two counts of interfering with child custody under Wis. Stat. § 948.31(2) (2005-06). This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that there was sufficient evidence to support the convictions. The element at issue in this case involved whether defendant caused the boys to leave their mother's care. Defendant's argument that this element was not satisfied because the boys were not with her at the time was rejected. Parental custody did not end because the children were outside of the mother's presence. Defendant's conduct clearly met the elements of the offense because he insisted that they come with him instead of walking home. Finally, because an argument relating to constitutional vagueness was not developed, it was not addressed.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

738 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ebersold


Appeal No. 2006AP833-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 232; 306 Wis. 2d 371; 742 N.W.2d 876; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 940


October 9, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
October 25, 2007, Decided 
October 25, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Marquette County: RICHARD O. WRIGHT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF89.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with one count of verbally communicating a harmful description or narrative account to a child. The Circuit Court for Marquette County, Wisconsin, granted defendant's motion to dismiss, concluding that defendant's Internet chat messages to the alleged victim were written descriptions outside the scope of Wis. Stat. § 948.11(2)(am) (2005-06). The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State's complaint alleged that defendant, a high school teacher, verbally communicated a harmful description or narrative account to a child by sending sexually explicit messages to one of his students in an Internet chat room. On review, the State asserted that the written messages sent by defendant were within the scope of communications prohibited by Wis. Stat. § 948.11(2)(am) (2005-06). The appellate court found that the statute was facially ambiguous; but after reviewing the statute and its legislative history, the appellate court agreed with the State and held that "verbally" was most reasonably read here as proscribing communication to children of harmful matter in words, whether oral or written. The statute indicated that the communication could be "by any means," suggesting the legislature intended to ban all communications of harmful material or narratives to children, whether in oral or written form. Defendant also failed to show that the statute did not give persons of ordinary intelligence fair notice that it prohibited written communication to children of harmful descriptions or narratives.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the State's complaint was reversed, and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Rizzo


Appeal No. 2006AP1788-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2007 WI App 251; 306 Wis. 2d 447; 742 N.W.2d 74; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 910



October 17, 2007, Decided 
October 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Rizzo, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 449 (Wis. Ct. App., June 16, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Kenosha County: MICHAEL S. FISHER and BRUCE E. SCHROEDER, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CF158.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of the repeated sexual assault of the same child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.025(1) (1999-2000), denied his postconviction motion for an in camera review of social service records related to the victim pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.78(2), and denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of sexually assaulting his stepdaughter, and his conviction was based upon the victim's testimony. After his conviction, defendant learned of a pending social services investigation that someone else had sexually assaulted the victim, who with the assailant, sexually assaulted defendant's son. On appeal, the court found that an in camera inspection of the social service records was required under either the Courtney F. test or the Shiffra-Green test. The social services records were reasonably likely to contain evidence that could provide an alternative source for the victim's sexual knowledge and diminish the impact of the expert testimony regarding the behavior of child sexual assault victims. As such, Rizzo made the requisite showing that the social services records were reasonably likely to contain relevant information necessary to a determination of his guilt or innocence. Because defendant failed to timely object to the verdict and jury instructions, he waived his claim that Wis. Stat. § 948.025 as applied violated his right to a unanimous verdict, and his counsel's trial strategy did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the denial of postconviction relief. However, the court reversed the denial of the in camera review and remanded the matter to the trial court to conduct an in camera examination of the social services records.

State v. Somerhalder


Appeal Nos. 2007AP155-CR, 2007AP156-CR

2007 WI App 251; 306 Wis. 2d 448; 742 N.W.2d 75; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 903



October 16, 2007, Decided 
October 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Somerhalder, 2008 WI 19, 307 Wis. 2d 295, 746 N.W.2d 813, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 125 (2008)
Review denied by State v. Somerhalder, 2008 WI 19, 307 Wis. 2d 295, 746 N.W.2d 813, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 119 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Brown County: MARK A. WARPINSKI, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2003CF1161, 2004CF841.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of five counts of sexual assault and two counts involving videotaping. He also appealed an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed two judgments of conviction and an order denying his motion for postconviction relief, arguing that he was entitled to withdraw his pleas and that his sentence was unduly harsh and based on improper factors. The appellate court affirmed. In the plea agreement, the State agreed to keep the presentence investigation (PSI) writer from having contact with the investigating officer. However, the PSI writer did in fact discuss the case with that officer. Thus, it was ordered that a new PSI be prepared by a different writer who would have no contact with the officer. Therefore, defendant received the PSI he had bargained for, and there was no manifest injustice warranting withdrawal of defendant's plea. The State did not breach the plea agreement because defendant's attorneys' testimony was found credible as to the terms of the agreement. Both attorneys testified that the agreement did not include any term limiting consideration of the dismissed and uncharged counts. They also testified that the agreement allowed the Sate to discuss circumstantial evidence of date rape drugs. Further, defendant's attorneys' performance was not deficient.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Williams v. Am. Transmission Co., LLC


Appeal No. 2007AP52


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 246; 306 Wis. 2d 181; 742 N.W.2d 882; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 882


August 7, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
October 4, 2007, Decided 
October 4, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Williams v. Am. Transmission Co. LLC, 2008 WI 19, 746 N.W.2d 812, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 84 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: JAMES E. WELKER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CV145.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, company, challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Rock County, Wisconsin, allowing respondent, property owner, to proceed with his claim for inverse condemnation against the company.


OVERVIEW: The company maintained electrical power poles and transmission lines on the owner's property, and asserted that its use of the property for more than ten years established the prescriptive right to continue the use under Wis. Stat. § 893.28 (2005-2006). The question the parties disputed was whether the construction and maintenance of the electrical poles and transmission lines, pursuant to a pole and wire agreement, constituted use of rights in real estate of another within the meaning of the statute. The appellate court ruled that "use of rights" encompassed the use at issue in the instant case. Wis. Stat. § 893.28(2) applied to permissive uses, and did not specify that the "use" be non-permissive. The Wisconsin Legislature had simply concluded that, if a utility had continuously used rights in property of another for at least ten years, then prescribing a right to continue that use was consistent with sound public policy. The Legislature had apparently determined that, even if the statute deterred some property owners from granting utilities permissive use of their property, alternative options, including condemnation when available, were sufficient.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded.

State v. Martinez


Appeal Nos. 2006AP2883-CR, 2006AP2884-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 225; 305 Wis. 2d 753; 741 N.W.2d 280; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 847


August 14, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
September 26, 2007, Decided 
September 26, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: TIMOTHY M. VAN AKKEREN, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 1992CF370, 1993CF240.
State v. Martinez, 198 Wis. 2d 222, 542 N.W.2d 215, 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1593 (Wis. Ct. App., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which denied his Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2005-06) motion for discharge from sentence.


OVERVIEW: In 1993, defendant was sentenced in state court to 14 years in prison. In January 2001, he was sentenced in federal court to concurrent terms on three counts of drug-related crimes. The federal sentence totaled 84 months and was consecutive to the state sentence. In June 2001, he was paroled on his state sentence directly to the federal government. After approximately four years and eight months of federal incarceration, he was released by federal authorities to state authorities to serve the remainder of his state-ordered parole. Three months later, he was incarcerated for violating his parole. The trial court denied his motion for discharge from sentence. On appeal, he argued that the trial court erroneously exercised its discretion by applying Wis. Stat. § 973.155 rather than Wis. Stat. § 973.15(5). The court disagreed. At the time defendant was serving his federal sentence, he did not have a custodial sentence to which the federal sentence could be, or could be presumed to be, concurrent. Under § 973.155 and the teaching of Rohl, defendant's credit request could not be granted because it would constitute impermissible double credit against two non-concurrent sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Lowden


Appeal No. 2006AP2087-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2007 WI App 230; 306 Wis. 2d 125; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 836



September 25, 2007, Decided 
September 25, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Lowden, 2008 WI 19, 307 Wis. 2d 293, 746 N.W.2d 811, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 45 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF3825.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Milwaukee County Circuit Court, Wisconsin, which convicted him of second degree sexual assault of a child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2) (2005-2006).


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the trial court erred when it denied defendant the opportunity to present evidence that the minor victim had intentionally misrepresented her age. The instant court concluded that the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion in limine when it refused to admit evidence that the victim had intentionally misrepresented her age. The victim's intentional misrepresentation of her age was not an affirmative defense. Evidence regarding defendant's belief about the victim's age and evidence suggesting that defendant's belief was reasonable was not relevant. Although defendant argued that his constitutional rights to confront and cross-examine witnesses was violated because the trial court did not permit him to introduce evidence of the victim's intentional misrepresentation of her age, defendant's constitutional challenge to § 948.02(2) was not premised on vagueness, overbreadth, or substantive due process grounds; Furthermore, defendant argument was undeveloped. Accordingly, the instant court rejected defendant's constitutional challenge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Rock County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Staci M. (In re Joseph J.M.)

September 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: RICHARD T. WERNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006TP39.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, mother, challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Rock County, Wisconsin, terminating her parental rights to her child.


OVERVIEW: The child was born in the hallway of a crack house. When the child was born, he had cocaine in his system, as did the mother. Within a few days after the child's birth, the mother voluntarily entered drug rehabilitation and the child was placed in foster care. The child was found to be in need of protection and services (CHIPS), and the county filed a petition to terminate the mother's parental rights under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(10) (2005-2006). The mother challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(10) on its face. The appellate court rejected the mother's substantive due process challenge. Each of the predicate steps under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(10) required the trial court to make findings and determinations about the parent's ability and fitness to parent based on the parent's individual circumstances. Also, as applied to the mother, Wis. Stat. § 48.415 did not run afoul of substantive due process safeguards. The CHIPS adjudication was a direct result of the mother's decision to use drugs and not seek proper medical care, and the mother's failure to appear was the cause of the default judgment in the termination of parental rights case.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Drew


Appeal No. 2006AP2522-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 213; 305 Wis. 2d 641; 740 N.W.2d 404; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 765


June 13, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
August 30, 2007, Decided 
August 30, 2007, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Grant County: ROBERT P. VAN DE HEY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF86.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to suppress and convicted him of substantial battery and possession of methamphetamines.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of substantial battery and possession of methamphetamines. On appeal, he claimed that the out-of-court identification of him in a photographic array should have been suppressed and that the subsequent in-court identification was tainted by the allegedly faulty photographic array. He asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress. The court concluded that Dubose did not alter the standard for determining whether admission of an out-of-court identification from a photographic array violated due process. The trial court applied the correct standard of Powell and Mosley in determining whether admission of the identification from the photographic array violated defendant's right to due process. Defendant conceded that the identification was admissible under such standard. Accordingly, the admission of the photographic identification did not violate defendant's right to due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. St. Germaine


Appeal No. 2006AP2555-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 214; 305 Wis. 2d 511; 740 N.W.2d 148; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 702


May 1, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
August 14, 2007, Decided 
August 14, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. St. Germaine, 2008 WI 6, 744 N.W.2d 297, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 946 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOSEPH R. WALL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF7212.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to suppress and convicted him of one count of manufacture of more than four but less than 20 plants containing tetrahydrocannabinols (marijuana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled no contest to one count of manufacture of more than four but less than 20 plants containing marijuana. On appeal, he claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence that the police discovered after a warrantless entry into a room that he was renting. The court found that the owner of the residence where the room was located provided valid consent for the search of the room such that there was no violation of defendant's rights under the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution or Wis. Const. art. I, § 11. Defendant was present in the kitchen and overheard the entire exchange that took place between the officers and the owner of the residence, during which the owner told the officers that defendant rented a room, without identifying which room, and consented to a search of the entire premises without limitation. There was no way for the officers to distinguish defendant's room from the rest of the house for which they had consent to search. Defendant's silence served as a tacit affirmation supporting the officers' reasonable belief that the owner had the apparent authority to provide such consent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Krist Oil Co. v. Bulk Petroleum Corp.


Appeal No. 2005AP1398


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2007 WI App 203; 305 Wis. 2d 376; 738 N.W.2d 190; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 672



July 31, 2007, Decided 
July 31, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Marinette County: DAVID G. MIRON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2000CV2.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petroleum corporation sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Marinette County (Wisconsin), which awarded summary judgment, damages, costs, and attorney fees to plaintiff gas station operator in an action for violation of the Wisconsin Unfair Sales Act, Wis. Stat. § 100.30 (1999-2000). The operator challenged the amount of costs and attorney fees that it was awarded.


OVERVIEW: The operator brought an action against the corporation for violation of the Act. The trial court awarded summary judgment to the operator and held that the corporation violated the Act on 238 days. The trial court awarded the operator statutory damages, plus costs and attorney fees. On appeal, the court concluded that the trial court erred when it ruled that a lack of documentary evidence under Wis. Stat. § 100.30(6)(a)7 was fatal to the corporation's summary judgment defense. The failure of the corporation to retain records to verify a lower competitor's price or to verify filing a notice with the Wisconsin Department of Agriculture, Trade, and Consumer Protection did not dispositively mean that it was not meeting competition. It only meant that the corporation had the burden of establishing that it actually was meeting competition in good faith. Nothing about the plain language of § 100.30(6)(a)7 required that advertisements or records be produced at trial. Nothing in § 100.30 precluded the corporation from offering testimony about the documents it relied on when making the pricing changes. A factual issue was raised as to whether the asserted documents ever existed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court also reversed the award of costs and attorney fees to the operator; on remand, the trial court was to vacate the order.

 

752 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roou


Appeal No. 2006AP1574-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 193; 305 Wis. 2d 164; 738 N.W.2d 173; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 635


June 6, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
July 18, 2007, Decided  
July 18, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Roou, 2008 WI 40, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 206 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Washington County: DAVID C. RESHESKE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CF126.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest to armed robbery with use of force under Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(1)(a) and 939.50(3)(c) (2005-06) and second-degree recklessly endangering safety under Wis. Stat. §§ 941.30(2) and 939.50(3)(g) (2005-06). Postconviction, defendant moved to withdraw from the plea agreement. The circuit court for Washington County (Wisconsin) limited the remedy to withdrawal of the plea to the reckless endangerment charge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled no contest to armed robbery and reckless endangerment charges, but the trial court misinformed him of the reckless endangerment elements. The trial court imposed a 25-year sentence on the armed robbery count and a concurrent sentence of 15 years on the reckless endangerment count. The trial court granted defendant's motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.30 as to the reckless endangerment charge based on the misinformation, but refused to vacate the entire agreement, leaving intact defendant's plea and sentence on the armed robbery charge. The appellate court determined that the erroneous exercise of discretion standard applied to the trial court's choice of remedy when faced with the motion to withdraw all or part of a plea agreement. The appellate court found that the trial court properly exercised its discretion when it denied defendant's request to withdraw from the entire plea because, inter alia, (1) withdrawing the defective plea left defendant with one less conviction and in the same position sentence-wise, and (2) the misinformation as to the reckless endangerment charge was not material or substantial as to the armed robbery charge.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling and the judgment.

State v. Wood


Appeal No. 2006AP1338-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 190; 305 Wis. 2d 133; 738 N.W.2d 81; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 626



July 17, 2007, Decision Dated 
July 17, 2007, Decision Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Wood, 2007 WI 134, 305 Wis. 2d 128, 742 N.W.2d 526, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 800 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: TIMOTHY G. DUGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1999CF4886.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to armed robbery, threat of force, and was sentenced to 10 years in prison. After learning of a letter by the Governor directing the department of corrections to block the release of certain violent offenders, defendant filed a motion to modify his sentence. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, construed the motion as a motion for resentencing and imposed the original sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant challenged the trial court's conclusion that a new factor in support of sentence modification had not been established and its conversion of his motion for sentence modification to a motion to vacate sentence. The appellate court found that the trial court properly concluded that the Governor's letter was not a "new factor." However, at that juncture, the motion for sentence modification should have been denied because, as the trial court implicitly found, defendant had not carried his burden to prove a new factor by clear and convincing evidence. Furthermore, defendant, who was acting pro se, repeatedly told the trial court that he had asked for, and wanted, a sentence modification and not a resentencing. The appellate court stated that the trial court should not have converted a motion for sentence modification to a motion for resentencing in the absence of a clear, unequivocal and knowing stipulation by defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded with instructions to vacate the sentence in effect, to deny the motion to modify the sentence, and to reinstate the sentence originally imposed with credit for all time served from the date the original sentence was vacated.

Leigha K v. Jason B. (In re Malakai H.K.)


Appeal No. 2006AP3121


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2007 WI App 203; 305 Wis. 2d 379; 738 N.W.2d 191; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 612



July 11, 2007, Decision Dated  
July 11, 2007, Decision Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Leigha K. v. Jason B., 2007 WI 134, 305 Wis. 2d 130, 742 N.W.2d 527, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 772 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Racine County: GERALD P. PTACEK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006TP58.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which granted petitioner mother's petition to terminate his parental rights to his child pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(9)(a) (2005-06).


OVERVIEW: At the time the child was conceived, the father was 21 years old and the mother was 15 years old. The father was later charged with having sexually assaulted the mother at the time of conception. The complaint alleged that the parents engaged in consensual sexual intercourse. The felony charge of sexual assault of a child was later amended and the father was ultimately convicted of two counts of fourth-degree sexual assault under Wis. Stat. § 940.225(3m), a Class A misdemeanor. The mother filed a petition for the involuntary termination of parental rights (TPR) against the father under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(9)(a). The trial court terminated the father's rights. On appeal, the court found that because the father was never convicted of any of the crimes specified in Wis. Stat. § 48.42(2m)(a), the mother was not entitled to deprive him of notice of the TPR petition and the trial court erred when it denied him standing to contest the termination of his rights. The trial court's ruling that the father's parental rights had to be terminated under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(9), regardless of the fact that he was never convicted of one of the specified offenses, misapplied the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of the trial court.

NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment and civil commitment order entered by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, in the action with respondent, the State of Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of a sexually violent offense. On December 16, 2002, the State filed a petition for appellant's detention pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.02(1)(b)1 (2001-2002), within ninety days of his mandatory release date of December 20, 2002. Stat. § 980.05(1) (2001-2002). The record established that the trial court could have found that good cause existed to extend the statutory deadline of Wis. Stat. § 980.05(1) (2001-2002), to avoid any potential loss of competency when it adjourned the probable cause hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Janesville v. Briarmoon


Appeal No. 2005AP3021


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 203; 305 Wis. 2d 376; 738 N.W.2d 190; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 595



July 5, 2007, Decided 
July 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Janesville v. Briarmoon, 2007 WI 134, 305 Wis. 2d 128, 742 N.W.2d 525, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 857 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Rock County: MICHAEL J. BYRON , Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005FO575.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment and order which required her to pay costs to respondent city related to this action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's chief appellate brief consisted of a number of assertions, each consisting of a conclusory sentence or two, with no reference to record citations or legal authority, and no analysis to support her contentions. Because appellant failed to develop any argument, let alone make a coherent one, the instant court rejected the arguments she did make. Because her brief contained no record citations, no analysis explaining how her claims were specifically supported by any legal authority, and no argument beyond conclusory broad statements, the instant court could not reach the merits of this case. While the instant court did grant some leniency to pro se litigants, the court could not go so far as to make the pro se appellant's arguments for her. In this case, without appellant's providing any supporting citations or analysis to accompany her undeveloped claims, the instant court declined to reach her inadequately briefed arguments.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.
