Petition denied by State v. Purifoy (In re Purifoy), 2012 WI App 52, 340 Wis. 2d 741, 2012 Wisc. App. LEXIS 224 (2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by, Stay denied by Purifoy v. McCullough, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 168096 (E.D. Wis., Nov. 26, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: RICHARD J. SANKOVITZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CI1.
State v. Purifoy, 99 Wis. 2d 801, 300 N.W.2d 81, 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3972 (Wis. Ct. App., 1980)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found him to be a sexually violent person and committed him to institutional care pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.01(7) (2003-04). On appeal, appellant challenged the timeliness of the petition seeking his committal, the sufficiency of evidence to support the circuit court's factual findings, and the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. ch. 980.


OVERVIEW: A habeas court ordered that appellant be released by May 22, 2002. Thus, the petition, filed on May 1, 2002, correctly alleged that appellant was within 90 days of release. The recalculation of appellant's mandatory release date did not render the petition untimely. As to appellant's challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence, the fact that appellant had not committed a sexually violent offense since his conviction in 1976 did not preclude a finding of dangerousness within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 980.02(2)(c) (2001-02). Further, the circuit court's conclusion that appellant was a sexually violent person was supported by evidence in the record, including appellant's high scores on an instrument designed to measure current psychopathology, his lack of remorse for his victims, his teeming anger, and his manipulation of the truth and the rules in order to avoid sex offender treatment and to carry on an illicit sexual relationship in a state mental health facility. Finally, appellant's constitutional challenge had already been rejected by the court in a prior case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Grand Videre Enters. LLC v. Town of Janesville


Appeal No. 2005AP1220


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 183; 304 Wis. 2d 633; 736 N.W.2d 542; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 587



June 28, 2007, Decided 
June 28, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: R. A. BATES, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CV936.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a corporation and condominium association, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) upholding a decision of defendant town board to rezone a parcel of land owned by intervenor property owners, which was adjacent to the condominium complex.


OVERVIEW: Applying the presumption that the zoning ordinance was valid, and giving controlling deference to the town board's zoning authority, the court concluded that the town board properly exercised its discretion in granting the petition to rezone the property. The record contained substantial evidence that rezoning the property would have benefited the public by providing a place where the public could fish, hunt, hike, train dogs, and sight their rifles. The court rejected plaintiffs' contention that the town board's sole purpose for granting the property owners' rezoning petition was to "legalize" the property owners' sport shooting business. The town board had previously determined that the property owners' use of their property was lawful, and the record was devoid of any evidence that the town board's sole purpose for rezoning the property was to legalize a nonconforming use. Finally, the court concluded that the town board did not engage in spot zoning. The size of the property was nearly 200 acres, which was much larger than other properties generally found to be subjects of spot zoning.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was affirmed.

State v. Brodeur

APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia County: JAMES MILLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CT507.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Columbia County, Wisconsin, denying his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: The officer was dispatched to investigate a report of a vehicle driving erratically on the highway. The caller gave the 911 dispatcher the license plate of the vehicle, a description and location of the vehicle, and stated that the vehicle was driving excessively fast and swerving. The caller also gave the dispatcher his name. The officer proceeded to the location and observed a vehicle matching the description relayed to him by dispatch. The officer observed the vehicle cross the fog line and move onto the gravel portion of the road. Based on his observations and the information he had received from dispatch, the officer performed a traffic stop of the vehicle. As a result of the evidence obtained during the stop, defendant was charged with driving while intoxicated. The appellate court ruled that the officer had reasonable suspicion to perform the traffic stop of defendant's vehicle. Based on the reliability of the tip and the other facts in the record, the totality of the circumstances provided the officer with reasonable suspicion to conduct an investigative stop of defendant.

State v. Keyes


Appeal Nos. 2004AP1104-CR, 2004AP1105-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 163; 304 Wis. 2d 372; 736 N.W.2d 904; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 547


January 27, 2005, Oral Argument  
June 14, 2007, Decided 
June 14, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Keyes, 2007 WI 134, 305 Wis. 2d 126, 742 N.W.2d 524, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 740 (2007)
Review granted by State v. Keyes, 2007 WI 134, 305 Wis. 2d 126, 742 N.W.2d 524, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 725 (2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by State v. Keyes, 2008 WI 54, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 304 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEALS from orders of the circuit court for La Crosse County: MICHAEL J. MC ALPINE, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2003CF339 2003CF340.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which denied their motion to dismiss a bindover and an information charging them with felony theft by contractor, party to a crime, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 779.02(5), 939.05, and 943.20(1)(b) and (3)(c) (2001-02).


OVERVIEW: Defendants owned and operated a construction contracting company. They were charged with felony theft by contractor, party to a crime. A preliminary hearing was held, after which the trial court bound defendants over for trial. The trial court denied defendants' motion to dismiss the bindover and the information. On appeal, the court concluded that Wis. Stat. § 779.02(5) prohibited a prime contractor who also acted as a subcontractor from taking a profit on items supplied as a subcontractor before all other subcontractors were paid for labor and materials in full, or proportionately in cases of a deficiency. Defendants could be held criminally liable because the undisputed evidence indicated that they intentionally used money from entrusted funds to pay themselves a profit. The trial court had sufficient evidence to deny defendants' motion to dismiss their bindover and information. Defendants admitted that the unaccounted amount of $ 36,038 was money that one defendant took as a profit. It could reasonably be inferred that clients did not consent to defendants paying themselves a profit before paying the subcontractors for labor and materials.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

State v. Williams, 2001 WI 88, 246 Wis. 2d 166, 630 N.W.2d 219, 2001 Wisc. LEXIS 482 (2001).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin ) of first-degree sexual assault of a child and one count of child enticement. After his motion for correction of his sentence was denied, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to correct an erroneous sentence because it was illegal as it unconstitutionally increased his originally-imposed term of probation to ten years in prison. The court of appeals declined to address the merits of defendant's claim because it was procedurally barred. Defendant failed to raise the sentencing issues in his direct appeal. Moreover, he failed to raise the sentencing issue in his pro se motion for postconviction relief. Defendant could have and should have raised the issue either during his direct appeal or during his first postconviction motion/appeal. Because he failed to do so in either his first or second appeal, his sentencing claims were procedurally barred. Moreover, defendant failed to provide the court of appeals with a sufficient reason to overcome the procedural bar. Defendant did briefly allege that his postconviction counsel's ineffective assistance should constitute a sufficient reason for failing to raise the issue. However, defendant failed to adequately brief such argument, and failed to reply to the State's response that his argument was insufficient to overcome the procedural bar.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Gallion


Appeal No. 2006AP2027


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2007 WI App 162; 303 Wis. 2d 747; 735 N.W.2d 194; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 505



May 30, 2007, Decided  
May 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Gallion, 2007 WI 134, 305 Wis. 2d 129, 742 N.W.2d 527, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 761 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DAVID A. HANSHER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2000CF1148.
State v. Gallion, 2002 WI App 265, 258 Wis. 2d 473, 654 N.W.2d 446, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1121 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for homicide by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle; his postconviction motion challenging the sentence was denied, and the denial was twice affirmed on appeal. Years later, defendant filed a motion seeking to withdraw his guilty plea on the basis that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, summarily denied the motion, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that he received ineffective assistance of counsel and that his guilty plea was unconstitutional because he was not properly advised that one of the charges would be dismissed. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the record showed that defendant knew one of the charges would be dismissed upon conviction, and that he could not be convicted of both charges. This was clearly stated before defendant entered his plea. Moreover, defense counsel noted on the record that she had explained to defendant that the statute allowed different ways of proving the offense. Further, the complaint was not required to contain evidence regarding prior convictions because the two statutes with which defendant was charged, Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a), (b) (1999-2000), did not require proof of other convictions, suspensions or revocations. Accordingly, there was no basis for trial counsel to seek dismissal of the complaint. The sentencing transcript demonstrated that trial counsel argued for leniency and emphasized defendant's extreme remorse, which carried more persuasiveness than the notation defendant relied on on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

763 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wuteska


Appeal No. 2006AP2248-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 157; 303 Wis. 2d 646; 735 N.W.2d 574; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 458



May 17, 2007, Dated  
May 17, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Wuteska, 2007 WI 120, 304 Wis. 2d 612, 741 N.W.2d 242, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 615 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Marquette County: RICHARD O. WRIGHT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2006CF25.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State brought a "hit-and-run" charge against respondent driver. The driver moved to dismiss the criminal complaint on the ground that the complaint failed to state facts concerning every element of the offense. The Circuit Court for Marquette County, Wisconsin, agreed with the driver and refused to bind her over for trial. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State argued that while the trial court's reading of Wis. Stat. § 346.67(1) (2005-06) might have been reasonable, it was more reasonable to read the statute to require that the motor vehicle operator identify himself or herself as the operator. The driver responded that the statute plainly did not impose this requirement. The appellate court concluded that § 346.67(1) required an operator of a vehicle to identify him or herself as the operator of the vehicle. With this construction of the statute, there was no dispute that the evidence at the preliminary hearing was sufficient to support a bind over of the driver on this charge as the driver inaccurately told the officer she was the passenger and left the scene without correcting that inaccurate information. Thus, the driver did comply with the statute, and the trial court erred in refusing to bind over the driver.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the trial court with instructions to order that the driver be bound over on the charge.

Geurink v. Wegner


Appeal No. 2006AP1507


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2007 WI App 162; 303 Wis. 2d 745; 735 N.W.2d 193; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 422



May 15, 2007, Decided  
May 15, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Geurink v. Wegner, 2007 WI 120, 304 Wis. 2d 611, 741 N.W.2d 241, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 701 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Lincoln County: PATRICK M. BRADY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV173.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Lincoln County (Wisconsin), which awarded judgment to defendants in an adverse possession action. Defendants challenged an order denying their claim for expenses under Wis. Stat. § 804.12(3) (2005-06) for successfully proving issues that were the subject of denials of requests for admissions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action to obtain a declaration that a portion of defendants' property had been gained by adverse possession. Defendants asserted that they owned the entirety of the property, which was obtained from a county in 1995. The county had obtained title to the parcel by tax deed on March 20, 1986. The trial court concluded that a tax deed was not derivative, but created a new title that extinguished all former titles and liens not expressly exempted by statute from its operation. The trial court rejected plaintiffs' argument that Wis. Stat. § 75.144 was such an exemption. On appeal, the court found that the trial court correctly concluded that the language of § 75.144 did not reveal by express language or necessary implication a legislative intent that the statute apply retroactively. Title to the property was taken by the county prior to the existence of § 75.144. The trial court was correct in declaring plaintiffs' claim of adverse possession extinguished by the taking of a tax deed in 1986. However, the trial court failed to properly analyze the four enumerated exceptions to an order for sanctions in Wis. Stat. § 804.12(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court on the adverse possession claim. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court on defendants' claim for expenses and remanded the case for further proceedings.


 

765 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Anderson v. Jansen


Appeal No. 2006AP1779


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2007 WI App 162; 303 Wis. 2d 746; 735 N.W.2d 194; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 423



May 15, 2007, Decided  
May 15, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marathon County: VINCENT K. HOWARD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CV41.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin), which granted defendant company's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction an action for breach of a proprietary mutual exchange agreement, breach of an implied contract of confidentiality, violations of Wisconsin trade secret laws, and intentional misrepresentation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a Wisconsin corporation. Defendant had its principal place of business in New York. Plaintiff brought an action against defendant for breach of a proprietary mutual exchange agreement, breach of an implied contract of confidentiality, violations of Wisconsin trade secret laws, and intentional misrepresentation. Defendant moved to have the complaint dismissed due to lack of personal jurisdiction. The trial court dismissed the complaint because it concluded that exercising personal jurisdiction over defendant would violate fair play and substantial justice. On appeal, the court found that Wisconsin had a significant interest in the outcome of the litigation because it directly bore upon the future of a Wisconsin company, the Wisconsin residents it employed, and perhaps the development of Wisconsin law. Further, plaintiff had an undeniable interest in obtaining convenient and effective relief for its claims. There was no dispute that defendant had significant minimum contacts with Wisconsin. Defendant did not demonstrate a compelling case that the burden of producing witnesses from New York was so grave as to violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Kimbrough


Appeal No. 2005AP1399


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2007 WI App 162; 303 Wis. 2d 743; 735 N.W.2d 192; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 441



May 15, 2007, Decided  
May 15, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CHARLES F. KAHN, JR., Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1992CF920898.
State v. Kimbrough, 180 Wis. 2d 470, 514 N.W.2d 55, 1993 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1385 (Wis. Ct. App., 1993).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to possession of a controlled substance, cocaine base, with intent to deliver, while armed. Defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief under Wis. Stat. § 974.06, which raised a host of issues not argued in his direct appeal or previous postconviction motion. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denied the motion, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had already had an opportunity (in both his no-merit appeal and in his first Wis. Stat. § 974.06 motion) to raise the claims asserted in the motion. Defendant's suggestions that ineffectiveness of counsel, coupled with functional illiteracy and claimed incompetency, constituted sufficient reasons for failing to raise his issues previously, were conclusory allegations that had no basis in the record.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was affirmed.

State v. Sloan


2006AP1271-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 146; 303 Wis. 2d 438; 736 N.W.2d 189; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 443


February 27, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
May 15, 2007, Decided  
May 15, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DENNIS P. MORONEY, 1 Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF1154.


1 The Honorable Dennis P. Moroney presided over the majority of the proceedings in this case. However, because of court congestion, the Honorable Elsa C. Lamelas presided over the motion to suppress.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to and was sentenced for manufacture of a controlled substance, Wis. Stat. §§ 961.14(4)(t), 961.41(1)(h)(3) (2003-04). He moved to suppress evidence seized from the search of a box and from the search warrant issued for his residence. The circuit court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, denied the motion. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Suspecting that defendant was attempting to ship contraband, employees of a private shipping company opened the box, found a duct-taped canister which they thought contained marijuana, and called police. After looking in the box, an officer conducted a field test and confirmed that the substance in the canister was marijuana. He then confiscated the package as contraband. The employees had the authority to examine what they considered to be a suspicious package. They properly contacted law enforcement, and the officer was authorized to replicate the search already conducted by the employees. The officer then got a warrant to search the return address listed by defendant on the package. However, the officer's affidavit did not state that he believed defendant was, or recently had been, engaged in any criminal activity at the residence. Although the affidavit contained probable cause to believe defendant possessed marijuana at the shipping company's facility, it provided no facts to link his possession to the residence. Given the absence of factual connections between crimes by defendant or others and the residence, no probable cause existed to search the residence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision with respect to search of the box left with the shipping company, but reversed the portion of the trial court's decision upholding the search warrant for the residence.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rusk County (Wisconsin) convicting him of operating while intoxicated, second offense.


OVERVIEW: A deputy pulled over defendant's vehicle for flashing the high-beam lights at the deputy and another vehicles. The trial court also accepted the deputy's testimony that the other oncoming vehicle did not have its high-beams on.

City of Shawano v. Midwest Props. of Shawano, LLC


Appeal Nos. 2006AP2656-FT, 2006AP2657-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2007 WI App 138; 302 Wis. 2d 263; 732 N.W.2d 864; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 354



April 17, 2007, Decided  
April 17, 2007, Filed  


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Shawano County: THOMAS G. GROVER, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2006CV90, 2006CV91.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Shawano County (Wisconsin) concluding it violated a plaintiff city zoning code regulating off-street parking. The property owner argued that the zoning code section in question applied only to businesses that were required to provide off-street parking for their customers.


OVERVIEW: The court agreed with the property owner's argument that City of Shawano, Wis., Zoning Code § 10.06(5)(c) applied only to parking spaces a business was required to provide on site under City of Shawano, Wis., Zoning Code § 10.05. So, for example, a restaurant in zone HB II is required to have one parking space per 150 square feet of floor area. The only way to explain the words "required off-street parking spaces" in City of Shawano, Wis., Zoning Code § 10.06(5)(c) was as a reference to the sections requiring various amounts of off-street parking for different types of businesses found in City of Shawano, Wis., Zoning Code § 10.05. Interpreting City of Shawano, Wis., Zoning Code § 10.06(5)(c) as a stand-alone provision was not consistent with the use of the term "required" in City of Shawano, Wis., Zoning Code § 10.06(5)(c) or with City of Shawano, Wis., Zoning Code § 10.06(1).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed.

State v. Miller (In re Miller)


Appeal No. 2004AP2372


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 138; 302 Wis. 2d 260; 732 N.W.2d 863; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 346



April 12, 2007, Decided  
April 12, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: MICHAEL J. MULROY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1999CI1.
State v. Miller (In re Miller), 2002 WI App 165, 256 Wis. 2d 692, 647 N.W.2d 467, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 564 (2002).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) which denied his petition for supervised release under Wis. Stat. § 980.08(4)(b) (2003-04). Defendant also raised due process and equal protection challenges to the amendments, as well as a separate vagueness challenge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was committed as a sexually violent person. The resolution of his case turned on the appellate court's interpretation and application of the newly enacted amendments to Wis. Stat. § 980.08(4) to a particular set of facts. Defendant filed his petition seeking supervised release in March 2004, before the April 22, 2004, effective date of § 980.08(4)(b)2. His hearing, however, had not yet been held. It was plain by the unambiguous language of 2003 Wis. Sess. Laws 187, § 8, that Wis. Stat. § 980.08(4)(b)2. applied to hearings commenced on the effective date of § 980.08(4)(b)2. Because defendant's hearing on his petition had not commenced until after the effective date of the amendments, the new law was not retroactively applied to him. Because the appellate court concluded § 980.08(4)(b)2. was not retroactively applied to defendant, it rejected his substantive due process challenge on the issue. The court did not reach the merits of defendant's other constitutional challenges because the circuit court applied the first ground under § 980.08(4)(b) in denying defendant's petition and because defendant's facial constitutional challenges were moot.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's order denying defendant's petition for supervised release.

State v. Richardson


Appeal No. 2006AP1992-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 138; 302 Wis. 2d 262; 732 N.W.2d 864; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 347



April 12, 2007, Decided  
April 12, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Marquette County: RICHARD O. WRIGHT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CM53.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Marquette County (Wisconsin) where he was convicted based on no-contest pleas to misdemeanor charges of possession of tetrahydrocannabinols (THC), contrary to Wis. Stat. § 961.41(3g)(e), and possession of drug paraphernalia, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 961.573(1). He appealed the judgment of conviction and the circuit court's order denying his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: The officer stopped defendant because he believed defendant's driving privileges were cancelled. Following the stop, the officer searched defendant's vehicle and seized the THC and drug paraphernalia found in the car. The sole issue was whether the information the officer had when he stopped defendant that defendant's driver's license was cancelled was stale, such that the officer lacked reasonable suspicion to stop defendant. There was no dispute that this was the only reason the officer had to stop defendant. The court performed a Terry analysis and held that because the officer could not remember when he first learned that defendant's license was cancelled, and because, under Wis. Stat. §§ 343.25(7), 343.26, and 343.16(5)(b), defendant could have regained his license without the officer's knowledge, the officer's belief that defendant's license was still cancelled was unreasonable. In his testimony, the officer admitted that there was nothing suspicious about defendant's driving prior to the stop. The only reason he offered for stopping defendant was his "prior knowledge" that defendant's license had been suspended after an incident the previous summer.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the circuit court's order denying defendant's suppression motion and the judgment of conviction. The cause was remanded with directions.

March 27, 2007, Decided  
March 27, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Stechauner, 2007 WI 120, 304 Wis. 2d 612, 741 N.W.2d 241, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 665 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Stechauner, 2011 WI App 19, 331 Wis. 2d 487, 795 N.W.2d 62, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 981 (2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Stechauner, 2015 WI App 68, 364 Wis. 2d 758, 869 N.W.2d 170, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 531 (2015)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by Stechauner v. Smith, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 173558 (E.D. Wis., Dec. 31, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MEL FLANAGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF6461.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded no contest in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) to one count of second-degree reckless homicide and one count of armed robbery with use of force, both as party to a crime. After his motion for post conviction relief was denied, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the statements he gave at the hospital and in the squad car were unconstitutionally obtained because he had not been advised of his Miranda rights. The court of appeals disagreed. The police testified that defendant was not in custody at the hospital, that he was not handcuffed or restrained in any way, and that he was not considered a suspect at that time. Defendant contradicted that testimony, claiming he was handcuffed and believed that he was in custody. The testimony of the police supported the trial court's findings that defendant was not in custody when he spoke with police at the hospital. The trial court found that the statement that defendant made in the squad car about how to remove the casing was a voluntary statement he made after he saw the detective struggling to remove the casing. That statement was not the product of police interrogation. The detective did not ask defendant how to remove the casing; rather, defendant, on his own, shouted out the information to the officer. Therefore, the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress his statements.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Oneida County: MARK MANGERSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CI2.
State v. Roberts, 2000 WI App 116, 235 Wis. 2d 277, 616 N.W.2d 525, 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 286 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant proposed patient challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Oneida County (Wisconsin), which committed him as a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed motions in limine seeking to exclude certain evidence relating to prior conduct in Wisconsin and other states from jury consideration. Some of the evidence was admitted, and the patient was found to be a sexually violent person. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court held that the patient provided no citation of authority regarding an alleged mistake in testimony from his parole officer regarding a charge in Michigan. He was unable to object to statements in one expert's report because he did not link the statements to the jury verdict or contend that the expert should have been excluded as a witness based on these alleged falsities. The description of one offense was not more damaging than the conviction itself. Moreover, the patient waived his argument regarding certain evidence because there was no objection at trial. He also waived his claim that information was not produced during discovery. The claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was waived since it was not raised in a postconviction motion. Finally, Wis. Stat. ch. 980, as amended by 2003 Wis. Sess. Laws 187, was applicable to the patient, and it was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MARY M. KUHNMUENCH, Judge. Reversed and cause remanded.
State v. Stokes, 136 Wis. 2d 557, 402 N.W.2d 390, 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3392 (Wis. Ct. App., 1987)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a committed individual, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered a commitment order against him after he was found to have been a sexually violent person. He also appealed from the order that denied his post-commitment motion.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of a commitment order that had been entered after he was found to have been a sexually violent person. He also appealed the order denying his post-commitment motion. The appellate court reluctantly concluded that although appellant's right to a speedy trial was not violated, it was very troubled that nearly six years elapsed from the filing of the petition to the beginning of his trial. And, because appellant's right to proceed pro se was improvidently revoked in violation of the Sixth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 7, the appellate court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for a new trial. The appellate court was not convinced that appellant's behavior amounted to serious or obstructionist misconduct, and that his behavior was obstreperous and so disruptive that the trial was unable to move forward. The record did not reflect that the circuit court gave appellant very much, if any, leniency, which, as a pro se prisoner, the circuit court should have given him. Additionally, there was enough evidence to establish a substantial probability that appellant would have engaged in acts of sexual violence under Wis. Stat. § 980.02 (2001-02).


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter to the circuit court for a new trial.

State v. Feldmann (In re Feldmann)


Appeal No. 2005AP2347


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 35; 300 Wis. 2d 474; 730 N.W.2d 440; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 141


January 26, 2007, Submitted on Briefs

February 21, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Feldman, 2007 WI 114, 737 N.W.2d 432, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 488 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: ROBERT J. WIRTZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CI1.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin), which committed him as a "sexually violent person" under Wis. Stat. § 980.01(7) (2005-06) pursuant to a petition filed by petitioner, the State of Wisconsin. Respondent's post-commitment motion for relief was denied.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was convicted of two counts of second-degree sexual assault of a child. He was later released on parole. His parole agent discovered that he had violated some of his parole conditions. His parole was revoked and he was returned to prison. The State filed a petition to detain him as a "sexually violent person" within the meaning of § 980.01(7). A jury concluded that he was a sexually violent offender. They heard testimony from his parole agent about his rule violations while in the community. Two psychologists offered expert opinions that he suffered from a mental disorder that created a substantial probability that he would engage in acts of sexual violence in the future. Respondent had every opportunity to challenge the State's proof. No equal protection violation occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Tallmadge v. Boyle


Appeal No. 2006AP1075


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 47; 300 Wis. 2d 510; 730 N.W.2d 173; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 142


January 3, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
February 21, 2007, Decided  
February 21, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Tallmadge v. Boyle, 2007 WI 114, 737 N.W.2d 433, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 512 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CLARE L. FIORENZA, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CV8986.
People v. Tallmadge, 103 Cal. App. 3d 980, 163 Cal. Rptr. 372, 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1641 (Cal. App. 2d Dist., 1980)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, an attorney and his insurer (attorney), in the client's legal malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The client was a former Wisconsin resident who was presently incarcerated in the California penal system for 15 counts of sexually assaulting minor girls. A trust retained the attorney to represent the client, in part, with respect to matters related to the trust and to assist in matters related to the multimillion dollar civil judgments the two young women victims had obtained based on the criminal conviction. The attorney was to focus on securing relief via a writ of habeas corpus. The attorney was fired in July 2003 and the client, a year later, filed an action against the attorney. The circuit court granted summary judgment in favor of the attorney in the client's legal malpractice action. The appellate court affirmed, stating that there was no evidence to demonstrate that the client had any possibility of securing a new trial on all 15 convictions. Any conclusory assertions that, but for the attorney's actions, the client would have been a free man, were merely speculative. In regard to the return of attorney fees, the trustee of the trust was the proper party to hold the attorney responsible, not the beneficiary. The client was the beneficiary of the trust.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, entered orders terminating appellant father's parental rights and orders denying his postjudgment motions. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The children were taken into protective custody pursuant to CHIPS dispositional orders. The father was incarcerated when the children were removed, but he was released shortly thereafter. The father's probation was revoked. He was expected to remain in prison until October 10, 2008. The children had been out of their parental home since August 27, 2003. On appeal, the father argued that he should be granted a new trial because he was entitled to a jury instruction stating that the jury was not to find grounds to terminate his parental rights due to his failure to meet conditions of return based solely on his incarceration. Nevertheless, a social worker testified that the father failed to complete an aftercare program and he made states that he did not need to attend a substance abuse recovery program. Based on this testimony, the father failed to demonstrate the jury found grounds to terminate his parental rights solely due to conditions of return he could not meet because of his incarceration.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Rock County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Bonnie B. (In re Crystal A.L.)


Appeal Nos. 2006AP2525, 2006AP2526


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 110; 300 Wis. 2d 582; 730 N.W.2d 461; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 88



February 8, 2007, Decided  
February 8, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Rock County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Bonnie B., 2007 WI 114, 302 Wis. 2d 108, 737 N.W.2d 434, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 487 (2007)
Review denied by Rock County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Bonnie B., 2007 WI 114, 302 Wis. 2d 108, 737 N.W.2d 434, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 551 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Rock County: R.A. BATES, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2006TP16, 2006TP17.
Rock County Dept. of Human Servs. v. Bonnie L. (In re Crystal A.L.), 2006 WI App 20, 289 Wis. 2d 221, 709 N.W.2d 113, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1104 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which, pursuant to a petition filed by respondent department of human services, terminated her parental rights to her two children under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2) and (6) (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: In 1993, the mother was convicted of first-degree sexual assault of a child and two counts of incest, for sexual abuse of her minor son. She was sentenced to nine months in jail and 10 years of probation. The rules of her probation prohibited her from having any contact with children, including her own. While on probation, she gave birth to two more children. She was arrested for violating the terms of her probation and sentenced to 12 years in prison. The trial court terminated her parental rights to the two children. On appeal, the court found that the application of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2) to terminate her parental rights was sufficiently narrowly tailored to the facts presented. The mother's conditions of return were specifically tailored to her situation as a parent incarcerated for the sexual abuse of her minor son. The reason she could not meet the conditions of return imposed by the department was that she had been convicted of sexual abuse of a child and could not have contact with any children, including her own. Termination of her parental rights for failure to meet the conditions of return imposed by the department did not violate her substantive due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Wille


Appeal No. 2005AP2839-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 27; 299 Wis. 2d 531; 728 N.W.2d 343; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 63


June 14, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
January 31, 2007, Decided  
January 31, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Wille, 2007 WI 61, 732 N.W.2d 859, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 288 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court for Portage County (Wisconsin) entered a judgment convicting defendant of causing death by procuring alcohol for a minor, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 125.075(1) (2003-04). Defendant appealed, contending that the evidence at trial was insufficient to convict him of violating the cited statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that criminal liability under the statute required that a defendant have knowledge that a specific victim would consume the provided beverages. The appellate court disagreed, stating that it would be absurd or unreasonable to interpret § 125.075(1) as requiring a personal interaction between defendant and the victim, or as requiring that defendant have knowledge that a particular underage person would consume the alcohol procured by defendant. The appellate court held that a violation of § 125.075(1) was proven when a defendant was shown to have procured alcohol beverages for one or more persons who were under 18 years of age, if the defendant knew or should have known that the underage persons were under the legal drinking age and an underage person who was under eighteen when provided the beverages died as a result. In the instant case, the appellate court concluded that the evidence at trial was sufficient to establish that defendant knew or should have known that the alcohol beverages he procured for a party would be consumed by persons under the age of twenty-one.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wis. Dep't of Corr. v. Saenz (In re Saenz)


Appeal No. 2005AP2750


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 25; 299 Wis. 2d 486; 728 N.W.2d 765; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 48



January 25, 2007, Decided  
January 25, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Saenz v. Frank, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 44169 (E.D. Wis., June 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dodge County: JOHN R. STORCK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005GN63.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed an order of the circuit court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) making permanent a prior order allowing respondent Department of Corrections to forcibly medicate, feed, and hydrate the inmate and denying the inmate's request for examination by an independent physician.


OVERVIEW: After the inmate went on a hunger strike to protest the segregation conditions in the prison, the Department petitioned the trial court for permission to forcibly feed, hydrate, and medicate him. The trial court granted the Department's petition and later made its order permanent. On appeal, the court held that even though the inmate possessed a constitutionally-based liberty interest in avoiding unwanted forced nutrition and hydration under the Fourteenth Amendment, the Department could, under certain circumstances, infringe on the inmate's liberty interest by forcing him to ingest food and fluids against his will. However, the court held that the trial court erred by entering an indefinite, ostensibly permanent, ex parte order to involuntarily feed and hydrate the inmate. The trial court also erred by waiting for three weeks after entering the ex parte order to hold another court proceeding on the matter; it should have conducted an initial hearing as soon as reasonably possible. The inmate also should have been granted the right to an evidentiary hearing when he disputed the Department's allegations that he was refusing to drink fluids.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

State v. Quintana


Appeal No. 2006AP499-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 29; 299 Wis. 2d 234; 729 N.W.2d 776; 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 14


November 20, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
January 17, 2007, Decided  
January 17, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Quintana, 2007 WI 114, 302 Wis. 2d 104, 737 N.W.2d 431, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 449 (2007)
Affirmed by State v. Quintana, 2008 WI 33, 748 N.W.2d 447, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 176 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Marathon County: VINCENT K. HOWARD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF733.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Wisconsin appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Marathon County, Wisconsin, dismissing the mayhem charge under Wis. Stat. § 940.21 (2003-2004) and the school zone penalty enhancers under Wis. Stat. § 939.632 (2003-2004) attached to two charges against defendant.


OVERVIEW: In the early morning hours, defendant allegedly entered the bedroom of his ex-wife and struck her forehead with the claw end of a hammer approximately three times. The ex-wife suffered a skull fracture and a scalp laceration running from above her eyebrow to behind her ear. The amended information charged defendant with solicitation of first-degree intentional homicide, first-degree reckless injury, aggravated battery, and mayhem. The mayhem and aggravated battery charges were alleged to have been committed in a school zone. The circuit court dismissed the mayhem charge because it concluded the statute was inapplicable to forehead injuries and dismissed the school zone enhancers because it concluded the statute was unconstitutional as applied. The appellate court ruled that the mayhem statute applied and that the school zone enhancer was not unconstitutional. The mayhem statute covered cutting or mutilation to the forehead, as the forehead, but not the entire head, could be considered an "other bodily member" under the mayhem statute. Also, the State offered multiple plausible reasons supporting the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 939.632 (2003-2004).


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Beecraft


Appeal No. 2006AP982-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 19; 298 Wis. 2d 551; 727 N.W.2d 375; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1266



December 28, 2006, Decided  
December 28, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of possession of tetrahydrocannabinols (THC) as party to a crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of THC as party to a crime. The trial court imposed a six-month suspension of his driver's license, fines, and costs. The same was true of his argument that his prosecution violated his right to pursue happiness guaranteed him by the Declaration of Independence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Olson v. Town of Cottage Grove


Appeal No. 2005AP2257


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 19; 298 Wis. 2d 548; 727 N.W.2d 373; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1271



December 28, 2006, Decided  
December 28, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Olson v. Town of Cottage Grove, 2007 WI 61, 300 Wis. 2d 191, 732 N.W.2d 857, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 81 (2007)
Affirmed by, Cause remanded by Olson v. Town of Cottage Grove, 2008 WI 51, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 301 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant real estate developer, filed a declaratory judgment action challenging the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, granting the motion for summary judgment filed by respondent town, on the basis that the developer's lawsuit was not ripe and therefore not justiciable.


OVERVIEW: The developer raised multiple challenges to a town ordinance containing a provision relating to the transfer of development rights (TDR). The developer attempted to subdivide property into residential lots. The developer subsequently failed in his attempt to develop his land because he could not meet the TDR requirements of the town ordinance. The developer sought to have the town ordinance declared unconstitutional on various grounds and sought other relief, including approval of his plat and compensation for the alleged taking of his property. The appellate court ruled that the lawsuit was ripe for adjudication and therefore was justiciable. The developer had availed himself of the rezoning and plat approval process, but failed because he could not meet the TDR requirements. The developer was permitted to test the validity of the town's ordinance before incurring substantial financial liabilities. It was sufficient that the town would continue to apply the ordinance's TDR requirements to any future plat approval the developer sought, since his property was in a receiving area subject to those requirements.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Grimes


Appeal No. 2005AP3143-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2007 WI App 19; 298 Wis. 2d 549; 727 N.W.2d 374; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1248



December 27, 2006, Decided  
December 27, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CF337.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicting him of possession of cocaine and an order denying his motion to suppress evidence seized from a search of his person.


OVERVIEW: Acting on a tip from an anonymous caller, police officer went to a bar, frisked defendant, and found several rocks of cocaine. Defendant pleaded guilty to possession of cocaine after the trial court denied his motion to suppress. On appeal, the court held that the officers did not have reasonable suspicion to conduct the investigatory stop of defendant, and therefore the resulting search and seizure of the cocaine was unconstitutional, because the anonymous tip did not have the indicia of reliability required under the J.L., White, and Williams cases, and was not otherwise justified by exigent circumstances or based on suspicious conduct independently observed by the officers. When they made the investigative stop of defendant, the officers had only the following information: (1) defendant's name; (2) the fact that he was a black male; (3) he was wearing a black wool waist-length coat and a black winter hat; (4) he was at a bar at a particular location; and (5) he was in possession of drugs. The printout of the dispatch record provided no height or weight information, and the height and weight information provided by the caller was extremely inaccurate as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Nelson (In re Nelson)


Appeal No. 2005AP810


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI App 2; 298 Wis. 2d 453; 727 N.W.2d 364; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1268


February 6, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
December 21, 2006, Decided  
December 21, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DIANE M. NICKS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CI3.
State v. Nelson (In re Commitment of Nelson), 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1284 (Wis. Ct. App., Mar. 2, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, committing him as a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (2003-2004) and denying his motion for reconsideration and a new trial.


OVERVIEW: On April 19, 2004, the State petitioned to have appellant committed as a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980. Between the time the State filed the petition and the time the circuit court found appellant to be a sexually violent person, the definition of sexually violent person changed. With the passage of 2003 Wis. Act 187, the Wisconsin Legislature changed just two words in the definition of sexually violent person, substituting "likely" for "substantially probable." The circuit court found appellant to be a sexually violent person under the new "likely" standard and committed him. Appellant challenged the recently modified definition of "sexually violent person" on both substantive due process and equal protection grounds. The appellate court found that none of appellant's arguments persuaded it beyond a reasonable doubt that Wis. Stat. ch. 980, as amended by 2003 Wis. Act 187, was unconstitutional on substantive due process or equal protection grounds. The new definition lowered the level of dangerousness required for commitment from "substantially probable" to "likely" to engage in an act of sexual violence.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

Britni E. v. Wallace R. T. (In re Hailie E. T.)


Appeal No. 2006AP567


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2007 WI App 19; 298 Wis. 2d 550; 727 N.W.2d 374; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1168



December 12, 2006, Decided  
December 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: ERIC J. WAHL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005GN6.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought to terminate guardianship of respondent grandparents. The Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin) held that the appropriate standard to be applied was the best interests of the child. Applying that standard, the circuit court denied the mother's motion to terminate the guardianship. The mother appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the guardianship should have been terminated absent a finding that she was unfit or unable to care for the child or that other compelling reasons required guardianship. The appellate court agreed with the mother that a compelling reasons standard was the appropriate standard when parents challenged an existing guardianship given the parents' constitutional entitlement to the custody of their children. The appellate court rejected the grandparents' attempt to distinguish the applicable judicial precedent where they conceded that they were essentially arguing that the judicial precedent was wrongly decided. The appellate court was without power to overrule a published opinion of the court of appeals. Since that judicial precedent controlled the results in this case, the circuit court's order was reversed.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. The cause was remanded with direction to apply the compelling reasons standard to the facts of the case.

State v. Nellum


Appeal No. 2006AP787-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2007 WI App 19; 298 Wis. 2d 551; 727 N.W.2d 375; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1177



December 12, 2006, Decided  
December 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Nellum, 2007 WI 59, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 184 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an inmate, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of armed robbery with threat of force as party to a crime in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(2) and 939.05 (2003-04), sentenced him to a 10-year term, and denied his postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: The inmate contended that the trial court erroneously exercised its sentencing discretion by imposing an excessive sentence and one that was disparate to that of a co-actor. He had pled guilty to armed robbery with threat of force as party to a crime in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(2) and 939.05 (2003-04) and he had received a 10-year sentence, consisting of five years of initial confinement followed by five years of extended supervision. His postconviction motion was denied and the appellate court affirmed. In its imposition, the trial court considered the seriousness of the offense, as well as the inmate's character, past criminal record and the need to protect the public from such criminal behavior. His sentence was not excessive because he received only one-quarter of the maximum potential sentence. It was also clear that the trial court properly assessed the individual factors pertinent to the inmate and a co-actor. The factors were very different between the two and supported the trial court's sentencing discretion. In part, the inmate had a pattern of violent criminal behavior. The co-actor did not and was going to college, whereas the inmate was "drifting in life."


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McQueen v. Twp. of Wyocena


Appeal No. 2005AP2947


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2007 WI App 19; 298 Wis. 2d 549; 727 N.W.2d 374; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1150



December 7, 2006, Decided  
December 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia County: PATRICK TAGGART, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV44.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the owner's claim against defendants a town and the town board. The owner had filed an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 alleging an equal protection violation when the town decided to veto the owner's rezoning petition.


OVERVIEW: The owner alleged that the town board filed a disapproval of his rezoning petitions before the county board had acted on the owner's proposed rezoning and that the town's actions were without legitimate governmental reason or purpose and were irrational, arbitrary, and capricious, and in violation of his right to equal protection under the United States Constitution. The court held that the trial court correctly limited its decision to the final disapproval because that was the only disapproval that actually caused the harm for which plaintiff sought damages. The town's prior disapprovals had no effect at all on the final outcome of the owner's rezoning attempt, because the county board eventually approved the owner's ordinance in spite of the town's expressed disapprovals. The trial court had found that the owner had not pointed to any similar parcels that had been zoned from agricultural to residential in the area near plaintiff's property. The court concluded that the owner had not shown that it was clearly erroneous for the trial court to find that the owner did not establish that he was treated differently from similarly situated owners.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Reynosa v. Ross


Appeal No. 2005AP2693


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2007 WI App 1; 298 Wis. 2d 247; 726 N.W.2d 356; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1059



November 15, 2006, Decided  
November 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: RICHARD J. KREUL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV526.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which enjoined her under Wis. Stat. § 813.125 (2003-04) from harassing respondent, her neighbor, and from having any contact with the neighbor by telephone, mail, in person, or by third parties.


OVERVIEW: The neighbor filed a petition seeking to enjoin appellant from harassing her. At trial, the neighbor testified that appellant yelled at her and threatened her with police involvement over a noisy muffler on her car, appellant called her landlord and the police to complain about her, appellant appeared at her place of employment and yelled at her and threatened her, appellant called the police to complain about loud music at the neighbor's house, appellant made numerous telephone calls to her, and on two occasions, appellant drove quickly down the street toward the neighbor such that the neighbor, who was carrying her baby on one occasion, felt threatened and unsafe. The court noted that the evidence before the circuit court indicated that appellant's harassing contact with the neighbor took many forms. The court stated that an order enjoining all contact was not overbroad if it was based on diverse types of conduct. Constitutionally protected activity could be enjoined if such a limitation was necessary to end the harassing behavior. Because appellant's harassment of the neighbor took several forms, enjoining all contact was within the circuit court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.
