State v. Gumieny


Appeal No. 2006AP1001-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2006 WI App 244; 297 Wis. 2d 586; 724 N.W.2d 704; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 982



October 24, 2006, Decided  
October 24, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Gumieny, 2007 WI 59, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 186 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Shawano County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of operating with a prohibited alcohol concentration, sixth offense, and denied his postconviction motion. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred by permitting the State to question him concerning his failure to call his mother as a witness and his post-arrest failure to contact police with his version of events.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sister called police to report that defendant was intoxicated and causing a verbal disturbance. When police arrived, they saw defendant's van parked across a driveway and asked him questions about how he got home. Defendant told police a friend drove him home, but the friend denied it when police called to check defendant's story. Defendant was arrested and taken to a hospital for a blood test, where he told police that 2 other people had driven him home. An officer read defendant the pre-interrogation warning from the alcohol report form, and he then declined to answer questions. At trial, defendant testified that he drank shots of his mother's whiskey after he arrived home, and the State questioned him about his failure to call his mother as a witness and to tell police his version of events. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court decision, holding that although the State erred by asking defendant a question about his post-Miranda silence as to his version of the events, the impermissible question elicited the same information as a permissible question on his pre-Miranda silence about having drinks after he arrived home.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

793 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Helsper (In re Attorney Fees)


Appeal No. 2006AP835-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 243; 297 Wis. 2d 377; 724 N.W.2d 414; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1011


October 17, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
October 17, 2006, Decided  
October 17, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: ERIC J. WAHL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CF83.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to vacate an order committing him to a county jail for the failure to pay attorney fees due under his judgment of conviction.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested, he petitioned for an appointed attorney, alleging that he had been rejected by the public defender but could not afford to retain an attorney. An attorney was appointed to represent him. The attorney was to be paid by the county, and defendant would be liable to the county for amounts expended on his behalf. Defendant pled guilty to two counts. After his attorney submitted his bill, one of the judgments of conviction was amended to require the payment of $ 919 in attorney fees. No hearing was ever held to determine whether defendant was able to pay the attorney fees. When defendant still owed $ 465 on his attorney fee obligation, the trial court issued an order authorizing his commitment to the county jail for 33 days. On appeal, the court concluded that the United States Constitution required the trial court to determine ability to pay at some point prior to commitment for failure to pay attorney fees. Wisconsin's recoupment statute, Wis. Stat. § 973.07 (2003-04), required a hearing to make that determination. No such finding was made at sentencing, at the time defendant's fees were set, or at the time the commitment order was issued.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the case with directions to vacate the commitment order.

 

794 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Keith v. Sand Ridge Secure Treatment Ctr.


Appeal No. 2005AP3185


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 244; 297 Wis. 2d 584; 724 N.W.2d 703; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 942



October 12, 2006, Decided  
October 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State ex rel. Keith v. Sand Ridge Secure Treatment Ctr., 2007 WI 59, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 160 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate's complaint sought declarative and injunctive relief against respondent secure treatment center, where he had been committed under Wis. Stat. ch. 980, regarding sexually violent offenders. The inmate ordered a book of photographs of families, and the center denied him possession of that book. The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) granted summary judgment in favor of the center. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The center provided the court with a copy of the policy that the inmate was questioning in an affidavit in support of their summary judgment motion. The policy, broadly described, set forth a process for reviewing reading materials and pictures that were sent to or in possession of residents of the center, and prohibited possession of "contraband" or "counter-therapeutic material." The center asserted they were following and applying that policy in denying the inmate possession of the book he ordered. Affidavits by center staff explained that the inmate was not permitted to receive the book because it was regarded as counter-therapeutic. According to the affidavits, the photographs of children in it could be perceived as erotic by those residents of the center who were sexually attracted to children. The inmate argued that the policy, or its application was an improper attempt at "mind control" by the center. He assembled that argument from passages in various cases concerning potentially obscene materials. But, none of the cases he cited came even close to holding that a committed person such as the inmate had a constitutional right to possess material deemed counter-therapeutic.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

795 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Hegarty v. Beauchaine


Appeal No. 2004AP3252


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 248; 297 Wis. 2d 70; 727 N.W.2d 857; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 933


June 6, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
October 10, 2006, Decided  
October 10, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Estate of Hegarty v. Beauchaine, 2007 WI 61, 300 Wis. 2d 192, 732 N.W.2d 857, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 240 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL D. GUOLEE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1998CV9906.
Estate of Hegarty v. Beauchaine, 2001 WI App 300, 249 Wis. 2d 142, 638 N.W.2d 355, 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1119 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a doctor and his insurance company, challenged decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin awarding respondents, the deceased's estate and the deceased's parents, damages in their survival and wrongful death action under Wis. Stat. §§ 895.01, 894.04 respectively. Respondents cross-appealed the trial court's reduction in the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted declaratory judgment that the Wisconsin Patients Compensation Fund's liability was not triggered. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 893.55(4) did not apply to the doctor because she was a first-year medical resident and, thus, not a health care provider under Wis. Stat. ch. 655. It followed that, pursuant to the primary policy, the doctor was independently insured under the umbrella policy, and she was not insured under it only subject to vicarious liability by the hospital. Therefore, the fund's liability was not triggered. The court also held that here was no evidence supporting the contention that the doctor was a borrowed employee. Although the trial court properly refused to order the production of the settlement agreement, it should have conducted an in camera review of the actual document prior to ruling on the motion because it was unclear whether the agreement was a Pierringer release; thus remand on that issue was ordered. Appellants' accusation that the parents' loss of society and companionship was an impermissible award for emotional distress in disguise was nothing more than an unsupported speculation.


OUTCOME: The court remanded and ordered that a settlement agreement be produced by respondents to the insurer. The court otherwise affirmed as to the appeal and cross-appeal.

 

796 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lynch


Appeal No. 2005AP2128-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 231; 297 Wis. 2d 51; 724 N.W.2d 656; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 920


May 12, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
October 5, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Lynch, 2007 WI 59, 299 Wis. 2d 326, 731 N.W.2d 636, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 127 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Lynch, 2008 WI App 172, 314 Wis. 2d 746, 760 N.W.2d 184, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 797 (2008)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, Claim dismissed by, Motion denied by Lynch v. Jenkins, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 53280 (E.D. Wis., Apr. 30, 2010)
Related proceeding at, Dismissed by, Request denied by, As moot, Motion denied by, As moot Lynch v. Dane Cnty., 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 112907 (W.D. Wis., Aug. 26, 2015)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Lynch v. Westfield, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 56487 (W.D. Wis., Apr. 28, 2016)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which sentenced him following his conviction for homicide by intoxicated use of a vehicle and two counts of fleeing from an officer resulting in bodily harm. He also appealed the circuit court's order denying his postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: The charges in this case arose out of an incident in which defendant, under the influence of alcohol, led police officers on a high-speed chase, which ended when defendant's vehicle collided with another. One person was killed and two people were injured in the collision. On appeal, the court first rejected defendant's argument that the statutes that made him ineligible for the earned release program, Wis. Stat. §§ 302.05(3)(a)1 and 973.01(3g) (2003-04), violated his rights to equal protection and substantive due process under the federal and state constitutions. The court concluded that there was a rational basis for not allowing persons convicted of crimes under Wis. Stat. ch. 940 to participate in the earned release program. Excluding persons whose conduct caused death or great bodily harm from the opportunity to reduce their period of confinement by participation in the earned release program was rationally related to the legitimate government purpose of punishing more serious crimes more severely. The court also determined that the circuit court did not erroneously rely on defendant's statements given in a television interview with defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Bender


Appeal No. 2006AP411-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2006 WI App 244; 297 Wis. 2d 585; 724 N.W.2d 704; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 910



October 3, 2006, Decided  
October 3, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 2005CM159. APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Douglas County: GEORGE L. GLONEK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Douglas County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to suppress evidence and convicted him of misdemeanor possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Police officers walked through an apartment building and located a very strong odor of marijuana coming from an apartment. The officers informed defendant that the police were at his door. An officer heard noises that sounded like things being moved in the apartment and believed the noises were defendant's attempts to hide or destroy evidence inside the room. The officer kicked at the door, ordering defendant to open the door. When defendant opened the door, the officer could see controlled substances in plain view. Defendant was convicted of misdemeanor possession of marijuana. On appeal, the court found that while a misdemeanor offense could justify a warrantless entry due to exigent circumstances, the exigent circumstances in defendant's case were impermissibly created by the police. The police gave no reason why they could not secure a warrant before entering the apartment. Before the police knocked on the door, there was no threat of destruction of the evidence. The police impermissibly created an exigency and then used that exigency to justify their warrantless entry. Such action ran contrary to the intent of the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and the order denying his motion to suppress. The court remanded the case with directions that all evidence obtained in, and derived from, the unlawful search of defendant's home be ordered suppressed, and that defendant's guilty plea be withdrawn.

Helgeland v. Wis. Municipalities


Appeal No.: 2005AP2540


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 216; 296 Wis. 2d 880; 724 N.W.2d 208; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 912


March 3, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
September 28, 2006, Decided  
September 28, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
Review granted by Helgeland v. Wis. Municipalities, 2007 WI 59, 299 Wis. 2d 324, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 61 (2007)
Review denied by Helgeland v. Wis. Municipalities, 2007 WI 59, 299 Wis. 2d 327, 731 N.W.2d 637, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 139 (2007)
Affirmed by Helgeland v. Wis. Municipalities, 2008 WI 9, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 6 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Wisconsin Legislature and municipalities, challenged a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that denied their motions to intervene as a matter of right under Wis. Stat. § 803.09(1), or for permissive intervention under § 803.09(2), in respondent employees' action that alleged Wis. Stat. §§ 40.02(20) and 103.10 unconstitutionally denied state employee health insurance benefits and family leave to same-sex partners.


OVERVIEW: The Legislature claimed it was entitled to intervene because it had a significant interest in establishing and defending its public policy decision not to provide domestic partner benefits and to balance the budget. The municipalities also argued that they should have been joined sua sponte as necessary and indispensable parties. The court held that appellants failed to meet the statutory requirements for intervention as of right. The court found that the Legislature failed to show it had an interest sufficiently related to the employees' action or that such an interest would have been impaired by a ruling in the action; and that the municipalities' interests were adequately represented by the existing parties in the case. Also appellants were not entitled to permissive intervention because the Legislature did not have a "defense" within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 803.09(2); and allowing the municipalities to intervene would result in undue delay from the proposed certification of a class action. The court concluded that the municipalities were not necessary parties under Wis. Stat. § 803.03(1)(b) and failed to develop their argument for joinder under Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

799 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Lindell v. Frank


Appeal No. 2005AP3070


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 223; 296 Wis. 2d 935; 724 N.W.2d 274; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 849



September 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN III and RICHARD G. NIESS, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV3076.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed an order by the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, dismissing his petition for certiorari review of a prison disciplinary decision, and an order denying reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: While incarcerated the inmate received a conduct report charging him with possessing contraband and with engaging in gang related activities. Specifically, the report alleged that the inmate possessed a letter mailed to him referring to activities of a known gang and a notebook recording the inmate's correspondence with gang members. A disciplinary committee found the inmate guilty of violating Wis. Admin. Code §§ DOC 303.20(3) and 303.47(2)(a). The committee found that his notebook and the letter contained references to gang activity and allowed an inference that inmate participated in gang related activity. The inmate's writ of certiorari alleged, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to find he participated in gang activity, the decision was arbitrary and capricious, and the proceeding violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. V. The appellate court affirmed the dismissal of the inmate's petition under Wis. Stat. § 802.05(3)(b)4 (2003-04) as the court relied on the documents and testimony to find that the evidence supported the committee's findings and that the any limitations on the inmate's First Amendment rights were reasonably related to limiting gang activity.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

800 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Bettendorf v. St. Croix County


Appeal No. 2005AP1286


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2006 WI App 194; 296 Wis. 2d 418; 722 N.W.2d 399; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 788



August 24, 2006, Decided  
August 24, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 2004CV279. APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for St. Croix County: SCOTT R. NEEDHAM, Judge.
Bettendorf v. St. Croix County Bd. of Adjustment, 224 Wis. 2d 735, 591 N.W.2d 916, 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 165 (Wis. Ct. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff land owner initiated a claim against defendant county to obtain a declaratory judgment that his special exception use permit was valid and transferable. He also sought judgment that the ownership clause of an ordinance was invalid and severable. The county counterclaimed. The Circuit Court for St. Croix County, Wisconsin, entered a summary judgment order and declaratory judgment enforcing the commercial zoning of the property.


OVERVIEW: The land owner owned a parcel of land in a town that was located in the county. The land owner used his land for commercial purposes since 1971, although the land was not then zoned for commercial use. On appeal, the appellate court agreed with the county's argument that St. Croix County, Wisconsin, Ordinance 108(85) was not severable because without the ownership clause, the ordinance did not present a complete law intended by the county board. Thus, the entire ordinance failed. The land owner, on the other hand, argued that the clause had to be severed pursuant to the local zoning code. Nevertheless, if the ownership clause were excised, the ordinance would be given an effect clearly not intended. A special exception use permit could not allow a use of property that contravenes its zoning, and thus the permit was invalid. Because the Ordinance 108(85) was invalid, the lot was correctly zoned agricultural residential. Thus, because a special exception use permit could not allow a use incompatible with or adverse to the underlying zoning ordinance, the land owner's permit for a truck repair shop and transfer point in an area zoned agricultural residential was necessarily invalid.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order and the judgment.
